Accidental Add

by Agatharioxoxo

Summary

Another Celebrity AU!

Rio had never been lucky. If she ordered food, they’d forget the sauce. She always picked the slowest checkout line, and if there was one chair with gum on it, her butt would find it.

If a celebrity was going to accidentally add the wrong person on Snapchat, it should have been someone cooler, someone who didn’t still trip over their own shoelaces. But one fateful Tuesday evening, luck finally threw her a bone in the form of an accidental Snapchat add.

Here she was, staring at her phone screen in absolute disbelief.

Agatha Harkness has added you as a friend.

Notes

See the end of the work for notes

Chapter 1

Rio had never been lucky. If she bought a lottery ticket, the universe would hand-deliver the winning numbers to someone else. If she ordered food, they’d forget the sauce. She always picked the slowest checkout line, and if there was one chair with gum on it, her butt would find it.

If a celebrity was going to accidentally add the wrong person on Snapchat, it should have been someone cooler, someone who didn’t still trip over their own shoelaces. But one fateful Tuesday evening, luck finally threw her a bone in the form of an accidental Snapchat add.

Here she was, staring at her phone screen in absolute disbelief.

Agatha Harkness has added you as a friend.

Agatha. Harkness.

Oscar-winner. Red carpet queen. The internet’s favorite “MOTHER” ever since she’d played that now-iconic villain role in Coven of Chaos. The woman who had millions of fans dissecting every smirk, every arched brow, every moment of effortless, knee-weakening charisma.

And she had accidentally added Rio on Snapchat.

"Yeah, right," Rio snorted. Probably a fan account. Or worse, a scam trying to trick her and steal her personal data. Still, curiosity got the best of her, and she clicked accept, looking at the stories of the account,

A mirror selfie of Agatha, but—wait. She was wearing glasses? Thick-rimmed, librarian-chic glasses.

Rio nearly dropped her phone. Agatha Harkness, the all-powerful, all-mysterious, perfectly put-together actress, wore glasses? This was not a publicly available photo. In public, she was all smoky eyes and confident smirks, but here she was, dressed in an oversized sweater, looking like she was about to grade papers.

It had to be a mistake. A glitch in the celebrity social media matrix.Agatha had obviously meant to add someone else—her friends or a family member? A fellow A-lister who also had cheekbones so sharp they could cut glass?

But before Rio could even process what was happening, a new Snap notification popped up to say she’d added to her story.

The first image was... onions.

A cutting board covered in onions, to be exact, with a caption that read: Crying over these like they’re a failed audition.

Rio frowned. This was not the type of content she expected from Hollywood’s reigning queen of elegance and mystery.

Then another post.

It was Agatha. Wearing glasses again.

Slightly askew, adorably dorky glasses. Not the kind Rio would expect to see on a woman whose mere existence had set the internet ablaze more than once. Her usually perfect hair was pulled into a haphazard bun, and she wore an oversized sweatshirt with just noticeable coffee stains on the collar.

Rio nearly choked on her own spit.

This wasn’t the Agatha Harkness who made dramatic entrances at film premieres, draped in couture and bathed in golden light. This was Agatha Harkness: Relatable Mess.

Another post. This time, a video.

Agatha leaned against a kitchen counter, lazily twirling a wooden spoon between her fingers. “Alright, idiots,” she said, in a voice that was somehow both exhausted and charming, “tonight’s culinary disaster is lasagna. Which I just realized I forgot to preheat the oven for. So this is going great.”

The camera tilted downward, revealing a baking dish that had been carefully prepped… and was now sitting, very uselessly, on the countertop.

Agatha sighed dramatically, adjusting her glasses with the back of her wrist. “Why am I like this?”

Rio clapped a hand over her mouth to muffle the very undignified noise that almost escaped. Removed it and then clapped a hand over her mouth again to stop herself from squealing. This was not the Agatha Harkness the world knew and loved. And it was, hands down, the best thing Rio had ever witnessed.

She knew she should remove herself from this account. She knew Agatha probably meant to add someone else.

But then—one more post appeared.

A mirror selfie. Agatha, still in her glasses, balancing a glass of wine in one hand and flashing a tired but triumphant grin. ‘Forgot to preheat the oven. But found a frozen backup lasagna in the freezer. Manifesting works’.

Rio exhaled, pressing her phone to her chest.

She was never removing herself from this account.

Rio set her phone down. Then immediately picked it back up.

Then set it down again, like that would somehow stop her from being a creep.

Her brain was screaming at her: This was an accident. Agatha Harkness did not mean to add you. You are not supposed to be here.

And yet.

And yet.

She opened Snapchat again. The account had no fancy verification badge, no obvious connection to Agatha’s official socials. Just the username ‘itsactuallyagatha’, which felt suspiciously casual for a woman who had walked the Met Gala carpet in a sculpted couture gown that made her look like a living Renaissance painting.

Rio chewed her lip.

She switched apps and searched Agatha Harkness Instagram.

The first result? Her verified public account, boasting an obscene number of followers. 180 million followers.

Every post was a work of art. Professionally lit photoshoots. Elegant behind-the-scenes shots. Red carpet close-ups where she looked like she’d been carved from the dreams of mortals. Even the candid pictures had an effortless aesthetic, like she had simply woken up bathed in golden sunlight and draped in a silk robe.

And yet, nowhere on this perfectly curated Instagram was there a single mention of glasses, messy buns, or lasagna-based existential crises.

Rio scrolled through the comments on Agatha’s latest post, a picture from some Vogue spread where she was wearing a suit that should be illegal.

- Mother
- Step on me
- She literally invented cheekbones
- I bet she smells like expensive wine and ambition

Okay, none of these people would believe that just five minutes ago, Agatha Harkness had been filming herself in a kitchen, dramatically lamenting the lack of oven preheating.

Rio switched back to Snapchat, her heart thumping. This wasn’t just an alternate account. This was a secret account. A close friends account.

Agatha Harkness—the Agatha Harkness—had accidentally let Rio into a digital inner circle that the rest of the world would kill to see.

She swallowed hard.

She should do the right thing. She really really should remove herself before Agatha realized her mistake.

But then, another snap appeared.

A blurry, close-up shot of Agatha’s own face, taken at an aggressively unflattering angle, captioned: This is what failure looks like.

Rio lost the battle. She had to stay.

Chapter 2

The following few days were silent with no new snap updates from Agatha.

Rio told herself this was for the best. Agatha had probably realised her mistake and blocked her, or more likely, she’d simply gotten busy with something far more glamorous than Snapchat. Maybe she was filming a movie, attending an exclusive party, or, Rio swallowed, quietly removing Rio from the account.

That would be fair. That would be expected. That would also be devastating. By day three, Rio had almost convinced herself to let it go. Almost.

Then, late in the afternoon, her phone exploded with notifications.

Snap chat notification. Snapchat notification. Snapchat notification.

She grabbed her phone and nearly dropped it in her hurry to open the app. The first image was pure chaos.

Agatha, mid-sprint, her usually sleek, untouchable composure utterly destroyed by the fact that she was currently covered in mud. Her face was streaked with it. Her expensive-looking hoodie, once white, now a tragic brown, looked like she’d lost a fight with nature itself.

The caption? I’m living in HELL

Rio, already choking on laughter, tapped to the next post.

A video. Agatha, panting, breathless, holding up her phone with one hand while the other pointed wildly toward a distant, blurry shape in the background.

“Do you see that?” she gasped. “That little blurry menace? That’s MY dog. That’s MY DOG who has been ignoring me for the last fifteen minutes.”

Rio squinted. In the distance, a large breed dog, a greyhound, maybe?—was joyfully prancing across a massive field, completely unbothered by Agatha’s suffering.

“Look at her,” Agatha wheezed, flipping the camera back to her own mud-streaked face. “She’s ruined me. My dignity is GONE.”

Another Snap.

A blurry picture of the dog mid-leap, paws coated in mud, soaring toward Agatha.

Caption: I’m under ATTACK

Another Snap.

Agatha, now on the ground, face-down in the mud, one hand stretched toward her phone like a fallen soldier.

Caption: Tell my story and my family I love them

Rio was shaking with laughter. She had tears in her eyes.

This was not the Agatha Harkness the world knew. This was not the confident, dangerously cool Hollywood goddess who had the world wrapped around her finger. This was a human disaster getting tackled by a seventy five-pound dog.

And Rio never wanted to leave this secret world.

Over the next few hours, Agatha continued to document her downfall in real time.

The snaps came in a relentless, hilarious flurry.

A video: Agatha, now sitting in the mud, legs stretched out in the puddles, completely resigned to her fate. Her dog, whose name Rio learned, was Remi, sat proudly beside her, tongue hanging out, completely unbothered by the destruction she’d caused.

“She has no remorse," Agatha announced, staring into the camera like she was filming a war documentary. “None. I could perish in this field, and she’d just roll on my remains."

Remi immediately flopped onto her back, wiggling around in the mud like she was making a snow angel, wagging tail sending flurries of mud into the air.

Another Snap.

A zoomed-in photo of Remi, looking almost clean, somehow having shaken off all the mud in a feat of physics-defying trickery except for her feet and the bottom of her legs.

Caption: HOW

Another Snap.

A selfie of Agatha back in her car, still filthy, her hair a birds nest of a crime scene, looking personally victimised by existence itself.

Caption: Guess who just tracked mud into a luxury vehicle? That’s right. It’s me

Another Snap.

The aftermath. Agatha’s pristine, high-end G Class SUV, absolutely wrecked. Mud splatters everywhere. Paw prints on the dashboard and all of the seating. Remi sitting smugly in the passenger seat on top of a designer cashmere scarf that Agatha had clearly sacrificed in a moment of desperation if containing the mud.

Caption: This was a $500 scarf. I’ve accepted my fate

Rio was howling.

The fact that the internet had no idea this was happening made it infinitely funnier. If people saw Agatha at an awards show tonight, looking immaculate in a custom gown, they would never know that just hours before, she had been defeated by her own dog and some wet dirt.

Hours later, unexpectedly, the Snaps shifted.

It started with a blurry photo of Agatha’s bare feet kicked up on what looked like a couch, a half-eaten takeout container of pasta in the foreground.

No caption. Just casual. Unpolished. Unbelievably normal.

Another Snap.

A dimly lit kitchen counter. An open bottle of wine, a glass half-full. A script, pages slightly crumpled, a highlighter and pen resting on top.

Caption: Learning lines. Send thoughts and prayers

Rio blinked. She had never, in all her time lurking on Agatha’s public socials, seen any behind-the-scenes glimpses like this. Every post on her Instagram was calculated, photoshoots, promotions, carefully worded captions. But this? This was real.

Another Snap.

A cozy, messy room. Blankets thrown over the couch. Books everywhere, on the coffee table, stacked on the floor, one half-open like she’d been reading and forgotten about it. A fluffy rabbit curled up against the armrest, staring at the camera like it had just been woken up. Rio’s brain short-circuited.

Agatha Harkness had a rabbit? No one knew Agatha Harkness had a rabbit.

Caption: Before you say it—yes, I’m have both a greyhound dog and a rabbit. I contain multitudes. And no, Remi doesn’t want to kill him

Another Snap.

A close-up of a handwritten letter, elegant cursive filling the page. The signature at the bottom? Agatha’s.

Caption: Writing thank-you notes like it’s 1823. My mama raised me right.

Rio exhaled. It wasn’t just funny anymore. It wasn’t just entertaining. She was seeing parts of Agatha’s life that no one else in the general public did.

Not the actress. Not the persona. Just…Agatha. And that? That was dangerously fascinating.

Chapter 3

Rio had never been the type to obsess over celebrities. Sure, she had favorite actors and actresses, and yes, she had definitely rewatched multiple scenes from Coven of Chaos more times than she’d admit, but she’d never been the kind of person to actively check a famous person’s social media every day.

Until now.

It had been a few days since Agatha’s last post, and Rio was embarrassingly aware of how often she was checking Snapchat for an update. She wasn’t proud of it, but she’d developed a routine, open the app first thing in the morning, casually scroll through, pretend she wasn’t looking for anything specific, then close it, rinse and repeat in the evening, and tell herself she was being normal. She was failing miserably at being normal.

Then, that Sunday evening, her phone exploded with notifications.

Snapchat notifications. Agatha Harkness has posted a story.

Rio clicked faster than she’d like to admit.

The first Snap was simple: a black-and-white photo of a woman, clearly taken years ago. She had an oval face, kind, gentle eyes, and a soft smile.

Caption: Happy Mother’s Day, Mama!

Rio frowned. She had never heard Agatha’s mother mentioned before. No interviews, no red carpet questions, nothing.

The next Snap was a grainy, candid photo—Agatha, much younger, maybe in her late teens, sitting on a kitchen counter while the same woman stirred something on the stove.

Caption: She let me sit on the counter until I was like, 22. Then she told me to act my age

Rio smiled, but there was a tug of something deeper in her chest.

Another Snap.

A video. Agatha, lying on a couch, hair a mess, no makeup, wrapped in a hoodie that looked too big. Her voice was softer than usual when she spoke.

“I don’t talk about my mom in public. Not because I don’t want to, but because—" She paused, rubbing a hand over her face as she yawned wide. "I don’t want her to have to deal with all the attention.”

The camera tilted toward the ceiling.

"Lilia is… a force of nature. The kind of person who refuses to give you a clear explanation to anything. I asked so many questions as a kid, and she’d just laugh and say, ‘Figure it out, Agatha.’"

Another pause.

“My mom adopting me was probably the best thing that ever happened to me.”

Rio froze.

Another Snap.

A blurry childhood photo, Agatha, maybe eight, sitting on a porch step, grinning wide, missing a front tooth. Her mom, Lilia, sat beside her, arm slung around her casually, like they had always been mother and daughter.

Caption:She has never treated me like I was anything but hers.

Another Snap.

A new photo. Lilia, now, standing in a sunlit kitchen, stirring something on the stove. She was mid-laugh, eyes crinkled, curly grey brown hair in a bun on top of her head, the same warmth from the old pictures still there.

Caption: Still won’t tell me her sauce recipe

Another Snap.

An old note, yellowed with age, Lilia’s handwriting scrawled across the paper.
‘You don’t have to look like me to be mine. You always were and are.’

Another Snap.

A final photo. Agatha and Lilia together, taken that day, sitting on a porch, coffee mugs in hand. Agatha was leaning against her, eyes half-closed, comfortable. Lilia’s arm was around her, like it had always been.

Caption: Happy Mother’s Day to the best

Rio swallowed again, this was too personal, it wasn’t in the public domain that Agatha was adopted.

Another Snap.

A glass of wine. A large TV screen in the background.

Caption: Anyway, that’s enough feelings for today. Time to drink and rewatch trash TV

The next Snap was a screenshot of a truly awful reality dating show, with Agatha’s caption screaming: WHY WOULD YOU PROPOSE AFTER THREE WEEKS??

Rio huffed out a laugh, even as her chest felt unreasonably tight. Because damn. She hadn’t expected to learn such personal things about Agatha today. And somehow, she felt like she knew her better than ever.

The next morning, Rio woke up to a further notifications.

Agatha Harkness has posted a story - the alert she’d set up for Agathas posts doing its job.

Her heart did that stupid little jolt of excitement before she could stop it. She swiped open Snapchat, fully expecting a hungover rant about the reality show from last night.

Instead she’d posted a video. But this time, it wasn’t filmed by Agatha. It was shaky, blurry and accompanied by the very familiar, very grumpy voice of none other than Bucky Barnes.

Rio almost dropped her phone. Bucky. Barnes. As in Hollywood’s golden boy. The critically acclaimed, painfully good looking, painfully talented leading man who had been in at least three Oscar-winning films.

And apparently, Agatha had dragged him on a hike before sunrise.

"It is half past four. IN THE MORNING." Buckys voice was thick with exhaustion and betrayal as the camera shook violently, trying to focus on Agatha ahead of him on the trail. “I want it on record that I did NOT agree to this."

Another Snap.

Agatha, far too awake, standing at the edge of a trail with a thermos of coffee in one hand and a deeply smug expression on her face.

Caption (clearly written by Bucky): This woman is a MONSTER (and yes shes distracting me with her phone like I’m her toddler)

Another Snap.

A selfie, Bucky in the foreground, wrapped in a hoodie, looking like he wanted to die, while Agatha stood behind him, grinning like an absolute menace, holding up a granola bar like it was a trophy.

Caption: It’ll be fun, Bucky! The sunrise will be worth it, Bucky! I am LITERALLY suffering

Another Snap.

A video, Bucky flipping the camera to show the sunrise, which, okay, was actually gorgeous, the sky painted in shades of pink and gold over the hills.

Then the camera swung back around to Agatha, who was sipping her coffee like she had just conquered the world.

“I told you it’d be worth it," she said, obnoxiously pleased with herself.

“I hope a bear eats you," Bucky muttered.

Another Snap.

An aggressively zoomed-in shot of Buckys absolutely dead inside expression.

Caption (Which Rio thought was Agatha writing it this time): Nature is healing

Another post. Another video, Bucky panting, practically keeled over, hands on his knees.

“We are” he wheezed, “two miles from the car. Two miles. And I have no energy left to live."

From behind the camera, Agatha could be heard cackling. “You’re a literal action star. You do fight scenes and chase sequences for a living."

“WITH STUNT DOUBLES, YOU MENACE."

Another Snap.

A final photo, Agatha and Bucky, both sitting on a rock, looking exhausted but weirdly peaceful, sipping coffee and staring at the sky.

Caption: He’ll never admit it, but he liked it

Buckys comment, added in tiny text at the bottom where he’d taken her phone back before posting: LIES AND SLANDER

Rio grinned so hard her face hurt. So.

Agatha Harkness and Bucky weren’t just co-stars in multiple movies, they were actual friends. Possibly best friends. Or a couple as a lot of people wished them to be? And the internet had no idea.

Chapter 4

Another few days passed with no further stories posted by Agatha.

Rio told herself she wasn’t waiting for anything. She had a life. She had responsibilities. She was a normal person who did normal things, not someone who was unreasonably invested in the secret Snapchat life of an A-list actress. And then the notifications hit. She was totally invested.

Agatha Harkness has posted a story.

Her heart leapt as she tapped into Agatha’s snap story.

A dimly lit bar. Half-empty glasses of whiskey scattered across the table. A terrible cocktail napkin doodle of what looked like Agatha and Bucky, except stick figures with aggressively dramatic cheekbones.

Caption: Welcome to chaotic gay drinks night

Another Snap

A video. Agatha and Bucky sitting in a booth, laugh-crying, both clearly tipsy.

*"I’m just saying—" Agatha wheezed, wiping a tear from her eye, “we could have solved so many problems years ago if people had just realised we were both gay."

“RIGHT?!" Bucky shouted, dramatically throwing his hands in the air. “Do you understand how many tabloids tried to make us a thing?"

“That one article, what was it called?”Agatha snapped her fingers, thinking.

“Are They or Aren’t They: Hollywood’s Most Will-They-Won’t-They?’" Bucky said dramatically, flipping an invisible scarf over his shoulder.

Another Snap.

A screenshot of an old tabloid article featuring a staged red carpet photo of Agatha and Bucky, standing way too close, both smirking like they had a secret.

Caption: Cutest couple lol

Another Snap.

A video, Agatha dramatically reading from her phone.

“Sources say Bucky Barnes and Agatha Harkness have undeniable chemistry”

“I mean, yeah," Bucky interrupted, shrugging. “Gay people have chemistry."

Another Snap.

A selfie, Agatha and Bucky, leaning against each other, looking smug as hell.

Caption: Plot twist: we’re in love with each other

Rio put her phone down. Then picked it back up immediately because what the hell.

Agatha Harkness and Bucky Barnes, two of the most relentlessly shipped people in Hollywood, two people the internet had spent YEARS analysing, making fan edits of, writing articles about— Were both gay.

And no one knew. Except, apparently, her. Rio was reeling. She sat there, staring at her phone, processing.

Because listen, she had always found Agatha attractive. It wasn’t exactly a secret, not even to herself. You didn’t have to be in love with someone to recognize that they were alarmingly gorgeous. But this? This changed everything.

Because before, Agatha Harkness had been unattainable. A distant, untouchable Hollywood goddess. Beautiful, yes. Charming, obviously. But straight, or at the very least, unavailable in a way that made Rio’s occasional daydreams about her purely theoretical.

But now?

Now she had confirmed, on Snapchat, with her own mouth, that she was into women.

And Rio? Rio was a woman. Oh no. She flopped back onto her bed, groaning into a pillow.

Her phone buzzed with another notification. Agatha had posted again.

Rio scrambled to open it. It was a video, still filmed at the bar. This time, Agatha and Bucky were half-drunk, aggressively debating something.

“Okay, but hear me out,” Bucky was saying, swirling his whiskey, “you could totally pull off dating a woman publicly. People would lose their minds."

“Oh, please," Agatha scoffed, taking a sip of her drink. “Like that wouldn’t be an absolute disaster."

“How would it be a disaster?"

“Because, dear Bucky," Agatha said, leaning in dramatically, "the second I go public with a woman, suddenly I’m the Internet’s 'Lesbian Mommy' and people start writing think pieces about how I personally invented being gay."

“Agatha," Bucky said solemnly, “I have bad news for you."

Another Snap.

A screenshot of a tweet from some random user: Agatha Harkness could breathe near a woman, and I’d thank her for her service. Step on me, Mother

Caption: SEE? PROOF

Rio wheezed. Because okay, yes, she had seen the Internet lose its collective mind over Agatha before. And maybe she had even contributed to the chaos once or twice (or a hundred times).

But now? Now she was here. In the secret inner circle. Watching Agatha talk about dating like it was a real possibility. Which meant Rio was going to die. Because she had gone from casually thinking Agatha Harkness was hot to knowing too much.

And worse? Now she fancied her even more.

The days that followed were hell for Rio’s sanity.

Because now, every time Agatha posted, Rio wasn’t just casually entertained, she was actively suffering. It was one thing to find a celebrity attractive when they were a distant, untouchable concept, but now?

Now, she was getting regular, unfiltered access to Agatha Harkness in her natural habitat. And it was ruining her life.

Another Snap. A video, Agatha sitting on the floor of her closet, dramatically sighing, surrounded by piles of clothes.

“I don’t want to get dressed. I want to wear pajamas to this meeting."

Another Snap.

A mirror selfie, Agatha in an oversized hoodie and leggings, hair in a messy bun, no makeup, looking unfairly gorgeous for someone who had just been whining about fashion emergencies.

Caption: I am a fraud. This is literally just expensive loungewear.

Another Snap.

A photo of her fridge, completely barren except for a bottle of champagne, some oat milk, and several different types of fancy cheese.

Caption: This is why I keep eating dinner at Buckys

Another Snap.

A video, Agatha sitting at her kitchen counter, eating takeout straight from the container, glasses perched on the end of her nose as she scrolled through her phone.

“Someone just called me 'mysterious' in an article," she mumbled, mouth full of noodles. “Honey, I just spent twenty minutes Googling 'why does my dog eat grass' like a confused suburban mom."

Rio was obsessed with this woman.

Another Snap. A bath snap.

Rio wasn’t ready.

It wasn’t explicit, but it was dangerous in a way that felt personal.

A steamy, dimly lit bathroom. A full wine glass balanced on the edge of a massive clawfoot tub. Agatha’s bare knee, just barely visible through the water.

Caption: This is what I deserve after today

Rio blacked out for a second.

Another Snap.

A follow-up video, Agatha, reclining in the tub, glasses on, wine in hand, looking like a literal goddess. Her voice was lazily amused as she spoke.

“Listen, if men get to post thirst traps by just sitting in cars and looking vaguely serious, I get to post this when it’s just you guys who see it.”

Another Snap.

A close-up of Remi, standing at the bathroom door, staring directly at the camera with the expression of a creature who has been Betrayed.

Caption: She thinks bath time is a personal attack

Rio threw her phone onto the bed and screamed into her pillow.

This was too much.

Because Agatha Harkness wasn’t just hot. She wasn’t just hilarious. She was also unfairly, devastatingly, unbearably charming in a way that was so much worse than Rio had ever prepared for.

And worst of all?

She couldn’t stop watching. She couldn’t stop yearning.

Chapter 5

Rio was spiralling. On a daily basis.

At this point, checking Agatha’s Snapchat had become part of her daily routine. Wake up. Check the time. Check Agatha’s Snapchat. Regret everything. Repeat.

So when an interview clip featuring Agatha popped up on her Twitter feed, she clicked on it instantly.

It was a new late-night appearance and Agatha was perched effortlessly on the talk show couch, all sharp cheekbones and easy charm, dressed in a purple suit that should have been illegal.

“You’re pretty private," the host was saying. “But you do have social media, with a lot of followers, what’s your relationship with it?"

“Oh, I post sometimes,"Agatha said smoothly, flashing that lazy, movie-star grin. “I don’t post often though, I like my privacy."

“So no secret socials that aren’t accessible to the public?”

“No of course not, I’m an open book.”

Rio choked on her drink.

Excuse me???

Snapchat notification.

Agatha had posted. With shaking hands, Rio tapped in.

A video on her story. Agatha, cackling, still in her suit, clearly laugh-crying at the interview clip playing on her laptop.

“No of course not,"she repeated mockingly, then snorted. "I would literally rather die than let random people see what I actually post."

Snapchat notification.

A screenshot of her private Instagram profile. Oh god. She had Agathas private instagram handle!!!

@Agatharemiandscratch

Caption: “This is the only account that matters. All my actual closest friends and family are on snap and here, no one else. If you see my public page, congrats! You know nothing about me."

Rio dropped her phone. She wasn’t supposed to be here. She wasn’t just following Agatha’s private Snapchat—she had been accidentally added to her inner circle. A group that, apparently, consisted of her closest friends and personal contacts.

Rio was a nobody. And Agatha Harkness—award-winning actress, international superstar, painfully gorgeous human being, had no idea she existed.

And yet, here she was. Seeing things no fan was ever meant to see. This was so much worse than she thought. And she had no idea what to do about it.

Rio stared at her phone, heart pounding. She should not be doing this. Really. But at this point, she had already stumbled too far into Agatha Harkness’s secret life and there was no way she was just going to—what? Walk away? Pretend she didn’t know? Be normal about it?

No.

Because if there was one thing Rio had learned about herself, it was that she was she was not normal. She was pathologically incapable of letting things go once she was invested.

So, with a deep, slightly unhinged breath, she opened her instagram and tapped ‘Follow’ on @Agatharemiandscratch

Another Snap notification.

Her phone buzzed instantly. She clicked without thinking.

Agatha Harkness has posted a story to her instagram. Her real instagram that, oh god, only had 78 followers, her account public account had 180 million.

It was a black and white photo of her in the suit still, Remi sprawled across her lap.

Then, the next post to her instagram story:

@Theegreenwitch finally got their ass on Insta. Took you long enough

Rio stopped breathing.

Agatha—Agatha Harkness - thought she was someone she actually knew.

And she had just acknowledged her. Publicly. Well, publicly to her actual friends and family.

Snapchat notification.

A post. A photo of Agatha’s laptop screen, open to her private Instagram, showing Rio’s username at the top of the new follower list.

Caption: Imagine it taking you years to make an instagram account

Rio was going to pass out.

This was officially out of control.

Because now? Now Agatha thought she was a friend. And Rio had absolutely no idea who she was supposed to be.

Rio was not okay.

Like, on a fundamental level, her entire body had short-circuited.

Because this? This was different.

It wasn’t a story or a random update to all of Agatha’s close friends.

This was a direct Snapchat.

To her. Agatha Harkness had messaged her. Personally.

She stared at the screen for a solid thirty seconds, her brain just looping the words over and over.

Agatha Harkness sent you a Snap.

And when she finally, finally tapped it open. It was a video. Rio hit play.

Agatha was lying on her couch, glasses on, wrapped in a blanket the size of a small country, lazily sipping a glass of wine.

“Alright, explain yourself," she said, raising an eyebrow. “What finally made you get an Instagram? I need to know. I demand an answer."

Then, and this was the part that almost killed her, Agatha leaned in closer, looking directly into the camera and said, in a mock-serious tone, “Is this a cry for help? Blink twice if you're in danger."

Rio dropped her phone onto her face. Because what the hell was she supposed to do now?!

This wasn't just casually lurking anymore. This was Agatha expecting a response.

And Rio, tragically, did not have the option to spontaneously combust.

Rio stared at her phone like it was a live grenade. Because Agatha Harkness was waiting for a response.

To a question that wasn’t even meant for her.

To someone, some actual friend—who Agatha thought she was talking to.

And Rio?

Rio was not that person.

Her first instinct was to just not reply. To throw her phone across the room and never log into Snapchat again.

But then—

Another direct Snap.

Another notification.

Agatha Harkness has sent you a Chat.

A. CHAT.

Rio practically ascended to another plane of existence. She did not open it immediately. She had to mentally prepare herself. And by "mentally prepare," she meant scream silently into her hands for a full minute.

Then, finally, she clicked on it.

Agatha: HELLO. EXPLAIN YOURSELF.

Agatha: Are you ignoring me??

Agatha: How dare you.

Rio wheeze-laughed so hard she almost died. Oh god. Oh god. She had to say something.

Her thumbs hovered over the keyboard, heart slamming against her ribs.

What the hell was she supposed to say?! She couldn’t just be like, ‘Hey, funny story, I’m not actually your friend, I’m just some random gay woman who has been secretly obsessed with your secret Snapchat for weeks!’

No. No, that would be a disaster.

She needed something vague. Something neutral. Something that wouldn’t make Agatha suspicious.

So, with every single one of her nerves on fire, she typed:

Rio: idk, felt like it was time lol

And sent it.

And then immediately regretted it because who even says that?! What kind of boring, vague, loser response was that?!

Another Snap.

Agatha sent a video response immediately.

Rio did not survive it.

Because it was Agatha’s face, up close, eyes narrowed in playful suspicion.

“Mm-hmm," she hummed, dramatically squinting. "Sure. I’ll allow it—for now."

Then, just as Rio was about to recover, Agatha smirked and said—

“I’ll be keeping an eye on you."

And then winked. WINKED.

Rio was dead.

Because now?

Now Agatha Harkness was watching her. Was this catfishing? Was she catfishing one of the most famous women in the world. Rio was never going to emotionally recover from this.

Chapter 6

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

For the next twenty-four hours, Rio lived in a state of absolute, gut-churning panic.

Because now, somehow, impossibly, she had a direct line to Agatha Harkness.

And worse? Agatha expected her to be a normal person. A real person. A friend or family member.

Which Rio, tragically, was not.

She spent the entire day overthinking everything, should she reply more? Less? Should she comment on Agatha’s snaps like a normal friend would? Should she just never open the app again and move to another country?

She needed a distraction from the tangled mess she now found herself in.

She went out with Alice.

Which, under normal circumstances, would have been a good thing. Alice was her best friend, the one person in her life who could drag her out of her own head and force her to have fun.

But in this specific case, on this particular night?

It was a catastrophic mistake.

Because Rio, in a moment of tragic, unforgivable stupidity, in her drunken haze, posted Snapchat stories of her night out. Snap stories which included her actual face. Because she was dumb and drunk and for a moment forgot that Agatha Harkness could see her posts.

Snap.

A video of her and Alice at a bar, Rio laughing into her drink while Alice ranted about something wildly unimportant.

Snap.

A photo of their drinks, captioned: Alice is on her fourth conspiracy theory of the night. Send help.

Snap.

A mirror selfie in the bathroom, her actual, real-life face staring back at the camera, completely ruining her secret double life. Crop top, toned stomach and blazer all on show.

Snapchat notifications.

Agatha Harkness has sent you a Chat.

Rio blacked out for a second, the realisation hitting her as she pulled her story upwards to see who had viewed her stories. Agatha had seen. Had seen all of them.

She clicked on it with the shaky hands of a person about to meet their doom.**

Agatha: ????

Agatha: Who the hell are you.

Agatha: HELLO?

Rio stared. Then stared harder. Because this was it.

This was the end.

Agatha knew. She knew.

And Rio?

Rio was completely, 100%, irreversibly screwed.

Rio was going to throw up. (She did throw up).

Or pass out. Or die in some other, equally dramatic way because Agatha Harkness had just discovered the truth because Rio had been stupid enough to post stories tonight.

And now? Now she was waiting for an answer.

She had two choices.

1. Tell the truth and admit that she was a complete stranger who had accidentally stumbled into Agatha’s most private social media account and then—like a complete dumbass just stayed.

2. Run. Run far away and never use snapchat ever again.

And Option 2 was looking really tempting right now.

Her phone buzzed again.

Agatha: Are you ignoring me?

Agatha: I literally just saw you post. You’re holding your phone.

Rio panicked and did the worst possible thing. She opened the chat.

Which meant Agatha could see that she had read the messages.

Which meant she had no escape.

So, practically vibrating with anxiety, she finally typed back:

Rio: okay so. this is awkward.

Rio:… funny story.

Snapchat notification.

Agatha sent a video.

Rio opened it like she was defusing a bomb.

Agatha was sitting at her kitchen counter, wine glass in hand, adorable glasses perched on her nose, squinting at the camera like she was studying a new species.

“Go on,"she said, sipping dramatically.

Rio wanted the ground to swallow her up.

Rio: so. uhh. funny thing is. i was never supposed to be here.

Rio: i think u added me by accident

Rio: and then i just. stayed. bc i was scared u’d notice if i left.

Rio: so. hi.

She sent the messages and immediately regretted all of her life choices.

Snapchat notification.

Another video from Agatha.

This time, Agatha didn’t say anything at first.

She just raised an eyebrow, lips pressed together in amused disbelief and stared directly into the camera for an aggressively long time. Then, she finally parted her lips and spoke.

“So let me get this straight," she said. "You realized you weren’t supposed to be here, panicked, and then just… stayed? Like a feral cat who accidentally wandered into someone’s house and refused to leave?"

Rio gave a short manic burst of laughter at the comparison.

Rio: basically yes

Rio: except the cat also found u really attractive and made terrible decisions because of it

And then, because she was already doomed anyway (and was drunk), she hit send.

Snapchat notification.

Agatha sent a chat back immediately.

Agatha: Oh.

Agatha: Well.

Agatha: I see.

Snapchat notification.

A photo, of Agatha’s face. Looking directly into the camera. Smirking.

Caption: So you think I’m attractive?

Rio screamed into her hands.

WHAT HAD SHE DONE.

Rio was too drunk for this. Or not drunk enough.

Like, on a molecular level, she did not have the sobriety required to handle flirting with Agatha Harkness in real-time.

Because that was what was happening now. Somehow, against all logic and reason, she was currently in a back-and-forth, increasingly chaotic flirtation with one of the most famous actresses in the world.

And it had all started because she accidentally admitted she found Agatha hot.

Snapchat notification.

Another video.

Agatha, sipping her wine, eyebrow raised.

“So," she said, swirling her glass dramatically, “how long have you been secretly thirsting after me, exactly?"

Rio, having returned to the table, snorted so hard Alice turned to stare at her.

"Why are you making weird noises?" Alice asked, narrowing her eyes suspiciously. "Who are you texting?"

Rio did not answer. Because she was too busy panicking over how to respond.

And because she was exactly three drinks past responsible decision-making, she did the dumbest possible thing.

She filmed a video back.

Snap.

“Honestly?" Rio said, leaning into frame, grinning like an idiot. "Ever since I saw you in glasses cooking pasta. It awakened something in me."

Snapchat notification.

Agatha’s reply was almost instant.

A photo, biting her lip like she was pretending to think really hard about something.

Caption: So what I’m hearing is… I should wear my glasses more?

Rio blacked out for the millionth time.

Rio: that would be dangerous for my health actually

Rio: but also yes

Snapchat notification.

Agatha sent another video.

And Rio, hopeless, doomed, fully invested in this mess, opened it immediately.

Agatha was reclining on her couch now, smirking at the camera, glasses perched at the end of her nose.

“Wow," she said, voice going deliberately sultry. “Didn’t realize I had this much power over you. Interesting."

Snap.

Rio filmed back immediately.

“Okay, you need to stop," she said, pointing dramatically at the camera. “Because if you keep talking like that, I’m going to lose my mind and say something embarrassing."

Snapchat notification.

Agatha: Now I’m curious. What’s the embarrassing thing?

Rio: not falling for that trap

Agatha: Oh come on. Just a little embarrassment. For me.

Snapchat notification.

A photo of Agatha pouting dramatically at the camera.

Caption: Pretty please?

Rio almost screamed in public. And because she was a disaster of a human being, she typed a response.

Rio: u know ur dangerously hot right? like. u have to be aware of this

Agatha: Oh, I’m aware. But it’s fun hearing you say it

Agatha: Drunk you is cute

Rio ignored Alices questions as she stared at her phone in awe.

Rio nearly ascended into the heavens. Because this? This was dangerous.

And she wasn’t entirely sure she wanted it to stop.

The next morning (afternoon if you were being specific), Rio woke up with a raging hangover, a vague sense of impending doom and full of regret.

That was unhinged.

Oh god, last night, she flirted with Agatha Harkness.

AGATHA. HARKNESS.

Like it was a casual, everyday thing. Like she wasn’t just some random gay woman who had accidentally infiltrated her private Snapchat and then proceeded to flirt recklessly with a literal movie star.

And now?

Now she had to live with it.

With the knowledge that a famous, devastatingly attractive woman knew she found her hot.

Because, for some ungodly reason, Rio had zero self-preservation skills.

Her phone buzzed.

Snapchat notification.

Agatha Harkness has posted a story.

Rio clicked so fast she almost dropped her phone.

The first image. A black screen with white text.

Caption: Some of you should drink more often. Highly entertaining. 10/10

Rio froze. Because that was about her. That was 100% about her.

And the worst part?

She could hear Agatha’s smug voice in her head as she wrote it. She closed her eyes and exhaled.

Get a grip, Rio. She clicked into the next post on Agathas story.

A video, Agatha standing in her kitchen, hair half up, half falling out of the messy bun it had once been, wearing an oversized sweatshirt that was definitely stolen from someone else.

"I am making coffee,"she announced dramatically, slamming the coffee grounds onto the counter. "This is a high-stakes mission. If I do not get caffeine into my system in the next five minutes, I’ll commit crimes."

She clicked through to the next post.

A photo of her laptop screen, a Zoom meeting in progress, Agatha had put crying emojis over each persons face.

Caption: If I look interested enough, maybe they won’t ask me to contribute

The next snap.

A blurry video of Remi jumping onto Agatha’s desk mid-zoom meeting, knocking over an entire cup of coffee.

“Oh my god—REMI, YOU LITTLE, aaargghgg!”

The next snap in the story.

A mirror selfie, Agatha, half-dressed, a jacket hanging off one shoulder, hair still kind of a mess, face set in mock-serious contemplation.

Caption: If I leave my house, does that mean I have to interact with people? And if so, is it too late to cancel all my plans?

Rio continued clicking, it was only 14:30 and Agatha had already had a full day by the looks of her story.

A video of Agatha in her car, sunglasses on, deadpan expression.

“I just made eye contact with a man at a red light, and he nodded at me. Like we had a moment. Sir, I am gay. Please calm down."

Rio was fully invested at this point (well not really at this point, she’d been invested since day one of being added).

Because no one else that was just normal got to see this.

The world only knew Movie Star Agatha—composed, confident, untouchable. But this? This was Agatha in her natural state—half-feral, dramatic, and barely functioning.

Rio was obsessed and maybe a little bit in love.

Rio had, however, fully convinced herself that Agatha was done with her.

She had flirted too hard, exposed herself as a dumbass and a creeper, and surely, surely, Agatha had better things to do than entertain some random woman who had accidentally infiltrated her private Snapchat.

So she braced herself for silence.

For the inevitable moment where Agatha would get bored, realise Rio should not have access to Agatha unfiltered and quietly remove her.

And yet as she was wallowing in embarrassment and self pity. A snap chat notification came through.

Agatha Harkness has sent you a Chat.

Rio choked on air.

She opened it so fast she nearly dropped her phone.

Agatha: Recovering from last night? Or do you always go radio silent after bombarding someone with flirtatious videos and chats.

Rio wheeze-laughed immediately.

This woman was dangerous, in the most delightful way.

Rio: okay first of all. rude.

Rio: second of all. i thought u were done entertaining my nonsense so i was mentally preparing to be ghosted

Snap. A direct snap.

Agatha sent a video.

And Rio, hopeless, doomed, fully aware she was in too deep, opened it.

Agatha was lounging in her car, head tilted back, sun glasses slipping down her nose, an infuriating smirk on her lips.

“Ghost you?" she drawled, raising an eyebrow. “Why would I do that? I’m having fun."

Rio blackout malfunctioned for a full five seconds.

Rio: define fun

Agatha: You have an expressive face, even over chat

Rio died because what the hell was she supposed to do with this information?

Agatha wasn’t ignoring her. She was actively engaging. Flirting. Teasing. Like she enjoyed this just as much as Rio did.

Rio was not prepared for Agatha’s next message.

Agatha: So, where exactly do you exist in the world, mystery woman?

Rio blinked. She hadn’t really thought about it before, but—yeah. Agatha had no idea who she was or where she lived. She was just some random gay disaster that conveniently lived not too far from gated community of the elite.

For a moment, Rio debated lying.

Saying she lived five states away to remove the possibility of anything remotely real happening. She laughed at the thought, who did she think she was - of course nothing real would happen.

But instead, she typed:

Rio: about 45 mins outside the city.

Agatha: Oh? So if I needed a getaway driver, you’d be within range?

Rio: absolutely. no questions asked. where are we going, what are we stealing, i’m in

Snap.

Agatha sent her a video, of her, grinning at the camera, now back home and reclining on the couch.

“Good to know I have a criminal on standby,"she said, smirking. "Now tell me—what do you do when you're not plotting hypothetical heists?"

Rio hesitated for half a second before typing the truth:

Rio: florist

Caption: You’re telling me I’ve been flirting with a woman who literally spends all day around flowers??

Agatha: Oh, you know. Soft, romantic, makes bad decisions when drunk. It tracks.

And now, Agatha knew she wasn’t far away.

This was dangerous.

And Rio didn’t want it to stop. Rio had had all control of her life.

Today’s story updates were pure chaos.

Caption: Unfortunately, this menace has returned

Chapter 8

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Over the next week, Rio noticed a shift in Agatha’s posts.

It wasn’t a dramatic change, Agatha still posted the occasional chaotic pet snap (Remi stealing an entire sandwich, Señor Scratchy hopping into an open grocery bag like it was his new home), and she still sent the occasional teasing message whenever Rio said something particularly flustered in their chats. But the tone of her story was different.

The silly, everyday disasters were still there, but they were fewer, interspersed with a different kind of content - work-related snaps, long hours on set, photos of scripts covered in notes, vague captions like ‘sleep is for the weak’ or ‘been in this trailer so long I think I live here now.’

Agatha was stressed, it was weird how in such a short amount of time she could tell that from her posts.

But the worst part?

Rio could tell that she was trying to hide it.

She still made jokes in the captions, still kept up the façade of being cool and unbothered, but there were cracks in the performance.

The selfies she posted between takes weren’t smug or playful anymore—they were exhausted. Her messy buns got messier, her glasses appeared more frequently and in some of the videos, her voice was a little more hoarse, a little more tired, like she was running on caffeine and sheer force of will.

Their messages became less frequent too.

Rio didn’t take it personally, she wasn’t entitled to Agatha’s attention, but it was a tiny bit upsetting to not have as much contact. She’d gotten used to waking up to something from her, whether it was a teasing comment, a blurry snap of Remi being an absolute menace, or some absurdly flirty message that made Rio want to launch herself into the sun.

Now, there were days where they barely talked at all.

When Agatha did reply, it was usually late, and her messages were shorter, less mischievous, more exhausted. A tiny bit dismissive.

Agatha: Sorry, long day. Work is kicking my ass.

Rio: ur telling me u can’t just roll onto set, say something cool, and leave? what do u mean acting is hard

Agatha: I know. I should just exist and get paid for it. Tragic oversight.

Sometimes, her replies were even shorter than that.

Agatha: I’m Dead

Agatha: If I have to hear one more “note” about my delivery, I will commit crimes

Rio didn’t push. She knew enough from their contact and her public persona that Agatha wasn’t the type to admit when she was struggling and she wasn’t about to be the weirdo who pried too much.

So instead, she kept things light, desperate to stay within Agathas orbit. Even if she was a temporary distraction for the mega star.

Whenever Agatha did message, Rio responded with something dumb, something teasing, something that required zero effort to answer.

Rio: i think u should just start improvising. go completely off script. say whatever feels right in the moment. maybe throw in a musical number

Agatha: I think that’s how I get fired

Rio: counterpoint: ur a superstar. what are they gonna do. tell u no?? unacceptable. stage a coup

She wasn’t sure if it helped, exactly.

But Agatha still responded, even if it was just a half-hearted comeback or an exhausted laugh.

And somehow, the tone of their conversations changed again, despite Agatha’s hectic schedule, the replies weren’t just short and stressed anymore—they were a bit more personal, a bit more playful again.

It started with little things: a joke about Rio’s cat obsession, a sarcastic comment about Rio’s constant “I’m not a morning person” messages. But slowly, Agatha began slipping in personal questions and comments, ones that felt a little less like ‘I might just be screwing with you’ and more like genuine friendship.

It was subtle at first. A ‘what are you doing tonight?’ just to fill in the awkward space, or a ‘I can’t stop thinking about that dumb joke you made the other day.’ Sometimes, Rio found herself laughing for no reason, reading Agatha’s messages, wishing for the chance to speak to her face-to-face.

It was like an unspoken rhythm between them, this snapchat conversation that had shifted, had become comfortable. They were friends. Agatha might’ve been a superstar but their chats didn’t feel like that. They were two people who could talk about anything without pretenses, who didn’t care about the gap between celebrity and regular person.

One afternoon, Rio had a message from Agatha.

Agatha: Hey. So this might be a weird question, but do you like coffee?

Rio blinked at the screen, wondering if she was seeing things. Coffee? Where was she going with this? Was it a set up for a joke?

Rio: I mean, yes? Who doesn’t like coffee?

Agatha: I was thinking… I’ve been feeling kinda frazzled lately. I could use some caffeine and a break from filming. Would you want to meet up? Maybe grab coffee somewhere?

Rio’s heart skipped a beat. Wait, what?

Her stomach churned. Was this real? Was Agatha—Agatha Harkness—actually asking her to hang out for coffee?

Rio: Wait, hold up. Are you seriously asking me to get coffee with you? Or is this some kind of cruel joke to mess with me?

She immediately regretted sending the message. It sounded too pathetic, too dumb. But to her surprise, Agatha replied almost immediately.

Agatha: No joke. I think you’re fun to talk to. I’m actually curious to meet the person who sends me the most ridiculous messages while I’m stuck in my trailer

Rio felt a wave of nervous excitement flood her chest. Agatha had actually said it—she thought Rio, weird Rio, was fun. And she wanted to meet her? That felt… surreal.

Rio: Okay, I’m in. But this might be weird for you. I’m just a regular person, you know.

Agatha: I’m a regular person too you know. I just need a coffee and a distraction for a bit. I promise I won’t bite.

Rio: Okay, okay, so coffee. But no pressure, if you change your mind

Agatha: No pressure on you either but I wont. Just you, me, and some good coffee

And suddenly, Rio was buzzing with anticipation.

She hadn’t expected any of this, hadn’t imagined that the casual flirtation would lead to something more real. She knew Agatha was probably just looking for a moment of escape from her crazy, high-pressure life, but still, the fact that Agatha was interested in her—like willing to be seen in public interested—made Rio’s heart race in a way she hadn’t expected.

Coffee with Agatha.

She had no idea what would come of it, but there was something magnetic about the way Agatha made even the simplest things feel like a big deal.

Rio could hardly believe her luck. She was going to meet Agatha in real life!
