Chapter 9

Over the next few days, Rio found herself checking Agatha’s stories more than usual (which meant that rather than rewatching a few times, she was rewatching them over and over, not that she was obsessed or anything. Except she totally was).

She couldn’t help it, she was down bad for the woman without ever having met her in person. But she would. For a date. A coffee date.

The day they were meeting Agatha posted a story of herself in front of a window, a sunlit glow casting across her face. She looked relaxed, almost carefree, and Rio couldn’t help but notice the smile tugging at the corner of her lips.

Caption: Today is going to be a good day. I’m manifesting it

It was a subtle post, but Rio had a feeling it was a reference to their coffee date later. She was already feeling a little nervous—would it be awkward? Would Agatha even show up? Was this just another one of those casual things that Rio had somehow made into something that it wasn’t?

Rio felt that familiar tension gnawing at her. Was Agatha just being friendly, did she flirt with everyone? Or was there something more?

As the hours passed, Agatha’s snap stories kept coming, each one innocent but carrying a subtle sense of anticipation. She posted a photo of a book, casually flipped over on the coffee table.

Caption: Going to finish a few chapters and start getting ready

The final post to her story, the one that hit Rio the hardest, was posted just an hour before they were supposed to meet. It was of Agatha, in a soft green sweater, standing in front of a large mirror with a playful little half-smile and her hair down. She looked effortlessly pretty, the kind of beauty that was effortless.

The caption, though, was what made Rio’s heart skip:

Caption: Ready. Here’s to coffee dates and good company

The words, so casual, hit Rio with the weight of reality. This definitely wasn’t just a meet-up—this was a date. Obviously she had delusions throughout the week that it was definitely a date and Agatha had been hinting at it all week, but now it felt real. Rio could barely keep her hands from shaking as she stared at the screen, trying to steady her breathing.

She had never felt more unprepared in her life. How did one show up for a date with Agatha Harkness of all people?

Rio spent the next few minutes pacing around her apartment, her thoughts racing a hundred miles per hour. She knew she had to calm down but it was hard when the thought of seeing Agatha in person made her feel like her heart was going to jump out of her chest.

Then, her phone buzzed with a notification.

Snapchat notification. Chat.

Agatha: I’m on my way. See you soon!

Rio couldn’t help but smile, the nervousness melting into excitement. She had no idea how this would go, whether it would be awkward, or if they’d just slip into a comfortable rhythm that they had over chat and snap. All she knew was that Agatha wanted to meet. She was just as interested as Rio was. Maybe. Hopefully. Or she was setting her up for the biggest prank that would totally destroy her.

And that was enough to send a warm rush through Rio’s entire body before she felt like she’d been doused in cold water. Oh god, what was she doing! What is this was a joke.

Rio had tried to plan the perfect outfit, but now she wasn’t sure if anything she wore would be good enough. She opted for something simple, similar to Agathas outfit on her story, a soft cream sweater, jeans, and boots.

When she arrived at the café, she saw Agatha sitting just inside, looking out the window, a coffee cup in hand and another on the table waiting. She looked completely effortless, her hair falling in natural curls around her shoulders, and there was that same soft smile on her face as she spotted Rio walking through the door.

“Hey, you made it!”, Agatha’s voice was warm, and Rio couldn’t help but feel a little lighter as she walked over to the table.

Agatha slid her chair out for her and motioned for Rio to sit down, her eyes never leaving Rio’s as she did. There was something in that look, a little spark, a glint of genuine excitement that made Rio’s heart race all over again.

“I’m glad you came,"Agatha said softly, settling in with her coffee.

Rio took a deep breath, trying to have the tension in her shoulders finally release. This wasn’t some casual thing anymore. It wasn’t about overthinking it.

She kept repeating like a mantra: We’re just two people, meeting up for coffee. And maybe, just maybe, it would turn into something more.

As Rio scooted into her seat, the weight of the moment hit her. Her heart was racing, and every breath felt like it echoed in her chest. She tried to remind herself that this was just coffee. It wasn’t a red carpet event, and Agatha wasn’t some unapproachable superstar—she was just a person.

But still, Rio couldn’t help the feeling of being just a little starstruck. This was Agatha Harkness, the actress she’d been watching on screen for years. And harassing over snapchat for weeks on end. And now, they were sitting across from each other, sipping coffee like it was the most normal thing in the world.

“Took you long enough! I was starting to think I’d have to drink this coffee alone,” she said with a playful wink, lifting her cup. Her voice was warm, full of genuine affection but there was a hint of flirtation in it, too.

Rio’s cheeks flushed as she sat down, trying not to let her nerves show.

“Sorry, I got a little lost on the way here,” Rio muttered, her hands nervously adjusting her jacket as she avoided Agatha’s eyes.

But Agatha didn’t miss a beat. She leaned forward a little, her eyes glimmering with that characteristic spark that Rio couldn’t seem to stop getting lost in.

“You don’t have to apologize. I just like making you squirm a little. It’s cute,” Agatha teased, her smile widening as she took a sip of her coffee.

Rio felt her pulse quicken at the flirty tone, her cheeks burning, blushing bright red. She tried to play it cool but couldn’t stop the small, nervous laugh that escaped her.

“You really like to mess with me, huh?” Rio joked, trying to mask her nervousness with humor.

“Oh, I’m just getting started,” Agatha said with a wink, clearly enjoying Rio’s reaction.

Then she pulled out her phone, holding it up to snap a quick picture of their coffee cups on the table. Rio wasn’t sure if Agatha was trying to be subtle or just showing off that they were together. Either way, she couldn’t help but feel a little overwhelmed that she was part of Agathas snapchat story.

Agatha captioned the story with a playful note:

Caption: Caffeine fix with a cute girl

Rio’s heart skipped a beat as she looked at the story. She stared at the post for a second, trying to hide the mix of emotions swirling inside her. Did she just call me cute? Was she serious? Or was Agatha just being charming like she always was?

When she looked back up at Agatha, she noticed the actress was watching her closely, a mischievous grin still on her face.

“Don’t get shy now,” Agatha teased. “It’s just coffee. Not like I’m gonna bite.”

Caffeine Fix with a Cute Girl. Thats all Rio had in her head.

Rio was going to die. Right here. Right now.

Not because of a freak accident or some dramatic Final Destination-style event, but because Agatha Harkness—actual, real-life, EGOT winner Agatha Harkness, had just called her cute and meant it?

And then posted it. On Snapchat. Fair enough it didn’t have her face but you could see her torso and arms.

Rio stared at the caption, her brain buffering so hard she thought she might actually pass out. Did she misread it? Maybe she was hallucinating. Maybe the nerves had finally fried her last functioning brain cell, and she was imagining all of this—

“Are you going to drink your drink,” Agatha teased, setting her phone down. “I got you a cappuccino- thats the coffee you drink right?”

Rio jolted so hard she almost knocked her cup over. “I—yeah! Coffee! I drink…coffee.”

Agatha raised an eyebrow, amused but also looking at Rio like she wasn’t entirely sure she was okay.

Desperate to distract herself, Rio grabbed her cup and took a sip.

And immediately regretted every decision she had ever made.

The coffee was near scorching hot.

She gasped in shock, but instead of swallowing like a normal person, she somehow managed to choke on it. The burning liquid slid the wrong way, and in her panic, she sputtered—

—and drooled.

Hot coffee.

Down her chin.

Right in front of Agatha Harkness.

For a moment, there was complete silence.

Then Agatha blinked. “...Did you just drool?”

Rio slapped a hand over her mouth, eyes wide in horror. Oh god. Oh god. This wasn’t happening.

“I—uh—I—” She couldn’t even speak. She just frantically grabbed a napkin and started dabbing at her chin, hoping, praying, that Agatha would just pretend it didn’t happen.

Agatha did not pretend.

Instead, she just watched, her head tilting slightly, her expression shifting from amusement to genuine concern. “Are… are you okay?”

Rio nodded way too fast. “Mmhmm! Totally! This is fine! Everything’s fine! Coffee’s just—” she let out a nervous, strangled laugh, “—hot! Who knew, right?”

Agatha squinted at her like she was assessing whether Rio was having a medical emergency. “...You sure?”

“Yes! I do this all the time.”

“…You drool coffee down your chin all the time?”

Rio’s soul left her body. “I meant…no! I meant…I just—” She buried her face in her hands. “Oh my god.”

Agatha bit her lip, clearly trying so hard not to laugh but failing miserably. “Hey, it’s okay. At least it wasn’t, like, all down your nice cream sweater or something.”

That was supposed to be comforting, but it just made Rio groan louder. “You’re never gonna let me live this down, are you?”

“Oh, absolutely not.” Agatha leaned forward, resting her chin on her hand. “But, on the bright side, this is already the most entertaining coffee date I’ve ever been on.”

Date.

She said that word again. Date.

Rio short-circuited all over again, her brain refusing to function. “I—I—uh—”

Agatha just smiled, sipping her coffee like Rio wasn’t actively self-destructing across the table.

“So,” she said casually, “tell me more about you. I know you’re a florist, but what else is there? Any fun stories? Besides the whole coffee drooling thing, of course.”

Rio groaned. “Please let me recover first.”

Agatha smirked. “Take your time. I’m enjoying the show.”

Rio, still feeling the nervous energy buzzing between them, squirmed in her seat. Finally, she asked the question that had been weighing on her mind since Agatha had first suggested meeting up.

“So, are you not worried about being seen?” Rio asked cautiously. “Like, with the paparazzi and stuff. Are they gonna show up here and make things awkward?”

Agatha paused for a moment, her smile softening. She put her cup down, her fingers tracing the rim absentmindedly.

“No,” Agatha said slowly, looking around the café. “This place is sort of my secret spot. It’s quiet, cozy, and I come here a lot. The regulars know me, but they don’t bother me.”

She glanced at Rio, the same relaxed, confident look on her face. “Most people don’t even care enough to take a second glance. They just want their coffee, and I want mine. Simple as that.”

Rio found herself relieved by Agatha’s words. It made sense—Agatha had probably carved out a little corner of her life where she could still feel somewhat like a normal person, not always under the spotlight.

But then, a playful grin spread across Agatha’s face again.

“Besides,” she added, her voice dropping just a little to a more teasing tone, “If anyone is going to be papped, it might as well be with someone as cute as you. I’m sure it would be a good shot.”

Rio’s face went hotter, but she couldn’t help the small laugh that escaped her lips. She wasn’t used to being on the receiving end of such confidence and it left her feeling a mix of flattered and completely overwhelmed.

Agatha leaned back in her seat, taking another sip of her coffee and giving Rio an expectant look.

“So,” she said casually, her eyes twinkling with curiosity, “You must have some interesting stories, right?”

Rio swallowed, trying to steady her breath. Now that they were finally sitting across from each other, the pressure seemed to suffocate her.

The coffee date stretched on, and despite Rio's nerves and embarrassing mishaps, the chemistry between the two of them was undeniable. They talked about everything from their favorite books to embarrassing childhood stories, and the conversation flowed so easily that time seemed to slip away without either of them noticing.

By the time they finished their coffee, the café was starting to empty out, and the afternoon sunlight had softened, casting a warm glow on everything. Rio sat back in her chair, feeling both content and a little sad that it was ending.

Agatha noticed the slight hesitation in Rio’s posture and smiled softly. “I don’t want this to end,” she said, her voice a little quieter now. “But I guess we should get going before they start kicking us out of here.”

Rio chuckled nervously, trying to shake off the slight heaviness in her chest. “Yeah, I suppose we should.”

As they stood up from the table, Agatha reached for her coat, her fingers brushing against Rio’s as she grabbed it. The contact sent a small electric jolt through Rio’s body, and she had to hold her breath for a second to calm her racing heart.

Agatha looked up at her, a sly grin curling on her lips. Without saying another word, she leaned in and pressed a gentle kiss on Rio’s cheek.

It was soft, lingering for only a moment, but it left Rio’s heart hammering in her chest. Her face flushed instantly, and she found herself frozen in place for a second. She didn’t know if it was the kiss or the way Agatha was looking at her, but the world felt like it had shifted slightly on its axis.

“I’ll see you soon, yeah?” Agatha asked, her voice light, as though nothing had happened. But Rio could see the sparkle in her eyes. Agatha knew exactly what that kiss meant.

Rio, still slightly dazed, nodded. “Yeah, definitely. I... I’ll be looking forward to it.”

Agatha’s smile widened, and she gave Rio a quick wink before turning to leave. Rio stood there for a moment, watching her walk out of the café, feeling like her legs might give way under her.

After a few moments, Rio finally snapped out of her daze and made her way home, feeling like she was floating.

Once she was settled in her pajamas she pulled up snapchat. Instantly clicking again to Agathas story. There were new snaps posted.

The first snap was of Agatha lounging on her couch at home, wearing an oversized hoodie and sipping from a new cup of coffee.

Caption: Home, coffee, and a little reflection. Sometimes, a good conversation makes everything better. ❤️

Rio’s heart skipped as she stared at the story. It wasn’t much, just a simple post, but there was something in the way Agatha had captioned it—like she was reflecting on their time together. Rio couldn't help but feel like she was part of that reflection.

A few moments later, another snap came through. This time, Agatha was standing in her kitchen, dancing around with a random song playing in the background. She looked completely carefree, laughing as she spun around as Remi bounced around her. It was chaotic, lighthearted, and completely Agatha. The caption this time was just one word:

Caption: Mood

Rio couldn’t help but laugh to herself. It was exactly the kind of spontaneous, goofy thing she now knew Agatha to do when she was alone at home.

A final snap popped up. This one was a little more intimate. Agatha had set her phone on a countertop and captured a soft, candid shot of herself sitting on the floor of her living room with her rabbit. There were candles lit in the background, the soft glow making Agatha’s features look even more radiant.

Caption: Grateful for today

Rio stared at the snap, feeling an overwhelming mix of emotions. The words seemed like they were meant just for her, even if they weren’t. She couldn’t shake the feeling that Agatha’s feelings were real, that everything they’d shared earlier wasn’t just playful flirtation—it was genuine.

Still, Rio didn’t want to get ahead of herself. Agatha was a superstar, after all, and Rio was just someone she’d met for coffee. She didn’t want to build up any expectations, but it was hard when Agatha’s posts were so captivating and seemed to hint at something more.

Rio wasn’t sure how to process it all, but one thing was for sure: she was hooked. Every post, every chat, every small interaction with Agatha was starting to feel like it meant everything.

She couldn’t wait to see what happened next.

Chapter 10

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

The next few days passed in a blur of excitement for Rio.

After that coffee date, she and Agatha’s Snapchats had gone from casual to frequent and sometimes downright ridiculous. What started as the occasional “look at this cute cat I saw” snap had spiraled into a full-on exchange of chaotic energy.

Agatha sent Rio the dumbest, most unhinged snaps imaginable—her aggressively trying to flip a pancake and failing spectacularly, her standing in front of a mirror trying on a hat that was three sizes too big, or a zoomed-in video of her blankly staring at the camera as dramatic opera music played in the background.

Rio, in turn, sent her own brand of nonsense—flowers from the shop that she had given terrible names ( Caption: this is Gregory, the saddest tulip), a sneaky video of Alice falling off a step ladder (she was fine, but it was hilarious), and even an accidental snap where she meant to show Agatha a cute flower arrangement but ended up sending a picture of her thumb.

Somehow, this exchange of nonsense felt... weirdly intimate. Every snap felt like another little peek into Agatha’s real personality, not the glossy A-list version. And every time Rio’s phone buzzed, she felt that little thrill of anticipation, hoping it was Agatha.

One evening, like clockwork, Rio settled onto her couch, fully prepared to waste an irresponsible amount of time rewatching Agatha’s story posts.

The first snap? Agatha, grinning at a dimly lit bar, her arm around Bucky, the human golden retriever (with teeth) of a best friend.

Caption: Getting our karaoke on! 🎤 Don’t judge, we’re professionals. #ItsAllAboutTheVibe

Rio snorted. Professionals? If Agatha’s singing voice was anything like her pancake-flipping skills, this was about to be interesting.

The next snap was a chaotic video—Bucky, dramatically belting out a verse of some cheesy pop song, while Agatha tried to harmonize but kept dissolving into laughter. Her voice was shockingly good—like, ‘she could out-sing some Billboard charting artists’ good. But the moment Bucky hit a bad note, she lost it, her laugh ringing through the speakers.

Then, the next snap nearly made Rio drop her phone in surprise.

It was a much-drunker Agatha, cheeks flushed, hair slightly messy, the selfie angle all kinds of terrible.

Caption: Who needs talent when you’ve got confidence?!

Rio couldn’t stop herself from laughing. It was weirdly comforting, seeing Agatha not as the impossibly perfect actress the world knew, but as a goofy, drunk woman in her thirties who took unflattering drunk selfies like the rest of humanity.

And then—

A notification.

It wasn’t a story. It was a direct snap.

Rio tapped it open, and immediately, her heart did a gymnastics routine.

The video started with Agatha sitting in a corner booth, her chin resting in her hand, a dopey, mischievous grin plastered on her face. She blinked at the camera, clearly drunk but still composed enough to be dangerous.

“Riooooo,” she sing-songed, her voice a little too loud for the intimate setting. And of course, she still sounded like an angel even while drunk. Unfair.

Agatha paused dramatically, narrowing her eyes. “I’m having so much fun, but you know what would make it better?”

She gasped, as if struck by a sudden, genius realization. “You.”

Rio had approximately three brain cells left.

Agatha leaned closer to the camera, her grin widening. “Next time, we’re doing karaoke together. And I will be judging you.”She pointed a finger at the camera, swaying slightly as she did so.

Then she giggled, dropping her head onto the booth cushion. “Just so you know, you’re kinda... special.” She paused again, as if debating what she’d just said, then nodded to herself, very satisfied. “Yep. Special. In a good way. Okay, byeeee.”

She blew an exaggerated kiss to the camera before the snap ended.

Rio sat there, staring at her phone like it had just delivered life-altering news.

Did Agatha Harkness just call her special?

She replayed the snap. Twice. Okay, five times. Agatha was definitely drunk, but that message? It felt real. The fact that she had sent her that snap, in the middle of a night out with her best friend, meant something, right?

Rio exhaled sharply, trying to ignore the fact that her face was approximately the temperature of the sun.

She quickly recorded a response, determined to keep it cool even though her insides felt like a shaken soda can.

The video was short, just her shaking her head dramatically. “You’re so right—I’m absolutely judging you, Agatha Harkness! Karaoke queen or not.” She smirked. “But next time, I’ll be there. Just don’t get mad when I pick the worst duet song imaginable.”

She hovered over the send button, hesitating for a split second before pressing it.

Now, all she had to do was wait.

Which was, of course, impossible.

She turned on a movie to distract herself. A movie that may or may not have starred Agatha, but that was beside the point.

Then, her phone buzzed again.

New Snap from Agatha Harkness.

Rio sat up so fast she nearly knocked over her drink.

She opened it.

It was another video, Agatha in the back of a car, probably on her way home, looking still very tipsy but with the most ridiculously smug smile.

“You’re right, I’m a mess,” she admitted, dramatically flipping her hair. “But I don’t even care. Because guess what? You’re fun, Rio.”

She leaned a little too close to the camera, whispering conspiratorially, “Let’s meet up again. And this time, you have to do karaoke with me.”

Then, just as Rio was about to combust—

Agatha winked.

And added, “We’ll have our own little duet... in more ways than one.”

The snap ended.

Rio sat in stunned silence, her entire system malfunctioning.

She was so screwed. She was obsessed with this woman.

The next morning, Rio woke up to see a flurry of snap stories from Agatha, and she couldn't help but grin. It was clear from the first snap that Agatha was feeling the effects of her night out. The first photo showed Agatha curled up in bed, her hair a tangled mess, with a slightly pained expression on her face. Remi was nestled beside her, looking far more well-rested than she was.

Caption: Having a rough morning… But Remis still winning, she has lost of the bed

Rio couldn’t help but laugh at the sight. Agatha was still as gorgeous as ever, even when half-dead from a night of karaoke and drinks. The way Remi was sprawled across her, like she was the one taking care of her, just added to the humor of the whole scene.

A few snaps later, Agatha posted a video of her a chaise across her bedroom, where Bucky was sprawled out, snoring loudly, wearing sunglasses despite it being morning. Agatha’s voice could be heard in the background, though her words were slightly muffled, and the caption read:

“Bucky’s still passed out like he doesn’t have a care in the world. At least he’s doing it in style”.

Then came the next snap, a video of Agatha holding her phone out in front of her as she slowly sat up in bed, rubbing her eyes. “I don’t know who allowed me to do karaoke in the first place,” she muttered, looking utterly exhausted. But then she flashed a mischievous grin at the camera and added, “Actually, I think I might’ve been born for the stage. But maybe next time I’ll avoid embarrassing myself.”

Rio chuckled, feeling like a small part of the chaotic energy Agatha had shared the previous night had seeped into her life. Agatha, though clearly hungover, was still radiating charm. It was the kind of relaxed, candid side that Rio loved seeing, one that felt human. Normal.

Then, a few snaps later, Agatha posted a photo of her breakfast—a giant bowl of cereal with a dramatic amount of sugar on top.

Caption: Cereal therapy. The only thing that will save me today. And yes, Remis eating my toast. No, I don’t care that she’s spoilt

Rio couldn’t resist sending a quick reply, teasing her: I thought you were the one with the confidence to sing karaoke but can’t even keep your toast to yourself? 🙄

Agatha’s snap came through almost immediately in reply, a blurry selfie of her with Remi perched on her shoulder, looking like a bodyguard.

Caption: I regret nothing. Except maybe letting Bucky make me sing ‘Dancing Queen’.

Rio’s laughter bubbled up as she read her message, feeling the lighthearted connection they had.

The next few snaps on Agatha’s story showed a more domestic side of Agatha, still lounging in bed, with a few clips of Bucky finally waking up on the chaise, groaning and rubbing his eyes. There was something endearing about their shared hangover recovery, with Agatha posting little moments of frustration mixed with humor. It felt so normal so unlike the life that anyone would expect them both to lead.

Then, one last snap —a simple photo of Agatha, still looking disheveled but with a content smile on her face, holding up a cup of coffee.

Caption: This is the cure. I think I owe l an apology for my embarrassing karaoke skills. But you know what? It was totally worth it

Rio smiled at the screen, feeling a sense of closeness with Agatha that she hadn’t expected. The casual nature of their messages made it seem like they were old friends, not someone famous and someone who had just met her.

As she stared at the screen, Rio couldn’t help but feel excited about what would come next. Agatha was down to earth, funny, and even a little bit clumsy when she wasn’t being perfect. It felt like a connection worth pursuing.

Chapter 11

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Rio’s phone buzzed with a new Snapchat notification from Agatha. She opened it immediately, excitement surging through her, tangled up with nervous energy.

It was a picture of Agatha, effortlessly stunning in a smart-casual outfit, standing in front of an upscale restaurant. The warm glow of the lights behind her cast a golden sheen over her face, making her look even more glamorous, like she belonged in that world—because she did. Agatha Harkness wasn’t just anyone. She was the kind of person who frequented places like this, who moved through life with the kind of confidence that made people stop and stare.

Caption: How do you feel about trying this place out for dinner tomorrow? I’ve just had a business lunch here, and it’s gorgeous. I can get us a reservation. ❤️

Rio’s heart stuttered in her chest. A date? A real date?

She had been trying so hard not to overthink things, to play it cool, to not let herself get too carried away by the playful messages and lingering glances. But this—this was different. This wasn’t just coffee or a casual hang out. This was an actual date in a high-end restaurant, a place that practically screamed romance and exclusivity.

Her fingers trembled slightly as she typed back.

Rio: I’d love that! I’d love to join you!

She hit send before she could overanalyze every word, before she could spiral into wondering if she should’ve played it cooler or if she sounded too eager. Her stomach felt like it was doing backflips.

And then, another realization crashed over her.

She had to tell Alice.

Alice had been her best friend since childhood, the one person Rio had always been able to confide in. If there was anyone who would understand the sheer insanity of what was happening right now, it was Alice.

She quickly started typing.

Rio: I need to tell you something, and I can't keep it in anymore. I’m kind of freaking out, but I need to be honest.

Alice’s reply came almost instantly.

Alice: Okay, spill! You’re scaring me a little with this dramatic intro!

Rio inhaled sharply, her fingers hesitating over the screen. How was she even supposed to phrase this in a way that made sense?

Screw it.

Rio: I think I’m going on a date with Agatha Harkness. For real.

She barely had time to process what she’d just sent before Alice’s response exploded onto the screen.

Alice: WHAT. WHAT. WHAT??????? ARE YOU KIDDING ME. IS THIS A JOKE. RIO, WHAT ARE YOU EVEN SAYING RIGHT NOW.

Rio bit her lip, half laughing, half panicking.

Rio: I swear, Alice. We’ve been talking on snapchat for a while now. It started out kind of casual, you know? I met her for coffee last week. But then today, she asked me out. To this super fancy restaurant. And I think she’s serious about it. I don’t know if I’m freaking out more about the fact that it’s Agatha Harkness or because she actually seems to like me

Another long pause. It was almost agonizing.

Alice: RIO WHAT ARE YOU SAYING. RIO. WHAT. WHAT DO YOU MEAN SHE “SEEMS TO LIKE YOU” OF COURSE SHE LIKES YOU. SHE JUST ASKED YOU ON A FANCY DATE????? HOW IS THIS HAPPENING. HOW IS THIS REAL. HOW IS THIS YOUR LIFE.

Alice: DO YOU UNDERSTAND HOW INSANE THIS IS. I NEED YOU TO EXPLAIN EVERY DETAIL TO ME RIGHT NOW. WHEN DID THIS START. WHEN DID SHE START SNAPPING YOU. WHEN DID SHE DECIDE YOU WERE WORTHY OF HER GLAMOROUS ATTENTION. I NEED A TIMELINE. IM LOSING MY MIND.

Rio let out a strangled laugh, running a hand through her hair. Yeah, that made two of them.

Rio: I KNOW. I KNOW. It doesn’t feel real. I feel like I’m in some kind of alternate reality where things like this actually happen. Like, am I secretly the main character in some ridiculous rom-com and nobody told me?

Alice: Apparently, yes. I need to know EVERYTHING. What are you going to wear? Are you going to tell me every detail after? Is she as hot in real life as she is on screen?

Rio groaned, flopping back against her bed, phone clutched to her chest. What was she going to wear? What was she even supposed to wear to a date with Agatha Harkness in a restaurant like that? Was she supposed to go full glam? Was a dress too much? Would dressing casually make it seem like she wasn’t taking it seriously enough? And what if she said something stupid? What if she got all nervous and awkward and ruined everything?

She exhaled sharply, forcing herself to stop spiraling. Agatha had asked her out for a reason, right? She wasn’t doing this as a joke. She wasn’t just being nice.

She liked Rio.

That fact alone made her brain short-circuit.

Her phone buzzed again.

Alice: Listen. You’ve got this. I know you’re freaking out, but you’re amazing, Rio. Don’t overthink it. Just be yourself, and you two will have an incredible time. And please, for the love of everything, ring me the SECOND you get home. I need every single detail.

Rio let out a slow breath, feeling a little steadier. Alice was right. She needed to stop freaking out. She needed to just breathe.

This was real. This was happening.

And tomorrow night, she had a date with Agatha Harkness.

The next morning, Rio woke up feeling jittery. Tonight. It was happening tonight.

She had barely gotten used to the idea of Agatha flirting with her, and now she was supposed to sit across from her at a fancy restaurant, making eye contact, eating expensive food, and acting like a normal human being?

Her phone buzzed. A Snapchat notification from Agatha.

She opened it to see a picture of a market stall overflowing with fresh flowers. Agatha stood in front of them, one perfectly manicured hand reaching toward a bouquet of deep red roses.

Caption: Flowers are very on theme for me at the minute.*

Rio’s heart nearly exploded. That was a reference to her.

Okay, keep it cool, she told herself, even though she was literally hugging her phone.

She snapped a quick response, showing a close-up of the tulips in the background, adding:

Rio: The tulips look good! Looking forward to tonight, see you soon Agatha

After sending it, she collapsed onto her bed and groaned into a pillow. She sounded so boring. How was she supposed to flirt when Agatha was so effortlessly cool?

The rest of the day was a blur of nerves. Every outfit she tried on either felt too much or not enough. She changed at least five times, overthinking everything from her earrings to whether she should attempt eyeliner (she shouldn’t but she did).

Eventually, she settled on her favorite little black dress, a cute jacket, and some heels that were just high enough to feel fancy without the risk of breaking her ankle.

As she was checking herself in the mirror, her phone buzzed again.

Another Snapchat story post from Agatha.

She opened it.

And promptly squeaked.

Agatha stood in front of a full-length mirror, her reflection a vision of elegance. A tailored deep forest green suit hugged her frame perfectly, a crisp white blouse tucked inside. She wore high heels and her hair fell in soft waves over her shoulders. Her makeup was flawless, enhancing her already sharp features.

Caption: All set for tonight.

Rio immediately felt three inches tall.

She could not compete with that level of sophistication. She looked like she was dressed for a cute dinner date. Agatha looked like she was about to Ocean 8 a whole fortune and break hearts doing it.

Panicking slightly, she snapped a mirror selfie back—her dress, her jacket, her considerably less dangerous heels.

Caption: You look gorgeous, Agatha. I’m trying my best to keep up. See you soon

And then, in a moment of courage (or stupidity), she added a wink emoji.

Immediately, she regretted it. Who even was she? Why was she winking?!

No time to dwell. She grabbed her keys and left before she could talk herself out of the whole thing.

By the time Rio pulled up to the restaurant, her nerves were a full-blown symphony.

And then she saw her.

Agatha stood near the entrance, hands tucked into her pockets, looking like she had just stepped out of one of her movies. The glow of the restaurant’s lights gave her an almost ethereal look, and the way she was smiling—warm, genuine, like she was actually excited to see Rio—made Rio’s brain short-circuit.

This was real. This was happening.

She got out of the car, determined to be cool about it, but as she stepped forward, her heel got caught on the curb.

There was no stopping it.

One second, she was walking toward Agatha with what she hoped was an air of confidence. The next, she was flailing, making a noise that sounded very undignified as she nearly face-planted into the pavement.

Instead, she stumbled forward, straight into Agatha’s arms.

For a long second, there was silence.

Rio was mortified. She was literally being held upright by Agatha, who smelled unfairly good, like expensive perfume and a hint of something deeper, warmer, something entirely intoxicating.

Agatha chuckled, her grip steadying Rio as she helped her back to her feet. “Well, that’s one way to fall for me.”

Rio let out a strangled sound. “I…that’s illegal. You can’t just say things like that.”

Agatha smirked, looking entirely too amused. “Noted.”

Somehow, Rio survived long enough to make it inside.

The restaurant was intimate and exclusive, the kind of place where everything looked polished and expensive.

The restaurant was so fancy that Rio immediately felt out of place. The napkins looked more expensive than her rent.

But she was determined to be classy.

Sophisticated. The kind of person who belonged in a place like this.

That lasted about five minutes.

The moment the waiter set down a ridiculously expensive bottle of wine, Rio reached for her glass at the exact wrong time, knocking the bottle slightly off balance.

It wobbled.

Her soul left her body.

Agatha’s reflexes were apparently supernatural, because she reached out and steadied it before disaster struck. Then she turned to Rio, smirking.

“Planning to cause some chaos?”

Rio, utterly mortified, immediately blurted out, “I was testing your reaction time.”

Agatha raised an eyebrow, amused. “And?”

“Ten out of ten. You passed.”

Agatha laughed, shaking her head. “Good to know.”

Rio spent the next five minutes gripping her wine glass like a lifeline, determined not to touch anything else.

Rio had one goal: Be normal.

Then the bread basket arrived.

Agatha, with her usual elegance, tore off a small piece and ate it like a regular human being.

Rio, in her infinite wisdom, decided to tear off a piece of bread with one hand.

Unfortunately, her brain forgot how physics worked.

The bread did not tear cleanly. Instead, she somehow managed to catapult a chunk of it directly into Agatha’s lap.

For a horrifying second, time slowed down.
Rio’s eyes widened. Agatha looked down at the piece of bread now sitting politely on her thigh.

Then she looked back up, expression unreadable.

Rio, in full panic mode, saluted.

Why? Who knows.

Agatha blinked. Then, slowly—so slowly—she started laughing.

“Are you… saluting me?”

Rio groaned, covering her face. “No. I mean yes. But only because my body malfunctioned.”

Agatha plucked the bread from her lap, popped it into her mouth like it was no big deal, and grinned. “If you wanted me to try that piece so badly, you could’ve just said so.”

Rio groaned louder. “I’m leaving my own body. Goodbye.”

Agatha laughed again, shaking her head. “Please don’t. I’m actually enjoying myself.”

Rio peeked at her through her fingers. “You are?”

Agatha smirked. “Oh, definitely.”

The conversation was surprisingly easy. Agatha asked more about Rio’s job as a florist, listening intently as Rio described the oddest customer requests she’d ever gotten (including the time someone wanted an apology bouquet for a cat).

“Did the cat forgive them?” Agatha asked, eyes twinkling.

“I hope so,” Rio sighed. “That bouquet was expensive.”

Agatha talked about her latest film project, about the chaos of working on set, about the time an animatronic nearly took her out mid-scene.

“Not the glamorous Hollywood lifestyle I imagined,” Rio teased.

“Oh, it’s a mess,” Agatha admitted. “But a fun one.”

At one point Agatha managed to get a bit of sauce on her thumb, which she licked off in a subconscious move, one that Rio took note of.

Rio, was in the process of choking on her own spit.

She quickly smacked her chest, coughing violently, praying to every higher power that Agatha hadn’t noticed.

Spoiler: Agatha noticed.

She raised an amused eyebrow as Rio finally made her way over, still slightly wheezing.

“Are you okay?” Agatha asked, the corner of her mouth twitching.

“Oh yeah, totally,” Rio said quickly. “Just… breathing. Weirdly. You know how it is.”

Agatha smirked. “I do?”

Rio had no idea what she was saying anymore.

They laughed, they ate, they shared more about their lives, their likes and dislikes. And as the night wore on, Rio forgot to be nervous.

By the time they stepped outside, the air had cooled, but Rio felt warm.

Agatha turned to her, eyes soft. “I had an amazing time tonight.”

“Me too,” Rio admitted. “I wasn’t sure what to expect, but… this was perfect, despite me embarrassing myself.”

There was a pause. A shift in the air. Agatha stepped closer, her hand brushing lightly against Rio’s arm.

Rio swallowed. Was this happening?

Agatha tilted her head, her voice teasing but quiet. “Would it be too forward if I kissed you?”

Rio almost said something dumb, like ‘Depends on the angle’ but thankfully, her brain short-circuited before she could.

Agatha leaned in, about to close the distance.

Rio’s brain shut down.

She realized, all at once, that Agatha was about to kiss her.

And in that moment, Rio panicked.

Not by pulling away. Not by saying something dumb.

No.

By shifting her weight at the exact wrong second, causing her to accidentally bump into Agatha’s shoulder instead of meeting her lips.

For a full, horrifying second, they just… stood there.

Agatha blinked. “…Did you just dodge me, did you not want me to kiss you?”

Rio immediately wanted to die. “NO! I mean yes of course I did! I didn’t mean to! My foot moved and then I—”

Agatha, looking far too amused, shook her head. “Unbelievable. I try to be romantic, and you juke me.”

“I DIDN’T JUU—”

Agatha, still smirking, gently cupped Rio’s face with both hands, effectively stopping her from any more unintentional evasive maneuvers.

“Let’s try that again,” Agatha murmured.

The kiss was soft at first, like she was savoring the moment, but when Rio responded—when she melted into it, hands finding their way to Agatha’s waist—it deepened, slow and real.

When they pulled apart, Agatha smirked. “I could get used to that.”

Rio, still breathless, let out a nervous laugh. “Trust me, I’m not going anywhere.”

Agatha grinned. “Good. Because this is just the beginning.”

And as Rio watched her drive away, she realized she really, really hoped that was true..

As Agatha got into her car, she posted a final Snapchat story from the front seat, showing the view of the city lights outside the window.

Caption: Had an amazing night with someone special. Can’t wait to see what’s next. ❤️

Rio, her heart still racing from the night, smiled as she swiped through the story. Someone special. She felt the same way.

Chapter End Notes

They finally kissed! Comments are appreciated!

Chapter 12

The next few days felt like a whirlwind for Rio. Every time her phone buzzed, her heart would leap in her chest, hoping it was another snap from Agatha. It had become an obsession, and she knew it. Actively acknowledged that it had been an obsession for some time now.

She couldn’t help herself.

Every time she opened Agatha's stories, she was looking for something, a new post, a new message, a clue that Agatha was just as interested as she was.

It was almost like she couldn’t believe it was happening. That someone like Agatha Harkness, who had such an enviable life, would be interested in her. It felt like a dream, and Rio was determined to enjoy every moment, even if it meant losing herself in Agatha’s world of snaps.

One evening, while scrolling through Agatha's Snapchat, Rio saw a post that made her heart race. It was a picture of Agatha standing in front of her current movie set trailer (which luckily for her was being shot locally), her hair pulled back in a loose ponytail, wearing a casual outfit that somehow looked effortlessly stylish.

Caption: Big news! Landed a new role in an exciting project I’ve been dying to share with you all. Can’t wait to dive in when filming here wraps up!

Rio’s eyes widened. She couldn’t believe it. Agatha had just landed another major role. She had worked hard, and it was clear that her career was soaring. Rio’s admiration for Agatha deepened, but there was something else too, pride. She felt proud of Agatha.

Before Rio could stop herself, she quickly sent a snap chat back:

Rio: Congrats on the new role! That’s amazing, Agatha. You’re going to crush it, as always. 😘

A few moments later, Agatha replied with a snap of herself smiling widely, showing a bit of excitement.

Caption: Thank you! I’m so excited, and you’re too sweet. I’m definitely going to need someone to celebrate with! Maybe I can talk you into another date? 😉

Rio froze, her heart skipping a beat. Did Agatha just ask her out again? Was this really happening? It took Rio a second to process the message before she quickly typed out a response.

Rio: I’d love that. I’m definitely up for another date. Just tell me when and where! 😏

She hit send, then quickly held her breath, waiting for Agatha’s reply. The uncertainty of it all made her stomach flip. But when Agatha’s message came through, her heart melted.

Agatha: It’s a date then. How does Saturday sound? I’ll make it worth your while, promise. 😘

Rio smiled, her fingers tapping out a quick response without thinking.

Rio: Saturday sounds perfect. I’m looking forward to it already. 😁

As soon as she sent it, she felt a wave of relief and excitement flood through her. It was official. They were going on another date.

But even as the excitement settled in, Rio couldn’t stop watching Agatha’s Snapchat stories. It was almost like she was waiting for another piece of the puzzle to fall into place. And Agatha didn’t disappoint. She posted a mix of work-related content and more personal moments. One story showed Agatha laughing with the cast and crew on set, giving Rio a glimpse of her behind-the-scenes life.

The next post, Agatha shared a snap of her with Remi, curled up beside her in her living room.

Caption: Relaxing after a long day of filming. Remis good company, but I’d be lying if I said I wasn’t wishing someone else was here to keep me company

Rio couldn’t help but feel the tension in Agatha’s words. She knew the reference was to her. It had to be. Right?

And that made Rio feel both flattered and a little giddy. Agatha was clearly still thinking about her, and she was making it clear that she wanted to spend more time with her.

Rio leaned back against her bed, a smile creeping onto her face as she watched the snap. She couldn’t help but daydream about what Saturday would be like. Would Agatha kiss her again? Would they do something completely different? Maybe dinner and then a walk, just the two of them, still away from the public eye, away from everything else. Just them.

As the hours passed, Rio’s mind continued to wander, lost in thoughts of Agatha and the next time they would meet.

Saturday couldn’t come soon enough.

The week leading up to the next date felt like it lasted forever for Rio. Every day, she’d eagerly check Agatha’s Snapchat stories, hoping for a new update. Agatha’s posts became a delightful mix of sweet moments, chaotic snippets of her life, and the occasional glimpse of Bucky, who seemed to be constantly by her side.

One morning, Agatha posted a snap of her making coffee in the kitchen, her hair still messy from waking up. She had a huge mug in her hand, steam rising from it.

Caption: My morning routine: coffee, Remi and Scratchy cuddles, and pretending I have it all together

Rio couldn’t help but smile at the sight. Agatha was so down-to-earth in those moments, a further glimpse into her everyday life, and it made Rio feel even closer to her.

Later that afternoon, Agatha posted another snap, this time with Bucky who was standing next to her while they were both in the middle of a grocery store trip. Agatha was laughing, her arms full of groceries, while Bucky had a shopping cart piled high with random items—some of which didn’t seem like they belonged in the same cart at all. Agatha’s caption was classic Agatha.

Caption: Bucky’s idea of grocery shopping: Anything goes. Pray for me, please

Rio couldn’t help but laugh at the image. It was just so real, two friends acting like complete goofs. And Bucky, always the troublemaker, seemed like someone who brought even more chaos into Agatha’s already hectic life. Rio found it oddly endearing, and she couldn’t wait to hear more about their ridiculous adventures.

That evening, Agatha posted a snap of Remi lying across her lap while she tried to get some work done at home. The snap was a cute, cozy moment, showing how Agatha balanced the demands of her career with the simple joys of life.

Caption: Remi: 1, Me: 0. Trying to work, but my daughter is demanding attention. Anyone else’s dog think they own the place?

Rio loved how Agatha was so open and unguarded in sharing these small glimpses of her life, and she couldn’t wait to actually be a part of it all. Hopefully, maybe.

The next day, Agatha posted a much more chaotic story, showing herself at a photo shoot. It was clear from the snaps that things weren’t going according to plan. Agatha was running around, in heels and a stunning dress, while the crew scrambled to adjust lighting.

Caption: The glamorous life of a movie star: Hair, makeup, and running around in heels like a chicken with its head cut off. 💁‍♀️

In another story, she showed a video of the behind-the-scenes mayhem as she accidentally knocked over a cup of coffee on set. Bucky could be heard laughing in the background as Agatha scrambled to clean it up, all while keeping her composure like a pro.

Rio couldn’t stop laughing as she watched the story. She felt like she was right there, part of the chaotic energy of Agatha’s life. Agatha in reality was so far removed from the idea of a perfect celebrity and Rio found that incredibly refreshing.

But then, something shifted. Later that week, Bucky was the one who posted something that made Rio’s stomach flutter at the sweetness of it. It was a video of Agatha and Bucky, they were lounging on a couch, Remi curled up between them. Agatha was holding a book, reading aloud to Bucky, her voice animated and warm. He’d covered the post with the caption:

Caption: Finally some downtime with Agatha and Remi. My most favourite person in the world 💕

Rio felt her heart swell. There was something about that moment—about seeing Agatha in this quiet, unguarded space—that made Rio realize just how deeply she was falling for her. She was a woman who loved deeply, cherished her friends, and valued her downtime, just like Rio did.

Then, just as Rio was lost in her thoughts, Agatha herself posted something. It was a selfie, taken at an odd angle, showing her laughing uncontrollably at something off-screen. Her eyes were bright, her cheeks rosy, and she had the kind of smile that could light up the whole room. She’d not bothered to put any caption.

There was something so authentic in that post, something real that Rio was drawn to. She wanted to see her this unguarded in person, wanted to be the one to make her face light up in laughter like that.

As the week drew to a close, Rio couldn’t stop checking Agatha’s stories. She felt more and more connected to her, and more and more eager to see her again. And as Agatha's snap story that evening popped up, showing a simple selfie in bed.

Caption: Ready for the weekend. I have a date tomorrow night which I cannot wait for!

Rio’s heart skipped. She couldn’t wait either.

Chapter 13

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Saturday had finally arrived, and Rio could barely contain her excitement. She had spent the entire week anticipating this moment, replaying every conversation in her head, wondering what Agatha had planned and how the evening would unfold. Would the night be as magical as their last date? Would she manage to keep her cool this time? The questions buzzed in her mind, an endless loop of nervous energy that no amount of distraction could quiet.

By mid-afternoon, she was a bundle of nerves. She spent extra time picking the perfect dress, a little black number that hugged her curves just right. She turned from side to side in the mirror, tugging at the hem, adjusting the neckline. Too much? Too little?

With a sigh, she grabbed her phone and typed out a message to Alice.

Rio: I think I’m spiraling.

Alice: Again?

Rio: YES. What if I embarrass myself again? What if she realizes I’m a disaster and regrets asking me out a second time?

Alice: Lol Rio this is the third time, coffee counts.… and hear me out… what if you relax and have a great time?

Rio: Unlikely to relax

Alice sent back a GIF of a cat dramatically collapsing onto a couch. Rio rolled her eyes but smiled. She needed to pull herself together.

Just as she was about to apply her lipstick, her phone buzzed.

Snapchat notification.

She clicked it and was met with Bucky’s story rather than Agathas as she was expecting.

The first post was a short video. The angle was slightly tilted, capturing Agatha standing in front of a mirror. She wore a stunning purple dress, though the way she was fiddling with the sleeves suggested she wasn’t happy with it.

Bucky’s voice came from behind the camera, teasing but affectionate. “Never seen her this nervous before. This is her second outfit change.”

Rio’s heart skipped. Agatha was nervous?The idea sent a flutter of warmth through her chest.

The next snap nearly stole her breath away. Agatha had changed into a sleek black jumpsuit with a plunging neckline that left little to the imagination. She looked like she had stepped out of a fashion magazine, her glossy black heels completing the look. Bucky was clearly gushing over her.

Caption: Looking a million dollars! My girl’s dressing to impress tonight. One word - STUNNING

Rio stared at the screen, heat rising to her cheeks. She dressed up… for me?

Her nerves skyrocketed. She quickly snapped a picture of herself in the mirror, tilting her head slightly, making sure the lighting caught her at the right angle. She wasn’t sure if she looked as flawless as Agatha, but she felt good. Confident, even.Well, as confident as someone about to go on a date with Agatha freaking Harkness could be.

She hesitated for a second before posting it to her story.

Caption: Ready for my date. Hope I don’t embarrass myself again! Wish me luck!😬💚

Immediately, she tucked her phone into her purse before she could overthink it. She had a date to get to.

Unknown to Rio, across town, Agatha stood in front of the restaurant bathroom mirror, gripping the edges of the sink as she stared at her reflection. Her heart was racing.

Bucky had been relentless the entire evening.

“I can’t believe you’re this worked up,” he had teased while lounging on her couch, watching her swap out outfit after outfit. “This isn’t even your first date with her.”

“That’s exactly why it matters,” Agatha had muttered, smoothing down the fabric of the jumpsuit.

Bucky had just smirked, arms crossed. “You like her.”

Agatha had shot him a glare, but it lacked heat. “Shut up.”

Now, standing under the dim lighting of the restaurant’s bathroom, she felt her stomach twist in knots. What if I come on too strong? What if she thinks this is too much?

With a deep breath, she pulled out her phone and took a quick snap of herself in the mirror. Her smile was genuine, but she could see the nervous energy in her eyes.

Caption: Is it weird that I’m nervous for my date? Meeting up with someone special

She sent it to her story before she could second-guess herself.

Rio had just stepped out of the cab when her phone buzzed again. She checked her screen and saw Agatha’s new snap.

The sight of Agatha in the restaurant bathroom, looking effortlessly stunning yet clearly nervous made Rio’s heart pound.

She read the caption twice. She’s nervous, too.

A rush of confidence surged through her. Maybe she wasn’t the only one overthinking everything.

Taking a deep breath, she smoothed down her dress and walked toward the restaurant entrance. Whatever happened tonight, she was ready.

When she stepped into the restaurant, her stomach was a tangled mess of nerves, but the second she spotted Agatha, everything else faded into the background.

Agatha was already waiting by their table, a tailored black jacket now draped over her sleek jumpsuit, making her look even more impossibly put-together. She stood when she saw Rio approaching, her lips curling into that warm, slightly mischievous smile Rio had already found herself looking forward to.

“You made it,” Agatha said, her voice laced with something soft—relief, maybe.

Rio, who had spent the entire cab ride hyping herself up, promptly forgot how words worked. “Yeah! Of course. I mean—why wouldn’t I? Not like I was gonna—uh—ditch you or anything.”

Agatha raised an amused brow, eyes twinkling as she pulled out Rio’s chair for her. “Well, that’s good to know. Would’ve been quite the ego hit if you’d stood me up.”

Rio groaned as she sat down, covering her face for a moment. Off to a great start.

“Can we pretend I didn’t just say that?”

Agatha let out a soft chuckle, sliding into her own chair across from her. “Not a chance.”

And just like that, the awkwardness melted into something easy, something light.

Dinner was Italian this time, and every part of it felt effortless. They shared plates of pasta, bickered about whether pineapple belonged on pizza (“Absolutely not,” Agatha had scoffed, to which Rio had dramatically clutched her chest in betrayal), and swapped ridiculous childhood stories.

At one point, as Agatha sipped her wine, Rio launched into an animated retelling of the time she had attempted to impress a girl in high school by pretending to be a skater.

“So there I was,” Rio said, gesturing wildly with her fork, “brand new skateboard, absolutely no ability to do anything cool. But did that stop me from attempting a sick trick in front of the girl I had a crush on?”

Agatha, already grinning, leaned in slightly. “Oh, please tell me you landed it.”

“I wish.” Rio let out a dramatic sigh. “Instead, I hit a rock, fell flat on my face, and my board rolled into the street, where it was immediately run over by a school bus.”

Agatha threw her head back with a laugh, the sound warm and unrestrained. “Oh, no. That’s tragic.”

“The worst part?” Rio shook her head. “The girl didn’t even like it. She just—sighed. Like she was embarrassed for me.”

Agatha winced sympathetically but was still clearly holding back laughter. “That’s brutal.”

“It was.” Rio pointed her fork at her. “You better not judge me.”

Agatha smirked, eyes twinkling. “Oh, I’m absolutely judging you.”

Rio groaned, slumping in her chair. “That’s fair.”

And that was the rhythm of the night—Rio being her usual slightly awkward self, and Agatha taking it all in stride, clearly entertained, clearly charmed.

There was a moment during dessert when Rio found herself staring, completely and utterly distracted as Agatha wiped a bit of cream from the corner of her mouth with her thumb. Just like last time.

She did it so absentmindedly, completely unaware of how breathtaking she looked in that second. The way the candlelight caught in her hair, the soft curve of her lips, the ease with which she carried herself—it was enough to make Rio’s heart trip over itself.

Agatha caught her staring.

“What?” she asked, tilting her head slightly.

Rio panicked. “Nothing! I mean—just—you had something on your face.”

Agatha’s lips twitched, clearly amused. “I got it, though.”

“Yeah,” Rio said weakly. “Yeah, you did.”

She was so down bad.

By the time dinner was over, Rio half-expected Agatha to say goodbye, maybe give her another kiss and part ways. But instead, Agatha glanced outside, where the city lights painted the streets in a warm, golden glow, and smiled.

“Want to walk for a bit?” she asked, slipping her jacket back on. “It’s a nice night.”

Rio, despite knowing that prolonging this evening meant prolonging her suffering, found herself nodding. “Yeah. That sounds… nice.”

And it was.

They strolled side by side through the quiet streets, the conversation still flowing effortlessly between them. At one point, their hands brushed, and Rio nearly short-circuited, but Agatha didn’t seem to notice—or maybe she did, she let her hand linger but moments later, when Rio didn’t take it, she casually slid her hand into the pocket of her jacket, as if stopping herself from doing something impulsive.

By the time they reached the parking lot, Rio was both exhilarated and exhausted from the constant internal battle of you idiot you should have taken her hand, you’ve messed it up, don’t make this weird, don’t make this weird, don’t…

Agatha turned to her with that soft, knowing smile. “Can I drive you home?”

Rio blinked, caught off guard. “You don’t have to do that—”

“I want to.” Agatha tilted her head, as if reading the hesitation on Rio’s face. “Unless you don’t want me to?”

Rio hesitated for only a second before exhaling. “Okay. Yeah. I’d like that.”

There was no rush to say goodbye. No eagerness to be apart. Just Agatha, looking at her like she was something precious.

And Rio, despite herself, let herself fall just a little bit more.

As soon as Rio climbed into Agatha’s G-Wagon, her heart started hammering against her ribs. It was ridiculous—she’d just spent an entire evening with Agatha, laughing, talking, completely in sync. But now, alone in the enclosed space of her car, the air felt… heavier.

She fumbled with her seatbelt, nearly missing the buckle before clicking it into place. Be cool, Rio. It’s just a car ride. People get driven home all the time. It’s fine. Normal.

Agatha started the engine after taking her address. The car smelled like her—a mix of something woody and subtly sweet, a scent Rio could drown in.

She sneaked a glance at Agatha, watching how effortlessly she moved. One hand on the wheel, the other adjusting the settings with an ease that made Rio’s brain short-circuit. Even driving, Agatha carried herself with that same quiet confidence, like she was in control of not just the car but the moment itself.

Rio, meanwhile, was not in control.

The distance between them felt almost nonexistent in the intimate space of the car. She could hear Agatha’s soft breathing, see the way her fingers flexed slightly against the wheel. It made Rio’s pulse quicken, an undeniable pull deep in her chest.

And then, before she could talk herself out of it, Rio reached over and slid her hand into Agatha’s.

It was instinctive, a quiet need for closeness that she should have taken during their walk. As soon as her fingers made contact, Rio felt a rush of warmth flood her system—oh, wow, okay, this was happening.

Agatha glanced over, eyes widening slightly, surprised but not pulling away. Instead, she simply squeezed Rio’s hand, intertwining their fingers. Her grip was firm, grounding, like it was the most natural thing in the world.

For a moment, neither of them spoke. The silence wasn’t awkward, though it was charged, filled with something unspoken, something real.

Rio’s brain, of course, did not shut up.

Oh my god, she’s holding my hand. And she’s not letting go. Holy shit, her hand is really soft. Do I have sweaty hands? Please don’t be sweaty. Oh god, what if they’re sweaty?

Her panic was momentarily derailed by how nice it felt—Agatha’s fingers wrapped around hers, thumb tracing idle patterns over the back of her hand, a small, unconscious gesture that made Rio’s chest squeeze.

She barely thought before pulling out her phone and snapping a picture. The soft lighting of the dashboard cast a golden glow over their entwined fingers, the moment so simple yet somehow monumental.

Caption: Feels right. Can’t explain it any other way. ❤️

Rio hesitated, then turned the phone to show Agatha, suddenly worried it was too much.

Agatha looked at the picture, then at Rio. A small smile played at the corner of her lips, something warm and amused.

“I think I’d have to agree.”

And that was it. Rio was done for. Absolutely, completely done for. Ruined forever. No one else would ever be able to compare.

They were still holding hands when Agatha pulled up in front of Rio’s apartment. The engine hummed softly as the car idled, but neither of them made a move to get out.

Rio turned to Agatha, heart pounding.

“I had a really great time tonight,” Agatha said, her voice quieter now, more intimate. Like she didn’t want the night to end.

Rio swallowed, suddenly feeling like she was standing at the edge of something big. “Me too,” she whispered.

The air between them shifted.

Agatha was watching her, her gaze flicking down to Rio’s lips and back up again. There was a pull a gravitational force drawing them together.

And Rio—well, Rio wasn’t going to hesitate. Not this time.

She shifted closer, her body angling toward Agatha’s, her heart hammering in her chest.

And then she froze. Because suddenly, her brain caught up to her actions, and all at once, her thoughts thundered in her mind.

What if I’m reading this wrong? What if she doesn’t want to kiss me? Oh god, what if I miss? What if I accidentally headbutt her? Or worse, what if my lips are dry?!

She panicked.

Like, full-body seized-up gay panic.

So instead of gracefully closing the distance, Rio’s body jerked forward in the most awkward, unnatural movement known to mankind. Her hand, still resting on Agatha’s lap, slipped, and she ended up face-planting into Agatha’s shoulder.

A soft thud.

A beat of silence.

Rio, still face-down against Agatha, screamed internally.

“Oh my god,” she groaned against the fabric of Agatha’s jacket. “Kill me. Just end it. I can’t live like this.”

She felt Agatha’s body shake.

Then laughter.

Warm, amused, affectionate laughter.

Agatha didn’t push her away. Didn’t make it weird. She just… laughed, a deep, rich sound that sent a whole new wave of heat through Rio’s body.

Rio slowly peeled herself off Agatha’s shoulder, mortified. “I—I was trying to—I thought I—” She exhaled sharply. “Never mind. I ruined it.”

Agatha was still grinning, eyes twinkling as she reached up and tucked a stray piece of hair behind Rio’s ear.

“I have dejavu right now but you didn’t ruin anything.” Her voice was impossibly soft. “You’re adorably awkward.”

Rio covered her face. “That is not what I was going for.”

Agatha chuckled, and then—before Rio could combust entirely—she reached out, tilting Rio’s chin up ever so slightly.

“Hey,” she murmured. “Relax.”

And then she leaned in.

This time, there was no hesitation, no panic. Just warmth, softness, intent.

The kiss was slow, unhurried, filled with something deliberate. Agatha’s lips moved against Rio’s in a way that made her melt, her whole body suddenly feeling too light, too heavy, all at once.

Rio sighed into it, fingers instinctively tangling in Agatha’s jacket, her entire brain short-circuiting.

And then, just as Rio deepened the kiss, moving to push her tongue into Agathas mouth—Agatha stopped.

She pulled back, breathing a little unsteady, eyes searching Rio’s with something unreadable.

“Rio,” she whispered, her voice a little shaky. “We need to slow down.”

Rio’s stomach plummeted. Ruined it. Oh my god, I actually DID ruin it.

“I—I’m sorry,” she blurted, hands flying up as she backpedaled at record speed. “I didn’t mean to—if I misread—oh god, I made it weird, didn’t I? I made it so—”

“Rio.” Agatha’s voice was patient, amused, and Rio realized she was still smiling. Not rejecting, not upset, just… steady.

Agatha reached for her hand again, squeezing gently. “I want this, you,” she said, her tone quiet but certain. “But I don’t want to rush. This is too important to screw up.”

Rio exhaled, chest loosening. “…You mean I didn’t screw it up?”

Agatha laughed, pressing a lingering kiss to Rio’s forehead.

“No, sweetheart,” she murmured. “Not even close.”

And that, that was the moment Rio knew she was in serious trouble.

“I don’t want you to go yet.”

Agatha smiled softly, her fingers brushing Rio’s cheek in a tender touch. “I don’t want to go either.”Her voice was full of sincerity. “But let’s take this slow. We’ve got plenty of time.”

Rio nodded, a small smile tugging at her lips. She felt a little flutter of excitement, a sense of anticipation for what was to come. Agatha wanted her, but she also wanted to get things right. And Rio felt the same way.

This wasn’t just about a hot kiss or a fleeting attraction—it was about something deeper. Something that was worth taking their time over.

Agatha leaned in one last time, placing a final soft kiss on Rio’s lips. “Goodnight, Rio. I’ll see you soon,” she whispered, her voice a promise that lingered in the air between them.

Rio watched as Agatha started the car and drove away, her heart still racing. As she walked into her apartment, she couldn’t help but smile.

She was definitely, madly, obsessively in love with Agatha Harkness.

The next morning, Rio woke up feeling lighter, her mind still replaying every moment of the night before. The kiss. The way Agatha had looked at her. The way she had pulled back—not because she didn’t want her, but because she did. Because she wanted to do this the right way.

Snapchat notification.

Agatha Harkness sent you a Snap.

Caption: Don’t look at me. Dont talk to me, I need Espresso first.

Rio let out a soft laugh, rolling onto her back as she typed out a response:

Rio: Noted. How about I just admire you from afar, then?

“Okay. You have my attention, you may now speak."

Rio laughed again, already feeling like her day was off to a ridiculously good start.

The rest of the morning was a steady back-and-forth of snaps - Agatha documenting her chaotic attempt at making breakfast (while Remi begged and stole from the side), Rio sending a picture of her flower shop.

Caption: Back to my humble life of selling pretty things

Caption: Please save him

Rio sent back a chat message as a response:

Rio: Even celebrities can’t keep houseplants alive???

Caption: Even the rabbit judges me. Bettayal

Caption: Top secret new script! Work mode activated.

Caption: Long day ahead. Wish me luck

Caption: Survived

Rio sent back a picture of the prettiest bouquet she’d created that day:

Caption: If you were here, I’d give you this. Consider this a virtual ‘You Did Amazing’ award. 💐

Agatha’s reply was immediate. A simple selfie, soft smile, messy hair, a warmth in her eyes that sent Rio’s heart flipping over itself.

Caption: You’re trouble, Rio

Caption: Okay, hear me out—nature date. Hiking, fresh air, questionable choices. You in?

Caption: Also, my daughter would like to attend. She insists

Caption: I mean… a date with you and Remi? How could I possibly say no? When are we doing this?

“Tomorrow. Noon. Bring appropriate shoes. And snacks. This is survival, Rio. We must be prepared."

Agatha: Oh, don’t worry. If we get lost, I’ll carry you out over my shoulder like a heroic lesbian in a period drama

Rio: I will hold you to that

Agatha: Also… maybe after, you could come back to mine? No pressure, just… hang out. Get some food. Meet Señor Scratchy in person, if you're lucky

Rio’s heart skipped.

This was something new. Agatha was inviting her into her space. Into her home.

Rio: I’d love that.

That evening, as Rio curled up on her couch, still buzzing from their conversation, she instinctively opened Snapchat, already knowing whose story she was about to re-watch like it was a tv show.

Agatha had posted again.

The first snap was a selfie. Agatha standing in her kitchen with her hair in a messy bun, wearing an oversized sweatshirt that had clearly been through multiple washes and probably belonged to Bucky at some point, glasses perched on her face.

Caption: Cleaning mode activated. Don’t be fooled, I watch a lot of cleaning tiktoks

“One of us is preparing our house for a visitor who they want to impress. The other is a freeloader who does not contribute to this household in any way.”

The next video showed Agatha attempting to vacuum but Remi kept chasing the machine like it was her mortal enemy, barking at it like it had personally wronged her.

“I am fighting for my life here. Remi please, mama needs this house clean.”

Rio didn’t know what Agatha meant, her house looked spotless anyway.

Then came a picture of her kitchen counter where some actual ingredients were laid out.

Caption: I’m about to cook. Groundbreaking I know

Caption: This better taste amazing

Then came another short video of Agatha, stirring something in a pot, a smug little smile on her face.

“Look at me. Domestic. A homemaker. A provider."

The camera zoomed in on Señor Scratchy, who was sitting on a cushion on the counter giving her the most judgmental rabbit stare ever.

“Okay, fine, I used too much salt, but we’re learning."

Rio’s chest felt warm watching all of it. She didn’t know why this made her heart race more than the expensive restaurant dates or the way Agatha flirted with her over snaps. But there was something so endearing about seeing Agatha like this, messy, normal, preparing for their date in her own chaotic way.

And the best part.

Rio would be with her in that space tomorrow.

Chapter Notes

The next day, Rio drove out to the hiking spot Agatha had sent her the co-ordinates for, the excitement thrumming in her veins making her feel ridiculous. It was just a nature date, just a casual hike, but knowing Agatha, nothing about today would be normal.

Her phone buzzed.

Snapchat notification.

Agatha Harkness sent you a Snap.

She opened it while sitting in her car, grinning at the sight. It was a video of Agatha standing next to Remi, both of them looking way too serious. Agatha wore sunglasses and an all-black athletic outfit.

“We are ready. We are prepared. We are about to conquer nature."

The camera panned to Remi, who was literally vibrating with excitement, tail wagging so hard her whole body shook.

“Well, one of us is prepared. The other is an unpredictable agent of chaos, just to warn you."

Rio laughed and sent back a selfie, showing herself in her own hiking gear, leggings, a tank top, and a flannel tied around her waist.

Caption: Reporting for duty. Please don’t let your daughter kill me!

Meeting up in person still made Rio’s stomach flip but the moment Agatha saw her, she grinned like a kid who just spotted a best friend on the playground.

"Look at you!" Agatha said, giving Rio an appreciative once-over before pulling her into a quick hug, placing a kiss against her cheek. "You really committed to the hiking aesthetic. I’m proud."

"Figured I should dress for survival," Rio teased.

Agatha smirked. "You assume I’d let anything happen to you. Foolish. I will fight a bear if I need to."

Rio raised an eyebrow. "Bold of you to assume you’d win against the bear."

Agatha just grinned. "I have a plan. It involves distraction, Remi, and a well-placed protein bar.”

Their banter continued as they set off on the trail, the peaceful atmosphere of nature clashing spectacularly with Remi, who was having the time of her life. She zoomed ahead, chased butterflies, and nearly tripped Agatha twice.

Naturally, Agatha shared some of the chaos to her snapchat.

A video of Remi darting through a field like a madman:

“Nature’s most majestic creature. No thoughts, just vibes."

A photo of Rio, back to the camera, standing on a rock, arms crossed like she was contemplating life:

Caption: She regrets agreeing to this

A clip of Agatha dramatically wiping sweat off her brow, “We are two hours in. Supplies are running low. Morale is questionable. No, I will not check the map.”

Rio snorted and took her own snap, Agatha pointing at something in the distance, side profile only so you couldn’t see her face, while Remi tugged at her leash in the opposite direction.

Caption: A fearless leader. And a woman trying to not get us lost

The moment disaster struck, Rio wasn’t even looking.

One second, everything was fine, Agatha was ahead of her, making some ridiculous joke about being an explorer in uncharted lands and then — SPLASH.

Rio’s head snapped up just in time to see Agatha face-down in a shallow stream, water splashing up around her while Remi pranced around the edges, barking excitedly like she had just conquered a great foe.

Rio’s laugh exploded out of her before she could help it. "Oh my god, are you okay?"

Agatha pushed herself up, completely soaked, blinking in disbelief before looking up at Rio like a betrayed heroine.

“I have been attacked."

"You tripped!"

"I WAS BETRAYED!"

Rio gasped for air between laughs, pulling out her phone as Agatha dramatically flopped back into the water like a fish, hair floating around her.

Snapchat was already open.

She recorded a video of Agatha floating in two inches of water, arms spread out like she was about to ascend to the heavens.

“RIP to my date. Taken too soon by the cruel forces of nature and her own dog.”

Agatha opened one eye, lifting her face slightly above the water, concealed by the veil of her hair. "Tell them I went down fighting."

Rio cackled, snapping another picture—Agatha sitting up now, back to her, hair dripping, looking like a drowned cat.

Caption: Survivor of The Great Stream Betrayal. 2025

Agatha sighed. "Remi, you absolute fool of a dog, why would you do this to me?"

Remi just wagged her tail, clearly thrilled by the chaos.

They ended up sitting on a dry rock while Agatha attempted to wring out her clothes, muttering dramatically the whole time.

"So," Rio teased, smirking. "Still think you could take a bear?"

Agatha paused, looked down at herself, soaked and defeated and exhaled.

"I may have overestimated my abilities."

By the time they made it back to Agatha’s car, the Snapchat chaos had reached peak levels.

Bucky had replied to one of Agatha’s posts.

Bucky 🏴‍☠️: LMAO I CANNOT BREATHE.
Bucky 🏴‍☠️: Remi saw an opportunity and took it. QUEEN

Caption. You’re dead to me

Caption: Today’s MVP: The agent of chaos herself

And then, in a more private moment, Agatha nudged Rio’s arm, smirking.
