Rio smiled, feeling that familiar warmth rush through her.

"Only if I get to officially meet Señor Scratchy."

Agatha laughed. "Deal."

And as they climbed into their cars, dripping, exhausted, but laughing, Rio realized that this might have been the most fun she’d had in a long, long time.

Following behind Agatha’s G-Wagon, Rio couldn’t help but feel a mix of nerves and excitement curling in her stomach. This was new territory, going to Agatha’s home, stepping into her personal space. Their dates had been nice, chaotic, and playful, but this? This was intimate in a way that made her heart hammer in her chest.

As they approached a gated community, Rio's eyebrows lifted. The entrance was guarded, the kind of place where you couldn’t just stroll in uninvited. The security booth had two guards, one of whom waved as Agatha rolled her window down.

"Evening, Miss Harkness," the guard greeted. "Bringing home a stray?"

Agatha snorted, glancing at Rio through her side mirror, a smirk playing on her lips. "This one’s special, Martin. Be nice."

The security gate opened, and Rio followed Agatha’s G-Wagon down a winding private road, passing massive, stunning houses, each with perfectly manicured lawns and long driveways. Everything about the place screamed wealth and privacy which made sense, Agatha was one of the biggest actresses in the world.

But it still hit different seeing it in person.

Agatha pulled into her driveway, and Rio had to physically stop her jaw from dropping. The house was gorgeous, modern but cozy, warm lighting spilling through the tall windows, a mix of dark wood and sleek black accents that somehow still felt lived-in.

She barely had time to take it all in before Agatha hopped out of her car and walked over to Rio’s, tapping on her window.

"You coming in, or are you just gonna sit there and admire my impeccable taste from a distance?"

Rio snorted, rolling her eyes as she got out of the car. "Your ego is out of control."

Agatha smirked. "And yet, here you are."

With that, she grabbed Rio’s hand, interlacing their fingers as though she’d done it a thousand times and led her inside.

Inside, the house was even more stunning —a perfect blend of luxury and personality. Plush furniture, soft lighting, a few scattered script pages on the coffee table and in the corner of the living room?

A giant dog bed, clearly owned by Remi.

Speaking of— Remi galloped in like a small horse, tail wagging, sniffing at Rio before flopping dramatically at her feet.

"Remi approves of you being here," Agatha said, watching as the dog nudged at Rio’s leg. "That’s a good sign."

Rio laughed, scratching behind Remis ears. "I feel honored."

Agatha guided her through the open-plan kitchen, where sleek black cabinets met a marble island big enough to host a cooking show, then past the living room, where floor-to-ceiling windows overlooked a backyard straight out of a magazine.

"Wait, is that a pool?" Rio asked, stepping closer to the glass doors.

Agatha grinned. "It is. Heated, too." She leaned against the counter, arms crossed. "I’ll take full credit for designing the backyard, but mostly I just wanted a place to drink wine in the hot tub."

Rio chuckled, still absorbing everything. "This place is… incredible. But it’s so you."

Agatha arched a brow. "Messy but charming?"

"Exactly."

They wandered through the hallway, where Agatha pointed out different rooms—her home office, a cozy guest room, another door she jokingly called 'The Forbidden Closet of Doom', until they reached the staircase and went up to her bedroom.

Agatha stopped at the doorway, tilting her head. "Want to see the inner sanctum, or should I keep some mystery alive?"

Rio smirked. "I feel like that ship sailed the moment I watched you fall into a stream."

Agatha laughed, pushing the door open.

The bedroom was exactly what Rio expected from the glimpses in her posts and somehow not at all, a massive bed with plush blankets, soft golden light filtering through the windows, books stacked on the bedside table, and a play enclosure in the corner.

Rio’s eyes widened as a familiar little creature twitched its nose at her.

"Señor Scratchy," she whispered. "It’s an honor."

Agatha grinned, walking over to scratch the rabbit’s ears. "He’s very selective about who he likes. Let’s see if you pass the test."

Rio crouched, holding out her hand, and to her delight, Señor Scratchy hopped over and gave her a sniff before nudging her fingers.

Agatha gasped dramatically. "Betrayal. He never likes new people this fast."

Rio grinned. "Guess I’m just special."

After the tour, they ended up back in the kitchen**, where Agatha pulled out a bottle of wine and the chicken she’d been marinading the day before.

"Drink?" she asked, already grabbing two glasses.

"Sure," Rio said, leaning against the counter, watching as Agatha poured.

There was something different about this moment. The air between them felt charged, heavier than before. Maybe it was the warm lighting or the quiet intimacy of being alone in Agatha’s house, or maybe it was just that Rio had been thinking about kissing her since their last date. Had had to physically stop herself while they were out hiking from grabbing her.

Agatha handed her a glass, then paused, looking at Rio in a way that made her heart stutter.

"You’re staring," Rio murmured, delighting in the blush that rose on her cheeks at the comment.

Agatha tilted her head, lips twitching into a smirk but her voice was softer when she said, “Yeah. I am."

Before Rio could overthink it, Agatha set down her wine and took a step closer, fingers brushing against Rio’s wrist.

"Is this okay?" Agatha asked, voice low.

Rio barely managed to breathe out, “Yeah."

That was all it took—Agatha crowded her against the kitchen island, closing the distance, her lips pressing against Rio’s in a way that was soft but confident, teasing but deep enough to make Rio’s knees feel weak.

Rio let her hands slide up Agatha’s arms, gripping her shoulders as she kissed back, letting herself sink into the feeling of Agatha’s warmth, her scent, the way she kissed like she had all the time in the world.

Then, Agatha’s hands found Rio’s waist, pulling her flush against her, deepening the kiss just enough that Rio felt the edges of her self-control start to fray.

The counter dug into Rio’s back, and she didn’t care, all she cared about was the way Agatha’s fingers tightened against her, the way she nipped at Rio’s lower lip before pulling back just enough to whisper against her mouth.

"God, I’ve been dreaming about this."

Rio let out a breathless laugh, hands still tangled in Agatha’s shirt. "Took you long enough, I’ve been waiting for you to do that all day."

Agatha chuckled, resting her forehead against Rio’s for a second before sighing. "You’re gonna be trouble, aren’t you?"

Rio smirked. "Hmmm."

Agatha just grinned, kissed her again, and muttered, “Good.”.

The next morning, Rio woke up feeling warm, happy, overwhelmed in the best possible way and maybe a little smug. Last night had been a lot, in the most amazing way. The kisses, the way Agatha had looked at her, the way they had curled up on the couch afterward, just talking, sipping wine, and stealing lazy contact in between conversation.

Now, she was lounging by Agatha’s pool, legs stretched out on a cushioned sunbed, the heat of the morning sun soaking into her skin wearing nothing but one of Agathas T-Shirts. Agatha was beside her, equally relaxed, one hand entwined with Rio’s fingers. Glasses on (and didn’t that do something to Rios heart rate) reading her script.

It was quiet. Peaceful. And Rio didn’t want to be anywhere else.

She glanced at their hands, Agatha’s fingers curled so naturally between hers, and without thinking too hard about it, she lifted her phone and snapped a picture, just their hands, fingers intertwined, resting against Rio’s bare thigh. Pool in the background.

Caption: ☀️🌊💛

It wasn’t a big declaration. Just a little something for her story. A test, maybe. A way to see if Agatha would object (even though she hadn’t objected to a very similar photo on their last date).

She posted it to her Snapchat story, then locked her phone and let her head tip back against the sunbed.

A moment later, Agatha shifted, glancing over at Rio’s phone with a lazy smirk.

"Did you just sort of soft-launch me?"

Rio snorted, biting her lip. "Maybe."

Agatha hummed, seemingly unbothered, stretching her legs out further. "Ballsy of you."

"Would you rather I delete it?"

Agatha smirked, eyes closing again. "Nah."

The peace and serenity were f a poolside lounge didn’t last long.

Because ten minutes later, Rio’s phone buzzed and when she checked, she saw that she had one new message.

From Bucky.

Bucky: 👀👀👀

Bucky: EXPLAIN. RIGHT NOW.

Agathas phone also started buzzing.

Bucky: AGATHA. WAKE UP. I KNOW YOU’RE NEXT TO HER

Rio snorted nudging Agatha’s arm with her elbow. "Bucky’s having a meltdown."

Agatha groaned, rolling over and reaching for her phone. Within seconds, her own Snapchat was opened and a video sent in response to her best friends drama filled messages. A sleepy, half-hearted glare aimed at the camera as she mumbled:

“Barnes, eat my ass.”

Rio was dying, but Bucky wasn’t done.

Bucky: I KNEW IT.

Bucky: I SAW THE SIGNS. I SAW THE LOOKS.

Bucky: WAIT. ARE YOU DATING OR JUST FLIRTING? I NEED DETAILS. RIGHT NOW.

Agatha, still sun dazed, rolled onto her side and pressed her face into Rio’s stomach with a groan.

"Block him for me," she muttered.

Rio laughed, taking the opportunity to run her fingers through Agatha’s messy curls. "Not a chance. This is way too fun."

Over the next few hours,Rio and Agatha continued the game, posting cryptic snaps to their stories that gave absolutely nothing away but just enough to keep people guessing.

Agatha posted a photo of her coffee mug next to Rios mug.

Caption: Sunday mornings are better like this."*

Rio retaliated with a boomerang of Remi flopping onto her lap, adding:

“She’s a terrible guard dog, by the way."

Meanwhile, Bucky’s Snapchat story had become a conspiracy board, filled with screenshots of their snaps, captions like:

Y’all. I am INVESTED.

Agatha said she’d never soft launch a relationship, but here we are

Do I approve? Do I panic? Do I plan the wedding?!

Agatha finally broke and messaged him directly.

Agatha: If you don’t stop, I’m uninviting you from movie night and taking my house key off of you

Bucky: YOU CAN’T SCARE ME. I HAVE SCREENSHOTS.

Agatha: I’m muting you now.

Bucky: COWARD.

Rio was doubled over laughing at this point, but what made her heart stutter was the fact that Agatha didn’t seem to care about the speculation from her best friends drama.

She was having fun with it.

This felt real.

Later that evening, after a long, lazy day swimming, lounging, and expertly dodging Bucky’s continued onslaught of nosy messages,Rio and Agatha found themselves curled up on Agatha’s couch.

The TV was on, but neither of them were really watching. Agatha was absentmindedly twisting a strand of Rio’s hair around her fingers and Rio was trying very, very hard not to read too much into still being in Agathas house over 24 hours later.

Because this felt like more than just casual flirting. It felt natural. Easy. Like they had known each other for years instead of just weeks (in person - they had technically known each other and being conversing for three months).

And yet, they hadn’t actually talked about what this was.

That little voice in Rio’s head, the one that liked to whisper warnings, that reminded her how many times she had gotten too invested in something that wasn’t real, that she was a weirdo who clung too tightly too quickly, was starting to get louder.

So she took a breath, swallowed her nerves and asked, “What are we doing?”

Agatha’s fingers stilled in her hair. “What do you mean?”

Rio hesitated, but she forced herself to keep going. “I mean is this just fun? A fling? Or do you actually want something more?”

She hadn’t meant for it to sound so serious ( again, too deep, too soon) but there it was—out in the open, buzzing in the air between them.

Agatha was quiet for a second, her eyes searching Rio’s face like she was weighing her words carefully.

Then, finally, she sighed and sat up a little, shifting so they were face to face, ocean blue eyes seeming to stare deep into Rios soul. “I wouldn’t have invited you here, into my home, if I just wanted a fling.”

Rio’s breath hitched. “You wouldn’t?”

Agatha shook her head, a smile tugging at her lips. “No, Rio. I actually like you. Like, really like you.”

The weight that Rio hadn’t even realized she’d been carrying lifted instantly, leaving her feeling giddy and weightless.

Still, she had to tease, just a little. “So, what you’re saying is… you’re obsessed with me?”

Agatha huffed a laugh, rolling her eyes. “I take it back. I hate you.”

Rio grinned but before she could respond, Agatha was already leaning in, brushing her lips against hers, soft and slow, like a silent promise.

After their conversation, Rio felt the rush of emotions settle inside her chest. Agatha didn’t just want this to be casual. She wanted something more. That knowledge made her heart skip a beat, and she found herself grinning like a fool.

But she also knew that subtlety was key. She wasn’t going to make any big declarations yet. So, she snapped a picture of her feet stretched out on the couch, no faces, just a little glimpse of her afternoon. Agatha’s presence in the background inly evidenced by half her arm showing thrown around Rios waist.

She posted it to her own Snapchat story.

Caption: Sunday vibes ☕💛

The picture was vague, just enough to make people wonder, was she still hanging out with someone? Whose was the gorgeous house she was in? It was the perfect balance of mystery and hint that someone had decided to take a chance on her, was with her.

A few minutes later, Rio checked her phone again, and she saw that Agatha had posted to her story, just for her and a handful of close friends. It wasn’t public, not like Rio’s story.

Caption: When the dog picks the guest over me… I’ve been betrayed

Rio: She’s a traitor

A few minutes later, Agatha replied with a smirking selfie, sending it straight to Rio’s chat. Her face was soft, looking effortlessly gorgeous.

Agatha: Don’t make me fight you for her

Rio laughed softly, feeling warmth spread through her chest at how easy this all felt.

But it wasn’t long before Bucky started sending questioning messages again. This time direct to Rio instead of to his best friend.

Bucky: So... y’all are having fun, huh?

Bucky: You two soft launching or what? Need a hint for the paparazzi?"

Rio smirked at the screen. Bucky’s was never subtle, but it was kind of funny that he was spying from the sidelines, that was usually Rio.

Rio: We’re just vibing. Nothing to see here. Go back to planning your next karaoke night

Bucky: I know what I saw. I’m an expert, ok? You can’t hide this from me

Rio rolled her eyes, tossing her phone on the couch. She could hear Bucky’s over-the-top antics already, as if he was already planning to tell the world every single detail ( of course he wouldn’t) , even though neither of them had made anything official yet.

But what surprised her was that Agatha didn’t mind.

She wasn’t worried about Buckys questions. She didn’t seem to care about being seen by her friends and family. It wasn’t about image, it was about what they shared between them.

Even now, as Rio checked her phone again, replaying Agatha’s snap stories, which were just sweet little glimpses of their time together, a quiet moment with Remi curled up by her side and the soft click of their wine glasses clinking together. Nothing flashy. Nothing public. Just theirs.

She glanced down at her phone, and as Agatha’s latest snap story popped up—Remi wagging her tail on Rio’s lap, her face absent from the frame but her laugh clearly audible—Rio felt a wave of contentment wash over her.

As Rio drove home that night, Agatha reluctantly informing her she had a talk show appearance that night, the warmth from the weekend still lingered. The hours (and night and then another day) spent with Agatha felt like they’d flown by, like a dream she didn’t want to wake up from. She smiled to herself as she glanced at the picture of her and Agatha’s intertwined hands still sitting in her gallery.

The memory of Agatha’s soft laugh, her teasing glances, and that heated kiss goodbye was enough to make Rio feel giddy all over again.

But, as the miles stretched on, Rio found her mind slipping into quiet reflection. Was this too much too soon? Was she rushing into something, or was it as real as it felt? She hadn’t expected this weekend to turn into anything other than a fun few days, but now… now, she was not so sure.

A few hours home, her phone buzzed in her lap, breaking her out of her thoughts. It was a snap from Agatha.

She opened it with a grin.

Agatha had sent her a video behind-the-scenes vibes before the talk show. It was a quick video, showing Agatha standing backstage at a busy set. She was in full glam, hair done in perfect waves, wearing a sleek black dress that shimmered under the studio lights. In the background, the faint sound of people hustling about, preparing for the show, was audible.

But what caught Rio’s attention was the brief moment when Agatha glanced at the camera, her smile a little softer, like she was thinking of someone in particular. Rio’s heart skipped.

She responded with a snap of her own, her face grinning brightly.

Caption: Looking amazing as always. Knock 'em dead, superstar. 💫”

She hit send and tried to push the growing excitement aside,

Later that night, Rio tuned into the talk show. She didn’t want to seem like she was stalking Agatha, or was already the overly obsessed girlfriend ( especially when they’d not actually defined their relationship) but how could she not watch when she had only been with her a fee hours ago.

Agatha was stunning on stage, her charisma was undeniable as she answered questions about her new projects, her acting career, and everything else she had going on. But, as the interview progressed, the host, clearly wanting to dig a little deeper, asked about Agatha’s personal life.

"So, Agatha, you’ve always been very private when it comes to your relationships," the host said, their voice teasing. "Is there anyone special in your life right now?"

For a split second, Agatha hesitated, and Rio couldn’t help but notice the way she adjusted in her seat, a little smile playing at her lips.

“I’ve learned over the years to keep some things for myself,” Agatha replied with a soft laugh. “But I’ll admit, there’s someone who’s been keeping me company lately."

The way Agatha said it, so casual yet so undeniably intimate, sent a wave of warmth through Rio. She couldn’t help but grin to herself. It was the first time Agatha had said something so openly in front of a crowd.

The host didn’t press further, seemingly satisfied with the response, but Agatha was still smiling when they switched topics. Rio couldn’t help but replay the moment in her mind. Someone keeping her company - was that her?

The thought made her heart race just a little faster.

As the show wrapped up and the credits rolled, Rio checked her phone once again.

Agatha had posted something else, another snap from behind the scenes after the show ended. It was a quick, candid shot of Agatha sitting in her dressing room, wiping off her makeup. Her hair was now a little messy from the show, her face relaxed and more natural than the glammed-up version from the talk show. She looked so… genuine.

Caption: And that’s a wrap. It was fun, but I’m so ready to crawl into bed with Remi

Rio smiled, feeling a warm connection even in these quiet moments. She’d been in that bed last night, had thoroughly enjoyed herself in that same bed.

She swiped to reply.

Rio: You looked incredible. Remis a lucky girl

Seconds later, Agatha’s reply came through.

Agatha: Thank you - I was a lucky girl last night so cant complain

Rio chuckled to herself, loving the playful, easy vibe they had.

She could not wait to be back in Agathas bed.

Chapter 17

The next few days felt like an emotional rollercoaster for Rio—each moment filled with a mixture of nervous anticipation and a lingering sense of excitement. She found herself checking her phone constantly, her eyes scanning for any new messages or snaps from Agatha. Sometimes it was a glimpse of her current set, a peek into the world Agatha inhabited—one that was so different from Rio’s own. Other times, it was something more personal, just Agatha at home in her element, sexy glasses and Remi included, that made Rio’s heart flutter. Each snap was like a thread slowly weaving them closer, connecting them in ways that made her feel both comforted and on edge at the same time.

But there was one thing that kept playing on repeat in Rio’s mind: When will they go out again?

She wasn’t the type to sit back and wait around for things to happen. Usually, when she liked someone, she went for it, took the lead. But with Agatha, there was this subtle tension. Things were building between them, and Rio couldn’t help how much she wanted this thing between them to grow and deepen. And yet, despite that, there was a nagging uncertainty in the pit of her stomach. Was it too soon to ask to see her again? Would she put Agatha off? Would Agatha realise that Rio was not worthy of being with her?

The thought of waiting for Agatha to make the next move though felt unbearable. She had to take control, had to make it happen. She couldn’t risk losing this connection. She wasn’t going to sit idly by, second-guessing herself any longer.

That evening, after a long day spent tending to flowers and customers at the shop, Rio slumped onto her couch, exhaustion washing over her. But as soon as she picked up her phone, the thought of Agatha sparked a fresh wave of energy.

She scrolled through their past conversations—texts filled with shared jokes, hints of deeper connections, and moments of unspoken understanding. Her thumb hovered over the screen, her heart racing with the thought of what was to come.

Just send it, she told herself, taking a deep breath. The butterflies were back, swirling in her stomach, making her fingers tremble slightly. She wasn’t usually the kind to second-guess herself, but this felt different. She could almost hear the voice of doubt whispering in her ear, What if she had her weekend of fun and now doesn’t care? What if she’s not interested in seeing me again?

But Rio shook it off. She had to push past the anxiety.

Her fingers flew over the keys as she typed:

Rio: So, I was thinking... how about a date tomorrow night? I take you out somewhere this time?

She stared at the message for a moment, unsure if it sounded too eager or too casual. She bit her lip, waiting for the voice of reason to chime in. When it didn’t, she pressed send before she could talk herself out of it.

The minutes stretched, each one longer than the last, as she stared at the screen, waiting for the familiar three little dots to appear, signaling Agatha’s response. Rio’s heart thudded in her chest. What if she says no?

Finally, her phone buzzed.

Snapchat notification.

Agatha: That sounds amazing. What do you have in mind?

Rio’s heart skipped a beat. It was like an immediate relief, a weight lifting off her shoulders. She wasn’t sure exactly what she wanted, but she had to make it special. This wasn’t just about doing something. It was about her being the one to make the effort this time.

Think, think, think she urged herself. Her eyes darted around the room, as if the right idea would just appear. Then it hit her.

Rio: I was thinking maybe a place that’s a bit less upscale, more cozy? I’ve heard of a great Thai restaurant. How does that sound?

She stared at the screen after hitting send, replaying her words in her mind. Was it too casual? Would she want something more fancy, like the restaurants she’d taken Rio? The self-doubt crept in, but she shook it off.

A few seconds later, Agatha’s reply lit up the screen.

Agatha: Thai sounds perfect. I’ll leave the rest to you. I trust your judgment

Rio exhaled in relief. That was easy. Maybe too easy. She allowed herself a small smile, feeling a bit more at ease. This felt right, like she could do this, like they were on the same wavelength. The pressure wasn’t overwhelming; it was just two people taking things one step at a time.

Rio: Alright, it’s a date. I’ll text you the details soon. Can’t wait to see you again

Agatha: Same here ❤️

As Rio read Agatha’s reply, a warmth spread through her chest. Same here. Those words made everything feel like it was moving in the right direction. Rio replayed the conversation in her mind, her thoughts spinning with excitement. This wasn’t just another date. This was her date.

She was in control, taking the lead, and Agatha was letting her. It felt empowering. But the butterflies wouldn’t stop. She couldn’t help but wonder, What if I mess it up?

The next morning, Rio did some research on the restaurant, making sure it had the right atmosphere. She wanted somewhere intimate, where they could talk without feeling rushed or distracted by the noise of a crowded room. It needed to be perfect—a place where they could just relax and enjoy each other’s company. It wasn’t about impressing her; it was about making it feel natural.

Rio: 7 PM good for you? I’ll pick you up. Can’t wait to see you

Agatha: Perfect. Send me your Reg and I’ll get you added to the gates. I’ll be ready. See you then, beautiful

Rio’s breath hitched as she read the message. Beautiful. The word hung in the air, sending a flush of warmth through her body. Beautiful. Agatha Harkness thought she was beautiful.

She spent the next few hours getting ready, trying to look as effortlessly beautiful as her date surely would. She slipped into a green dress—one that hugged her body just right—and spent extra time on her makeup, making sure it was subtle yet polished. Not too much. Not too little. Just enough. She wasn’t sure if she was trying to impress Agatha or herself, but either way, she wanted to feel confident when she saw her.

“Wow, you look amazing,” Rio said, unable to keep the admiration from her voice. She could feel her cheeks flush as she took in the sight of Agatha.

Agatha’s lips curved into a playful grin. “You’re not so bad yourself.” She stepped forward, closing the distance between them, and before Rio could process it, Agatha kissed her lightly on the lips. The soft pressure sent a thrill through her, and she pulled away, breathless.

“Shall we go?” Agatha asked, her hand brushing against Rio’s.

Rio smiled, wide and genuine, as she opened the passenger door for Agatha. Her nerves were still there, swirling in her stomach, but they felt different now. They weren’t about fear; they were about excitement. The anticipation of what was to come. She ran around to the driver’s side, still trying to contain her excitement as they drove off, both of them carrying the unspoken promise of something special ahead.

The evening had been everything Rio had hoped for. The cozy, dimly lit Thai restaurant had been the perfect setting—soft, intimate, and filled with the rich scents of lemongrass and garlic. They shared plates of green curry and other dishes, their conversation flowing easily between laughter and thoughtful silences. Rio had never felt more at ease. Her heart had raced with excitement each time Agatha smiled at her, each time their fingers brushed, the connection between them undeniable.

At the end of the meal, they stepped outside, hands naturally intertwining, walking together under the soft glow of the streetlights. Rio’s heart was light, full of the quiet joy of being with someone who felt right in all the ways she hadn’t expected. Everything felt perfect. But as they approached the car, that perfect moment was shattered.

A burst of camera flashes, followed by the harsh clicking of lenses, stopped Rio in her tracks. She froze, her stomach dropping as she realized what was happening. Paparazzi. She hadn’t considered the fact that less upscale meant more accessible, more chance of them being spotted.

The air around them seemed to grow thick, as if the world had suddenly spun out of control. Rio’s face flushed a deep crimson as the camera flashes assaulted her from all directions. Her heart pounded in her chest, and she instinctively pulled away from Agatha, her mind scrambling, missing the slight hurt that passed over Agathas face.

What do I do?

The questions came too quickly, too loudly. “Who’s she?” “Is this a girlfriend?” “How serious is this?”

Her hands trembled as she tried to make sense of the chaos. The public eye. She hadn’t thought about it. She hadn’t prepared herself for this. Agatha was a star, but Rio was just a regular person, someone who had never been in the spotlight like this. They’d avoided this on all of their previous dates.

The constant flashes, the way the questions felt invasive, it was overwhelming.

Agatha, however, appeared unfazed. She stood next to Rio, calm as ever, her posture relaxed despite the sudden storm of attention. She squeezed Rio’s hand gently, looking over at her with a soft, reassuring smile.

“Hey, don’t worry. Just keep waking,” Agatha said, her voice steady, like this was something she did every day. Her words, calm and patient, should have reassured Rio, but instead, they made her feel even more lost. She hadn’t thought of how accustomed Agatha was to this. To all of this.

Rio’s gaze flickered between Agatha and the paparazzi. She felt like she was suffocating, caught between the bright lights and the weight of expectation.

This isn’t what I signed up for, she thought, her chest tightening with panic. This is her world, not mine. Oh god why did I think this was a good idea?

The flashes continued, blinding, unrelenting. The constant barrage of questions felt like they were pushing her further away from Agatha, and the longer she stood there, the more disconnected she felt. She wanted to escape. She wanted to disappear. Her mind raced with worry.

How can we be normal if this is what happens every time we go out?*

Agatha turned slightly, addressing the photographers with a practiced, almost rehearsed smile, brushing off their questions like she was used to this kind of attention. Rio watched her, heart sinking as Agatha effortlessly handled the chaos, her calm demeanor only highlighting just how much Rio was struggling.

“Are you okay?” Agatha’s voice broke through Rio’s spiraling thoughts, gentle and concerned.

Rio blinked rapidly, trying to pull herself together, but the flood of emotions hit her all at once. She wanted to say she was fine, to tell Agatha that it didn’t bother her, that she could handle it. But the truth was, she didn’t know if she could. The intensity of it all was overwhelming, and she could feel the pressure building inside her.

“I… I don’t know,” Rio admitted, her voice small, shaky. “I didn’t think it would be like this. I didn’t know how much this... all this attention would affect me.”

Agatha’s expression softened, and for the first time, Rio noticed a crack in her calm exterior. Agatha shifted closer, squeezing her hand with a hint of nervousness. She’s worried, Rio realized, a pang of guilt twisting in her stomach. She hadn’t thought about how this might affect Agatha.

It wasn’t just Rio who was caught in the storm; Agatha had to deal with it every day.

Agatha took a deep breath, her gaze flicking back to the photographers for a moment before focusing back on Rio. “I get it. I’m sorry you didn’t know how bad it could get. I didn’t think it would be like this for you, but it’s… part of the job. It comes with being in the public eye. I’ve been doing this for so long, and I’ve never really thought about how it might affect someone else... someone I care about,” she admitted, her voice softer now. “But if you’re with me, you’ll have to deal with this. It’s always going to be a part of my life.”

Rio’s heart skipped at the quiet vulnerability in Agatha’s voice. She could see it now—the strain that Agatha was hiding behind that practiced smile, the way her hand tightened around Rio’s, holding onto her as though she was frightened it would be the last time, the way her eyes searched Rio’s face for any sign of hesitation.

She swallowed hard, trying to find the right words, but her mind was a jumble of conflicting emotions. I want to be with her. I’m down bad for her already. I like her so much. But this... this world is so overwhelming. I’m not sure I can handle it.

“I... I didn’t realize how hard it would be,” Rio said finally, her voice barely above a whisper. She felt so out of place in that moment, her uncertainty hanging heavy between them, her anxiety taking over. “I didn’t think it would feel so... suffocating. I don’t know if I can handle being in the spotlight like this. I don’t know if I can be a part of this.”

Agatha’s face tightened as she attempted to hide her hurt, the smile slipping from her lips as her eyes darkened slightly. Rio could see the worry creeping in, the fear that this was too much for Rio, that all of this attention would drive them apart. Agatha’s shoulders slumped just a little, as if the weight of Rio’s uncertainty had taken something from her.

“I never wanted to put this on you,” Agatha said quietly, her voice almost brittle. “I never wanted you to feel like you have to deal with this just because you’re with me. But if you’re going to be with me, this is part of it. As much as I wish it was different. And I understand if it’s too much. I won’t push you if you’re not ready for it.”

Rio’s heart tightened. The last thing she wanted was to hurt Agatha, to make her think she couldn’t handle it. I want to be with her, Rio thought. But can I really keep up with this? Can I handle this kind of pressure, the constant scrutiny?

She took a deep breath, trying to steady her nerves, her fingers still tangled with Agatha’s. “I don’t want to walk away, Agatha. I really don’t. I just need time to figure out how to... how to deal with this. I want to be with you, but I’m not sure I can be okay with the cameras, the flashing lights. I’m not sure I’m strong enough for this.”

Agatha’s eyes softened, and she gave a tight, almost nervous smile. “You don’t have to be strong, Rio. You don’t have to be okay with it right away. I’m just asking if you’re willing to try, to stick it out with me even if it’s hard sometimes.”

Rio looked at her, searching her face. There was so much vulnerability in Agatha’s eyes—so much uncertainty, just like Rio’s. For the first time, Rio saw Agatha’s fear of losing her, and it made her heart ache. Agatha’s scared, because she cares, Rio realized. She’s worried that I won’t be able to handle her world.

Finally, after a long pause, Rio nodded. “I’m willing to try,” she said softly, her voice steady despite the swirling emotions. “I’ll try. But I need you to understand that this won’t be easy for me. It’s a lot.”

Agatha exhaled in relief, the tension leaving her shoulders as she smiled at Rio, a mix of hope and gratitude in her eyes. “I understand. We’ll take it slow. I promise, I will do everything I can to protect you from it all as much as I can.”

Rio smiled back, her mind worried but her heart full. As they drove away, she knew that no matter how difficult the road ahead might be, being with Agatha felt worth it.

“I’m up for it.” Rio said, her voice steady now, a small but confident smile spreading across her face. “Let’s see where this goes.”

Agatha reached over and took Rio’s hand once more, giving it a gentle squeeze. The car pulled away from the flashing lights, and for the first time that night, Rio felt a sense of calm settle in her chest. Whatever was to come, she was ready to face it—with Agatha by her side.

The car glided through the streets, the sound of the engine almost drowned out by the hum of Rio’s thoughts. She still couldn’t quite believe everything that had happened—how quickly things had escalated from shy glances to being with Agatha in the same car, holding hands, the paparazzi still flashing in the distance as they drove away. It was all so surreal, but the feelings she had for Agatha were anything but.

Rio’s heart skipped, her breath catching as the kiss grew more passionate, more urgent, the world outside fading away. As they pulled apart, both of them breathing a little heavier, the flash of cameras lit up the car once more. The paparazzi had caught the kiss—a perfect shot of Agatha looking at Rio with the softest, most affectionate expression. It was as if the whole world could see the connection between them. A snapshot of love, or something close to it.

Agatha winced at the sound of the cameras clicking outside the window but didn’t let it faze her. She kept her gaze fixed on Rio, her expression both playful and sincere.

“Well, that will definitely make the press .” Agatha said with an apologetic grin, her hand still resting on Rio’s cheek. “You know, people will at least know we’re more than friends now.”

Rio’s heart fluttered at the mention of the word friends, she had no idea what they were yet, but she was ready to find out. But she also couldn’t shake the nervous excitement that crept up on her.

“I don’t mind if they think that,” Rio replied, her voice a little shaky from the kiss and the emotions swirling inside her.

Agatha’s eyes softened, and she took a deep breath. “Good, because I really don’t want us to be just friends or just dating, Rio.”

Rio blinked, unsure if she heard correctly. “Not friends or dating?” she repeated, her voice uncertain.

Agatha smiled, her thumb gently tracing the curve of Rio’s jaw. “Hmmmm. I want to be with you, Rio. I want you to come back to mine again with me tonight. And... I want to know if you’ll be my girlfriend.”

The words hung in the air, and Rio felt as if the ground had shifted beneath her feet. She had been so wrapped up in the whirlwind of their time together that she hadn’t even fully processed the idea that Agatha might feel this way about her. But hearing it out loud, seeing the sincerity in Agatha’s eyes, made it feel incredibly real.

Rio’s mind raced for a moment. Her heart was hammering in her chest as she looked at Agatha, taking in her soft smile and the vulnerability behind her words. There was no doubt that Agatha felt something real for her—something deeper than the rush of a few dates or a fleeting attraction. She could see it in her eyes, hear it in her voice.

“Agatha...” Rio whispered, her voice cracking slightly. “Yes. 100% yes. I want to be your girlfriend.”

The smile that spread across Agatha’s face was nothing short of joyous. It was a genuine smile, the kind that reached her eyes and made everything around them feel brighter. She leaned in again, kissing Rio more tenderly this time, her lips lingering as she whispered against them, “You just made me so happy.”

The car was filled with an intimacy that Rio had never experienced before—just the two of them, surrounded by the city lights, but in their own little world. Agatha pulled back, her eyes sparkling.

“I’m glad you said yes, Rio. Tonight’s just the beginning for us.” She rested her forehead against Rio’s for a moment, her hand still gently holding Rio’s, as if grounding them both in this moment of newfound connection.

The paparazzi had gotten their shot, but Agatha didn’t care. This wasn’t about them. This was about what they had, about the way Agatha’s words made Rio feel like she was exactly where she was supposed to be.

“So, you’re staying with me tonight, right” Agatha asked softly, her voice teasing but sincere.

Rio smiled, her heart full. “I’m staying.”

And with that, Rio drove them home, the night ahead filled with possibilities, new beginnings, new love, and the shared feeling that this was something they both wanted to explore, no matter what the paparazzi, or anyone else, might think.

Chapter 18

The next morning, Rio woke up to the faint scent of coffee and the distant hum of a blender. Sunlight filtered through the luxurious curtains of Agatha’s bedroom, casting a warm glow over the plush bedding. For a moment, she just lay there, staring at the ceiling, processing everything.

She was in Agathas house. In her bed again. After officially becoming her girlfriend.

A sleepy, satisfied smile stretched across Rio’s lips as last night replayed in her head. Agatha had been so sweet, so affectionate, they had stayed up late talking, curled up together on the couch, sharing soft kisses and whispered confessions. Agatha had insisted on making them both tea, and they had ended up watching bad reality TV until they had celebrated their new relationship in bed together.

And now, she was here, waking up in Agatha’s bed, in her home, knowing that last night wasn’t just a dream.

The sound of a Snapchat notification pulled Rio from her thoughts. Groggy but curious, she reached for her phone on the bedside table and opened the app.

Bucky had posted to his story.

She tapped on it, and immediately, a video popped up.

Bucky was in Agatha’s kitchen, sitting on the counter, grinning like an absolute menace. Agatha stood behind him, her hair still messy from sleep, wearing Rio’s hoodie that she’d had in her night bag, which somehow looked ridiculously good on her.

“Ladies and gentlemen,” Bucky said dramatically, zooming in on Agatha, who was busy pouring coffee into a mug. “I have an important announcement. Our beloved, once emotionally unavailable ice queen—”

“Bucky.” Agatha’s voice came out warningly, but the smile on her face betrayed her amusement.

“—has finally been tamed,” Bucky continued, dodging a dish towel Agatha threw at him. “She is now a taken woman.”

Agatha rolled her eyes but didn’t deny it. Instead, she took a sip of her coffee and muttered, “I hate you.”

Bucky grinned at the camera. “Anyway, congrats to Rio for pulling this off. Never thought I’d see the day.”

Rio groaned, her cheeks heating up. Oh my god. He was here. Downstairs.

Before she could even process the secondhand embarrassment, another notification popped up, this time from Agatha’s private Snapchat story.

She hesitated for only a second before tapping on it.

The first snap was a picture of her coffee mug, sitting beside another one.

Caption: Morning coffee for two. ☕️💜

The second snap was a boomerang, Agatha sitting on the couch, Remi midway climbing onto her lap while the fluffy dog wiggled excitedly.

Caption: She loves me now but will ditch me the minute Rio wakes up

The next snap was a Video, Agatha, still in Rio’s hoodie, giving the camera a sleepy but genuine smile.

“Yeah, okay. Bucky’s an ass, but he’s not wrong. I really like her."

The snap ended, and Rio just stared at her phone, feeling her heart do a ridiculous little flip.

She really liked her.

Rio didn’t even hesitate—she took a quick selfie, still wrapped in Agatha’s blankets, her hair slightly messy from sleep.

Caption: I like you too. 💜

Then, without overthinking it, she sent it directly to Agatha.

A moment later, she heard soft footsteps approaching the bedroom, and when she looked up, Agatha was standing in the doorway, holding two mugs of coffee—one for each of them.

“Good morning, sweetheart,” Agatha murmured, her lips curving into a soft smile as she walked over and sat on the edge of the bed, handing Rio her mug.

Rio took it, feeling a warmth spread through her chest that had nothing to do with the coffee.

“Morning,” she replied, biting her lip to stop herself from smiling too hard. “Is Bucky still here?”

“No, I sent him home,” Agatha leaned in, pressing a slow, lingering kiss to Rio’s lips before whispering against them:

“Get used to waking up here because I’m not letting you go.”

And just like that, Rio knew she was in way too deep.

By the time Rio got home later that afternoon, she could tell something was off.

Her phone had been vibrating nonstop, Snapchat notifications, Instagram requests, texts from numbers she didn’t recognise.

She had brushed it off at first, assuming it was just a little extra attention because of the paparazzi photos from last night.

But then she opened Instagram.

Her follower count had tripled.

Her DMs were a mess—messages from old school friends, exes, distant relatives she hadn’t spoken to in years. The kind of people who had never really cared before but were suddenly very interested in her life now.

One particular message made her stomach drop.

Lisa (Ex-Girlfriend, 2019):
Damn, Rio, you really went for someone famous, huh? Didn’t take you for a clout chaser lol. Hope you’re good though! It would be good to meet up soon!

Sophie (Ex-Girlfriend, 2021):
Hey. Didn’t expect to see your face on a gossip site, lol. Crazy. We should catch up, I miss you

Megan (Old High School Friend):
OMG RIOOO WTF. YOU’RE DATING AGATHA HARKNESS? TEXT ME BACK NOW. I NEED DETAILS

Rio groaned and locked her phone, tossing it onto her bed like it had personally offended her.

She had expected some attention—but this? This felt invasive.

She flopped onto her bed, rubbing her face. She didn’t ask for this. She just liked Agatha. She wasn’t trying to be some celebrity girlfriend or make headlines.

Her phone buzzed again. This time, it was a Snapchat from Agatha.

Agatha: I’m guessing by the radio silence that you’ve checked your phone. You okay?

Rio exhaled, sitting up and grabbing her phone again. She hesitated for a second before responding.

Rio: I’m fine. Just a little… overwhelmed

Agatha read it almost immediately.

Agatha: Yeah, I figured. It’s gonna be weird for a bit. But just so you know—you don’t owe anyone a response

Rio smiled a little. She knew that. But hearing it from Agatha made it easier to believe.

A second later, another message popped up.

Agatha: Come back to mine. I’ll cook for you.

Rio: That’s a dangerous offer. You did mention you set off your smoke alarm making toast once

Agatha: Okay, Bucky set off the smoke alarm, not me. And I actually CAN cook. You’ll see

Rio hesitated for only a moment before typing back:

Rio: I’m on my way

Whatever was waiting for her on social media could wait. Right now she just wanted to see Agatha.

Rio threw on a comfy sweater and jeans, grabbed her keys, and was out the door within minutes. The second she slid into her car, she felt relief, leaving behind the buzzing phone which was thrown in her bag, the flood of DMs, the overwhelming weight of sudden public attention.

The drive to Agatha’s was familiar after only driving back a few hours ago. She knew the turns, the landmarks, the moment when her GPS would tell her to take the private road leading into Agatha’s gated community. The security recognised her, waving her through without a second thought.

By the time she pulled into the driveway, some of the tension in her shoulders had eased.

She barely had time to ring the doorbell before the door swung open, revealing Agatha in sweatpants and a fitted long-sleeve top, barefoot, a lazy smile on her lips.

“You made it, sweetheart,” Agatha said, her voice warm and teasing as she pulled Rio inside. The moment the door shut behind them, Agatha wrapped her arms around Rio’s waist, holding her close.

Rio exhaled, melting into the hug.

“I needed to see you,” she admitted, voice muffled against Agatha’s shoulder.

Agatha pressed a kiss to her temple, her hold tightening just a fraction. “Yeah, I figured.”

She pulled back, studying Rio’s face. “It’s a lot, huh?”

Rio let out a breathy laugh.“Understatement of the year.”

Agatha reached up, tucking a strand of hair behind Rio’s ear. “You’re handling it better than I did my first time seeing my name in the tabloids.”

Rio lifted an eyebrow. “What did you do?”

Agatha grinned. “Cried in my trailer for an hour, got drunk with Bucky, and threatened to delete all my socials.”

That pulled a genuine laugh from Rio, and Agatha’s eyes softened at the sound.

“Come on,” Agatha said, taking Rio’s hand and leading her toward the kitchen. “I promised you food, didn’t I?”

When Rio stepped into the kitchen, she immediately noticed three things:

1. There was flour on the counter
2. A bottle of wine was already open
3. The smoke alarm was… conspicuously missing from the ceiling

Rio narrowed her eyes. “Agatha. Where’s your smoke detector?”

Agatha didn’t even blink. “Temporarily removed for my own sanity.”

“Why?”

“Because,” Agatha said, stepping around the counter and dramatically gesturing to a pan on the stove, “it was being a little bitch about me making homemade pasta.”

Rio stared at her. “The smoke detector objected to pasta?”

Agatha pointed accusingly at the stove. “Okay, it wasn’t just the pasta. There was also an incident with the garlic bread.”

Rio folded her arms. “What kind of incident?”

“…It may have been slightly on fire.”

Rio blinked. “You set bread on fire?”

“I fixed it!” Agatha insisted. “And we have a perfectly good pasta dish now. So I think I deserve some credit.”

Rio bit back a smile. “I’ll be the judge of that.”

Agatha smirked, reaching for the wine bottle and pouring them both a glass. “Fair enough. But if you hate it, you’re still stuck with me for the night, so you better pretend to love it.”

“Oh, I’m staying the night again?” Rio teased, taking her wine glass.

Agatha leaned in, her voice low and amused.

“Sweetheart, if you think I’m letting you go back home, stressed , after driving here and back once already, you’re out of your mind.”

Rio’s heart stuttered in her chest, but she just took a slow sip of her wine and smirked.

“Alright,” she said. “Let’s eat.”

Dinner was chaotic, mostly because Agatha kept making Rio laugh, spilling more about her past disastrous cooking attempts and how Bucky had once banned her from using the oven for a month.

The pasta? Surprisingly decent.

After dinner, they curled up on Agatha’s ridiculously comfy couch, Remi stretched out over both their laps, watching some old movie Agatha had put on for ‘aesthetic purposes’ but was clearly half-watching at best.

At some point, Rio’s phone buzzed again.

She glanced at it, saw more notifications from Instagram, Snapchat, and old contacts trying to reach out, and sighed.

Agatha, who had been playing with Rio’s fingers absentmindedly, noticed. “Want me to toss your phone in the pool?”

Rio laughed, but something about the offer was tempting.

Instead, she turned her phone off completely and placed it on the coffee table. “There. No more distractions.”

Agatha grinned, pulling Rio closer. “Good. Because I was about to demand your full attention.”

“Oh yeah?” Rio murmured, smirking as she turned to face her.

Agatha tilted her head, her eyes dark and playful. “Mhm. I think my girlfriend deserves a proper distraction after the day she’s had.”

And then she leaned in, capturing Rio’s lips in a slow, deep kiss, wiping away every single thought except for this.

Chapter 19

Rio had never been so aware of her phone before. It sat face-up on her kitchen counter, buzzing relentlessly like a bomb about to detonate. She hadn’t even looked at her notifications yet. She couldn’t.

Her stomach was in knots.

Instead, she paced the kitchen, clutching a mug of tea she had no intention of drinking, replaying the last few days over and over in her mind.

Her time at Agathas house, hiding from the world.

The paparazzi.

The pictures of them kissing in the car.

It was all out there now.

And judging by the sheer volume of her notifications, everyone had seen it.

Rio took a deep breath, forced herself to grab her phone, and opened Instagram first.

Her follower count had exploded, not just by a few hundred, but by thousands. How had they all even found her!

Then she checked her DMs.

It was worse than she’d imagined.

Her inbox was a war zone.

Some messages were sweet, fans of Agathas gushing over how cute she and Agatha looked together.

Some were jealous, mostly from people who had convinced themselves that they were supposed to be dating Agatha instead.

And then there were the worst ones. More exes had reached out.

Serena (a one night mistake from four years ago): Wow. Didn’t expect to see you in the tabloids, lol. So… guess you’re too famous to catch up now?

Lena (a toxic disaster of a relationship): Oh, so you’re dating Agatha Harkness now? Wow, Rio. You always did like attention.

Elle (nice, but extremely clingy colleage fling): Hey! Crazy seeing you on my feed. I was actually thinking about you the other day… maybe we should talk?

Rio groaned, chucking her phone onto the couch like it had personally offended her.

This was a lot. She was just a florist.She wasn’t built for this. Before she could spiral any further, her phone buzzed again. This time, it was a Snapchat notification.

Not from the public chaos—this was from Agatha’s Snapchat.

She was met with a photo of Agatha, sprawled on her couch, wearing an oversized hoodie and eating cereal straight from the box. The caption?

Rio, are you alive? Did you die from notification overload? Blink twice if you need me to sue someone.

Rio snorted, some of the tension finally breaking.

Then another direct snap came through. A video this time.

Agatha, still in her hoodie, looking far too pleased with herself.

“Bucky and I are currently taking bets on how long it’ll take before you lose your mind and break your phone. I said by noon. Bucky said by now. If I win, he has to cook dinner for a week. If he wins, I have to let him DJ my next house party. Please, Rio. For the love of God, don’t make me suffer through his tragic taste in music.”

Rio shook her head, laughing despite herself. But before she could reply, another snap from Agatha came through.

This time, it was just a screenshot of her Instagram comments.

Specifically, the comment from another ex.

And then came Agatha’s next snap—a close-up of her unimpressed face, captioned:

Caption: EXCUSE ME???????

Rio choked on air.

Then the next one, Agatha, dramatically laying across her kitchen counter, looking like she was in emotional distress.

Caption: Your exes suddenly coming out of the woodwork like cockroaches. 🚨🚨🚨

Then, finally, one last snap.

A video of Bucky reading the comments out loud while Agatha looked fuming, absolutely howling with laughter.

“Ohhhh, this is RICH. ‘Didn’t expect to see you in the tabloids, we should catch up!”

Rio groaned, covering her face with her hands. Why was this her life now?

Finally, she grabbed her phone, typing out a quick response.

Rio: PLEASE stop reading my comments I’m already dying.

Agatha responded immediately with another snap, a picture of Remi sleeping on her lap.

Caption: Don’t worry, Rio. Your mine now, even if your exes are thirsting after you ❤️

Rio froze. Her heart did a weird thing in her chest.

Then, before she could overthink it, she sent back a selfie, her face buried in a pillow, only her eyes peeking out.

Rio: How are you handling this so well?? I feel like I’m having an identity crisis.

It took Agatha a minute to respond, but when she did, it was another video.

She was sitting cross-legged on her couch, looking soft, relaxed, and… kind.

“I’ve been dealing with this for years, sweetheart. I promise, it gets easier.”

Rio bit her lip, staring at the screen. Then Agatha added, “But if it ever gets too much, you tell me, okay? You come first. Not the tabloids. Not the fans. Just you. I can have my manager put some blockers out”

Rio swallowed hard, warmth blooming in her chest.

How was Agatha Harkness real and how did she get so lucky?

She hesitated, then typed:

Rio: What if I’m just being dramatic?

Agatha responded almost instantly.

Agatha: You’re not. This is a LOT. And I know you didn’t sign up for it. But I’m here. We’ll figure it out together, okay?

Rio exhaled, some of the panic finally easing.

Maybe… just maybe… she could handle this.

That evening, Rio was still reeling from all of the attention when her phone lit up.

Snapchat notification.

This time, it was a photo of Agatha’s feet up on her coffee table, a glass of wine in her hand, and Remi sprawled over her lap like a spoiled prince.

Caption: You should come over. Let’s hide from the world together.

Rio’s stomach flipped. Come over? To her house? Again?

She had only been home for two days and the idea of being around Agatha again, alone, in her gorgeous house, was both exciting and terrifying. Terrifying because she could easily get used to it.

And then another Snap arrived.

A video this time. Agatha, tilting the camera up from her wine glass, giving Rio a knowing smirk.

“Bucky’s here too. He says you’re not real until he sees you in person. So. You gonna prove your existence, sweetheart?”

Rio groaned, burying her face in her hands.

But then she peeked out, bit her lip, and responded with a Snap of her car keys in hand.

Caption: On my way. Tell Bucky to prepare himself

Forty-five minutes later, Rio was pulling up outside Agatha’s house.

She barely had time to take a deep breath before the front door swung open and Bucky Barnes himself was standing there, arms crossed, giving her a once-over.

“Hmm.”

Rio blinked. “Uh. Hi?”

Bucky squinted. “You’re real.”

“…I am.”

Bucky turned his head, yelling back into the house. “SHE’S REAL, AGATHA. YOU’VE NOT BEEN CATFISHED BY AI AFTER ALL.”

Rio choked on air as Agatha’s laughter rang out from inside.

“Oh my God,” Rio muttered, covering her face. “I should have stayed home.”

“Nah, you’re already here,” Bucky said, grinning as he stepped aside. “C’mon, let’s see if you can survive us both in person.”

Rio wasn’t sure she would.

But she stepped inside anyway.

Agatha was curled up on the couch in sweatpants and a loose sweater, hair a little messy, makeup smudged just enough to make her look ridiculously good without trying and her glasses. She was wearing her glasses.

Rio swallowed hard.

“How’s my favorite florist?” Agatha asked, smirking.

Rio raised a brow. “I’m your only florist.”

“Exactly,” Agatha said, patting the spot beside her. “Now get over here before Bucky starts grilling you about your childhood trauma.”

Bucky winked from the kitchen. “Oh, don’t worry. I’ll get to that later.”

Rio laughed, shaking her head as she sat down beside Agatha who immediately kissed her in greeting. Remi immediately throwing her two front legs across her lap, curling up like she owned her.

Agatha watched with a small, amused smile. “Yeah. You’re officially part of the household now.”

Rio leaned into the couch, relaxing. Maybe this… wasn’t so scary after all.

Rio had barely sat down before a glass of wine was being placed in her hand.

Agatha smirked, curling up against the arm of the couch, her legs casually draped over Rio’s lap next to Remis like it was the most natural thing in the world.

Bucky, meanwhile, flopped onto the opposite end of the couch with a beer in hand and a dangerous glint in his eye.

“So,” he started, stretching his arm across the back of the couch and zeroing in on Rio like a shark sensing fresh blood. “I gotta say, you’re handling all this surprisingly well.”

Rio let out a breathless laugh, giving him a look. “Handling what?”

“You know,” Bucky gestured vaguely. “Dating a world-famous actress. Being thrown into the public eye overnight. Having deranged exes crawling out of the woodwork like a zombie movie.”

Agatha groaned, tossing a throw pillow at him. “Can you not?”

“What?” Bucky caught it effortlessly. “I’m just saying. Most people would be losing their minds right now.”

“Oh, don’t worry,” Rio said dryly, taking a very necessary sip of wine. “I had a full-blown panic attack this morning. It was great.”

Agatha nudged her knee gently. “I told you I’d handle it, sweetheart if needed.”

Bucky snorted. “And you did. By roasting her exes.”

Rio laughed. “Honestly? That helped.”

Agatha smirked. “See? My methods are flawless.”

Bucky rolled his eyes. “Sure, sure. Anyway.” He leaned forward, resting his elbows on his knees. “I need to do a very important check before I can fully accept you into this little dysfunctional family.”

Rio raised a brow. “Oh?”

Agatha groaned, covering her face. “Don’t.”

Bucky ignored her. “Rio. Favorite horror movie. Go.”

Rio perked up instantly. “That’s easy. *The Thing 1982, obviously.”

Bucky lit up. “Solid choice. Good taste.”

“I know.” Rio smirked. “Your turn.”

“Alien.” Bucky took a sip of his beer. “Moss Weaver? A goddess.”

“Fair,” Rio admitted. Then, because she couldn’t resist, she turned to Agatha. “And yours?”

Agatha side-eyed both of them, clearly unamused. “Casper.”

Rio and Bucky both stared at her.

“…Casper?” Rio repeated.

Bucky was already cackling.

“Oh, shut up,” Agatha huffed, snatching Rio’s wine and taking a sip like she deserved it. “It’s a classic.”

Rio was grinning too hard. “Agatha. That is not a horror movie.”

“It has ghosts.”

“It’s a kids' movie,” Bucky laughed. “Were you traumatized by a cartoon, Aggie?”

“I was five!”

Rio leaned into Agatha’s side, mock-consoling her. “It’s okay. The ghosts can’t hurt you anymore.”

Bucky wiped a fake tear away. “Our big, bad, Hollywood icon… defeated by Casper.”

Agatha let out a dramatic sigh, shaking her head. “I hate both of you.”

Over the next hour, the three of them somehow ended up trading embarrassing stories, half-empty wine glasses and beer bottles scattered around the coffee table.

Bucky went first—recounting the time he accidentally slid into the DMs of his childhood crush, only to realize he had no idea who he was and thought he was a scam bot.

Rio nearly cried laughing.

Then Agatha, reluctantly, told the story of how she once tripped on her own gown at a red carpet event and dragged an entire set piece down with her.

Rio, who had actually seen the video of that moment resurface online a few months ago, was in tears.

Finally, they turned to Rio.

“Alright, florist girl,” Bucky grinned, stretching. “Your turn. What’s the most embarrassing thing you’ve ever done?”

Rio groaned, face heating up. “God, there’s too many.”

Agatha smirked. “Oh, come on. Spill.”

Rio buried her face in her hands. “Okay. Fine. One time, I, uh… accidentally texted my boss ‘I love you’ instead of ‘thank you’.”

“Nooo,” Agatha wheezed, clutching her stomach. “Oh my God, did they say anything?”

Rio groaned. “Immediately replied with ‘appreciate it, but I’m married.’”

Bucky nearly fell off the couch.

Agatha, tears in her eyes, clutched Rio’s arm. “You—are my favorite person. Seriously.”

Rio grinned, warmth blooming in her chest. She had been so nervous about this. About meeting Bucky. About stepping even further into Agatha’s world.

But now?

Sitting here, laughing until her sides ached, Agatha’s hand resting casually on her thigh, Bucky cracking jokes at their expense—

It felt natural.

Like she was meant to be here.

As the night wound down, Agatha stretched dramatically, then pulled out her phone.

“I should warn you,” she mused, “Bucky documents everything*”

“You’re one to talk,” Bucky shot back, already typing.

Snapchat notification. BuckyBarnes added to his story.

Rio opened it instantly.

The first post? A selfie of him looking exhausted, with Rio and Agatha laughing in the background.

Caption: Trapped in third wheel hell. Pray for me.

The second? A blurry photo of Agatha, mid-sentence, gesturing wildly.

Caption: She’s talking about Shakespeare, I am perishing.

The third? A video of Remi now curled up between Rio and Agatha.

Caption: The dog has chosen its new mom It’s over for all of you

Rio snorted, nudging Agatha. “You let him do this?”

Agatha smirked. “He’s annoying, but he’s my annoying.”

Bucky grinned. “And now, by extension, your problem too.”

Rio sighed, but there was no real complaint behind it.

Honestly? She didn’t mind. At all.

Chapter 20

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

It had been a relatively peaceful few weeks since Rio’s name first hit the tabloids.

Thanks to Agatha’s legal team of doom, the reporters and paparazzi who had been swarming her little flower shop in the beginning had been swiftly dealt with. No more camera flashes through the window, no more invasive questions when she tried to make deliveries, no more strangers lurking outside like they were waiting for her to slip up and say something scandalous.

Now, the only thing she had to worry about was not accidentally cutting herself while trimming rose stems.

Which was good, because lately, her mind was occupied with only one thing—Agatha.

She caught herself smiling at nothing at least five times a day. Sometimes more. It was ridiculous, really.

It wasn’t just the fact that she was dating the Agatha Harkness —a world-famous actress, Hollywood’s golden girl, a literal dream to millions. Yeah, that part was surreal. And, okay, maybe a little bit of an ego boost.

But more than that, it was her.

It was the way Agatha still sent her snaps of Remi, her spoiled greyhound, dramatically demanding treats. The way she’d send texts like, ‘Saw this flower today, thought of you’, followed by some blurry photo of a random bloom she’d spotted on set.

It was the way Agatha made Rio feel seen.

Wanted. Cherished.

She was falling. No—she had already fallen. And that was terrifying. Sure she had loved Agatha as an idea, as a fantasy, but now she LOVED her.

Before she could spiral too hard about it, the front bell chimed, signaling a customer.

She turned, a polite smile already forming—only to freeze when she saw who was standing in the doorway.

Her stomach dropped.

“Oh, hell no.”

Natasha.

Her ex.

Natasha had always been the worst kind of ex—the kind who still acted like she had a claim on Rio, despite being the one who had cheated on her.

And now, after years of radio silence, she had the audacity to just show up?

Now?

When Rio’s name had just hit the press and Natasha was a wannabe instafluer?

Yeah. Not subtle.

Rio exhaled sharply, crossing her arms. “What are you doing here, Natasha?”

Natasha grinned, all fake charm and calculated ease, like she was already enjoying whatever twisted game she was playing. “What? Can’t a girl visit an old friend?”

Rio didn’t blink. “We’re not friends.”

Nat clicked her tongue, stepping further inside. “Damn. Fame’s changed you already, huh?”

Oh, she wanted to deck her.

Instead, she took a deep breath and glared. “I don’t have time for this.”

Nat, unfazed, shrugged dramatically. “Look, I just wanted to talk. Maybe grab coffee, catch up—”

And then, before Rio could react, she leaned in like she was about to kiss her.

Like she thought she could just waltz back in, pull some dramatic stunt, and get her face in the tabloids.

Rio’s entire body reacted on instinct.

She stepped back fast, grabbing the nearest thing within reach—a spray bottle she used to mist delicate flowers—

And sprayed her right in the face.

“WHAT THE—” Nat stumbled back, spluttering.

Rio didn’t lower the bottle. “Are you kidding me?” she snapped. “You thought you could just show up here and kiss me?”

Nat wiped her face, looking absolutely offended. “Jesus, Rio, you used to enjoy it.”

“Oh, screw you.”

Nat held up her hands. “Alright, alright, no need to—”

“Get. Out.”

There must have been something in her voice, something cold, something final, because Nat’s smirk dropped.

Rio had always been the nice one. Always let things slide. Always gave people too much leeway.

Not today.

Not when she had something worth protecting.

Natasha exhaled sharply, shaking her head. “Fine. Whatever. I’ll see you around, superstar.”

And with that, she turned on her heel and walked out, probably off to brag about this little interaction to her followers.

Rio exhaled, her grip loosening on the spray bottle. Her hands were still shaking, not from fear, just pure, pissed-off adrenaline.

And then, her phone buzzed.

A Snapchat notification.

Rio’s frustration ebbed as she pulled it out of her pocket, already smiling when she saw the name on the screen.

Agatha.

It was a photo. Agatha was sitting in a makeup chair, her hair halfway done, holding up her script with a dramatic, suffering expression while a stylist worked around her.

Caption: Another 14-hour day, send help (or snacks or your body)

Rio huffed out a laugh, shaking her head.

Without thinking, she snapped a photo of her own face, rolling her eyes dramatically.

Caption: Imagine being this dramatic about your literal dream job.

Agatha’s reply was instant.

Agatha: Imagine having zero sympathy for your incredibly sexy girlfriend.

Rio bit her lip, warmth pooling in her chest.

She tapped out a quick response.

Rio: Imagine knowing you’re sexy and using it against me.

Agatha: Sweetheart, I don’t have to use anything against you. You’re already weak for me.

Rio groaned, pressing a hand to her face.
Rio: Shut up.

Agatha: Make me.

God, she was insufferable. And sexy. And turning Rio on with just her teasing.

Rio: Okay. I’m never kissing you again. There. You’re made

Agatha: Oh no. How will I survive. I am so devastated. So very heartbroken

Rio snorted. You’re the worst.

Agatha: *And yet, you love it

Her heart stopped. She stared at the words, pulse hammering in her throat. She did love it. She loved her.

Agatha sent another message before she could panic.

Agatha: Just saying. You’re kinda obvious

Rio exhaled, staring at the screen.

And then, before she could second-guess herself, she typed back.

Rio: Yeah. I do love it

Agatha’s response came almost immediately.

Agatha: Good. Because I love it too

Rio’s chest ached. In the best possible way.
She bit her lip, smiling down at her phone.

Yeah. Natasha was a distant memory.

Rio stared at her phone, Agatha’s words glowing on the screen like a tiny sun.

Good. Because I love it too.

Her breath caught in her throat. That was so close to the words she actually wanted to say and hear.

She knew Agatha was playful, always toeing the line between teasing and serious, but this—this didn’t feel like a joke.

She reread the message about five times, heart hammering against her ribs like it wanted out.

Agatha loved it too. Loved her maybe?

She was in love with Agatha. She’d known it for a while now, had felt it in the way her chest ached when they were apart, in the way she craved the sound of her voice, the warmth of her laugh.

In the way she needed Agatha, not in a desperate, unhealthy obsessive way, but in a way that felt like natural. Like something essential.

But she hadn’t said it yet. Hadn’t let the words slip free. Not out of fear that it wasn’t true—God, she knew it was true. No, it was something else, something harder to explain.

She’d never been anyone’s first choice before. Never been loved in the way Agatha made her feel loved.

Natasha had never looked at her like she was it. Had never made her feel safe enough to say those words without worrying they’d be thrown back in her face later, twisted into something ugly.

But Agatha— Agatha was different.

She told Rio she was beautiful when she was covered in dirt from working in her shop all day, sent her sleepy voice notes when she was sleeping at her own home as soon as she woke up just to say good morning. She made Rio feel like she was the most important person in her orbit, like she wasn’t just another passing thing, but something she wanted to hold onto.

And God, Rio wanted to say it.

Wanted to tell her yes, I’m in love with you, wanted to hear Agatha say it to her, just to be sure she hadn’t imagined the connection they had.

But now, sitting in the quiet of her flower shop, hands still unsteady from the confrontation with Nat, she hesitated.

Because if she said it, it was real.

And real things could break.

Her phone buzzed again.

Agatha: Rio? Did I just freak you out? You can pretend I didn’t say that if you want

Rio’s heart squeezed.

She could picture Agatha now—biting her lip, second-guessing herself, probably wondering if she’d triggered Rios ability to spiral.

She hated that she’d made her wait even this long. So before she could talk herself out of it, she started typing.

Rio: You didn’t freak me out

Agatha’s reply was immediate.

Agatha: Good, I mean it you know

A pause.

Rio: Prove it to me - your place tonight?

Agatha: Your cooking then 😘

Rio exhaled, a smile tugging at her lips. Yeah. That wasn’t too heavy, but soon, soon she would tell her.
