Chapter 21

Rio sent a snapchat of her face, pouting and eyes fluttering.

Caption: Pretty please can you meet Agatha?

Rio fidgeted with her phone, watching the little typing bubble appear and disappear as Alice debated her answer.

Finally, a message popped up.

Alice: Okay. But if she’s weird or scary in real life, I’m running.

Rio: You’re weird and scary in real life.

Alice: Yeah, but I’m FUN weird and scary.

Rio: Fair point

Alice was trying to sound casual, but Rio knew her best friend. She was freaking out.

Which was hilarious because Alice had never been intimidated by anyone in her entire life.

She’d once flipped off a fellow police officer who cut her in line for coffee. She had personally told off multiple people for being rude to a baristas. She was fearless.

But now?

She was nervous about meeting Agatha.

Which was even funnier because, unbeknownst to Alice, Agatha was nervous too.

Agatha: Are you sure she wont hate me?

Rio snorted, texting back.

Rio: Why would she hate you?

Agatha: Because I’m famous and dating you, and she’s your ride-or-die best friend. Best friends always hate the new person at first.

Rio: Bucky doesn’t hate me. She doesn’t hate you.

Agatha: Yes but he’s wired wrong. Yet - she doesnt hate me yet

Rio rolled her eyes.

Rio: I’m more worried about YOU hating HER, honestly. She has no filter

Agatha’s response was instant

Agatha: Oh, I know. I’m going through her Twitter right now

Rio froze.

Rio: YOUR WHAT?

Agatha: I have to make sure I’m not walking into a trap. Your best friend is feral.

Rio: YOUR SCROLLING ALICE’S TWITTER??

Agatha: It’s an experience.

Rio died inside. Alice’s Twitter was an unhinged wasteland.

No filter. No shame. Just pure chaos.

Rio: I’m afraid to ask what you’ve seen.

Agatha: She threatened to fight God over a canceled TV show.

Rio: That’s pretty normal

Agatha: She also said last year, and I quote, “If I ever meet Agatha Harkness in person, I’m either punching her in the face, making out with her or asking her for money.”

Rio choked on air.

Rio: OH MY GOD.

Agatha: So yeah, I think I have even more of a right to be nervous.

Rio facepalmed. This was going to be a disaster.

They picked a neutral location, a cozy little brunch spot where neither of them could cause too much damage.

Alice and Rio arrived first.

Agatha arrived a few minutes later, wearing sunglasses indoors like a criminal trying to avoid detection. Or a megastar not wanting to draw attention to herself.

Rio sighed when Agatha sat down in the booth they’d chosen. “You’re not in the mafia. Take those off.”

Agatha hesitated before dramatically removing them.

Alice, meanwhile, was just staring at her. Like she was studying an exotic animal in the wild.

“…You’re real,” Alice finally said.

Agatha arched an eyebrow. “Last time I checked.”

Alice narrowed her eyes. “You’re shorter than I thought you’d be.”

Agatha looked genuinely offended. “I’m five-five.”

“You give taller energy,” Alice shrugged. “It’s the personality.”

Agatha turned to Rio. “Is this her version of a compliment?”

Rio sipped her coffee. “Honestly? Yeah.”

Agatha sighed. “Great.”

Alice leaned in, squinting at Agatha like she was searching for a sign of weaknesses.

“So, tell me,” she said, steepling her fingers, “what are your intentions with my best friend?”

Rio groaned. “Alice, oh my god.”

But Agatha? Agatha just grinned.

“My intentions?” she repeated, tilting her head. “Long walks on the beach. Late-night conversations. Stealing her hoodies. Maybe someday we’ll get another dog.”

Alice’s eyes narrowed further. “Uh-huh.”

Agatha leaned forward, a spark of mischief in her eye. “Your turn. What are YOUR intentions with my girlfriend?”

Alice blinked, stunned at her cool facade being so easily disarmed. “What?”

“You’re very intense,” Agatha said seriously. “Should I be worried you’re planning a hostile takeover? Trying to win her for yourself?”

Alice snorted. “Ew, no. She steals the blankets.”

Agatha gasped. “She does! I tell her that all the time!”

Rio, who had been minding her business. suddenly found herself under attack.

“Okay, hold on—”

“Yeah” Alice confirmed, grinning. “Total menace. A sleep fiend.”

Agatha turned to Rio, betrayed. “I told you. You let me freeze in my own bed.”

“Oh my god, I—”

“She also talks in her sleep doesn’t she,” Alice added gleefully. “Once I heard her arguing with someone about sandwiches at three a.m.”

Agatha lit up. “What was her argument?”

Alice sipped her coffee. “She was pro-mayo.”

Agatha clutched her chest. “I knew I picked the right girl.”

Rio buried her face in her hands. “You two are the worst.”

By the time brunch ended, Agatha and Alice were practically best friends. Which, for Rio, was equal parts heartwarming and terrifying.

Alice made a dramatic show of pulling Rio aside before they left.

“I approve,” she declared. “But if she breaks your heart, I’m legally required to throw hands.”

Rio sighed. “I wouldn’t expect anything less.”

“And also,” Alice added, grinning wickedly, “she just told me how you call her ‘baby’ when your tired.”

Rio blanched. Agatha, from across the room, just winked.

They spent the rest of the evening curled up in bed, Rio half in Agatha’s lap, content with how the meeting between her best friend and who she was slowly beginning to think was the love of her life, went so well. She was mesmerised watching Agatha read her scripts with her glasses perched on the edge of her nose.

At some point, Agatha dozed off, her head resting against Rio’s shoulder.

It was peaceful. Perfect. Both tangled together sound asleep.

Until midnight hit.

And suddenly— BLARING MUSIC

Stevie Nicks, specifically.

The opening notes of Edge of Seventeen shattered the silence like a bomb going off.

Agatha, who had been fast asleep mere seconds ago, groaned loudly, dragging a pillow over her face.

“Oh no,” she mumbled into it.

Rio jolted up, alarmed. “What the hell?”

There was movement downstairs. A clatter. A shake of a cocktail shaker.

The unmistakable sound of a blender.

And Agatha, with the deep, tired sigh of someone who had seen this exact scenario too many times before, just muttered—“Mother.”

Rio blinked. “What?”

But before Agatha could answer, a woman’s voice rang out from downstairs—loud, delighted, and just a little bit tipsy.

“MIDNIGHT MARGARITAS, BABY!”

Agatha groaned. “I hate my life.”

Rio stared at her. “You’re telling me that at midnight, on a random weekday, your mother just... shows up and starts making margaritas like she’s in Practical Magic?”

Agatha didn’t even bother lifting her head. “Yes.”

“And you just... let it happen?”

Agatha sighed dramatically, finally peeling herself up from the bed.

“There’s no stopping Lilia,” she said grimly. “You can only hope to contain her.”

Rio, who had never met Agatha’s mother before, had only seen the snapchats on mothers day, was now deeply intrigued.

And slightly terrified.

They made their way downstairs, the sound of Stevie Nicks still shaking the walls.

And there, standing in the kitchen like some kind of tequila-wielding sorceress, was Lilia Calderou.

Agatha’s mother.

Wearing an expensive silk kimono, perfectly winged eyeliner despite the hour, and mixing margaritas like it was her full-time job.

She spotted them and grinned.

“Ah! The lovebirds have arrived!”

Agatha dragged a hand down her face.“Mother. It’s the middle of the night.”

“And?” Lilia said, completely unbothered, pouring margaritas into salt-rimmed glasses. “You think Stevie Nicks only works in daylight? Midnight margaritas, darling—it’s tradition.”

Rio - who had no idea what was happening but was loving every second of it - finally spoke up.

“You’re actually just like the movie.”

Lilia beamed. “Oh, sweetheart, I am the movie.”

Agatha, exhausted beyond belief, just grabbed a margarita and downed half of it in one go.

Lilia gasped. “Where are your manners?! Introduce me to the poor girl you’ve been hoarding away these past few months!”

Agatha sighed. “Mother, this is Rio. Rio, my mother—Lilia, agent of chaos and destroyer of peace.”

Lilia laughed delightedly, stepping forward and grasping Rio’s hands.

“Oh, honey, you’re even prettier in person,” she said, squeezing her hands warmly. “I was worried my daughter was going to end up a spinster, but you’re absolutely stunning.”

Rio, who had never been called stunning by an older, elegant, tequila-wielding woman before, just... blushed.

Agatha groaned. “Mother, please.”

“What? I’m just saying, if I were twenty years younger, I’d be very jealous.”

Agatha tilted her head back, exasperated. Pulling out her phone and capturing a video of the blender and line of drinks.

Caption: When your mom literally thinks your life is a movie

Rio, flustered but amused, just laughed. “It’s nice to meet you.”

“Oh, sweetheart, the pleasure is mine,” Lilia said dramatically, handing Rio a margarita. “Tell me, has my daughter been treating you right? Because I’ll have you know, she’s never been this in l…”

“MOTHER,” Agatha interrupted, grabbing Rio’s hand and pulling her toward the living room. “We’re going back to bed, you can sleep in the guest room.”

Lilia just cackled, sipping her margarita.

“Love you too, baby!” she called after them.

Agatha collapsed onto the bed face-first.

Rio sat on the edge, still processing.

“…So that’s your mom.”

Agatha’s muffled voice came from the pillow. “The woman, the myth and the legend”

Rio bit back a grin. “I think I love her.”

Agatha lifted her head just enough to glare.

“Don’t encourage her.”

Rio just laughed, flopping down next to her.

Midnight margaritas, huh?

Dating Agatha Harkness was never going to be boring.

Chapter 22

Rio still wasn’t over the whole midnight margarita ambush.

Agatha’s mother was a lot. In the best, most ridiculous way possible. She had sent Rio a Snapchat request the next morning, which Rio had tentatively accepted, only to immediately receive a picture of a perfectly made mimosa.

Caption: Breakfast is waiting. I see why my daughter likes you

Rio had screeched when she opened it, while Agatha, still half-asleep, had just groaned and buried her face in a pillow.

“She’s testing you.”

“Testing me for what?”

“To see if you can survive her.”

Honestly, Rio wasn’t sure she could.

Agatha had been ridiculously busy the next few days, which meant Rio only got to experience her life through Snapchat stories and chaotic texts.

There were pictures of script pages, half-covered in her scrawled notes, captioned: If I have to cry in ONE more scene, I’m billing my therapist.

One of Bucky filming her from a horrific angle as she sat slumped in a makeup chair, looking utterly exhausted, captioned: Glamorous life of a movie star.

A video where she whisper-screamed at a malfunctioning coffee machine on set: “If you don’t work, I don’t work.”

And, of course, the occasional cute one, Agatha and Remi on a walk, the dog’s ears flopping in the wind, captioned: My child, my everything

Rio obsessively watched them all, feeling a little ridiculous for missing Agatha so much when she’d just seen her.

She was getting so soft.

Then, one night, Rio was flipping through Agatha’s latest Snap stories when she got a message.

Agatha: Hey, sweetheart, can I call?

Rio, already grinning like an idiot, sent back a selfie from bed with an exaggerated thumbs-up.

A second later, her phone rang.

“Hey,” Rio said, voice already warm just from hearing Agatha’s voice.

“Hey yourself,” Agatha purred. “So, listen—I have a movie premiere coming up. For that thing I shot last year. And I was wondering…”

“…Yeah?”

“…If you’d come with me.”

Rio froze.

“Like… as in… a red carpet?”

Agatha laughed. “Yes, Rio, as in a red carpet.”

“Oh,” Rio said, mind blanking entirely. “Oh. Oh no.”

Agatha snorted. “What do you mean, oh no?”

“I mean, oh no, I’ll be looked at.”

Agatha laughed again, but softer this time. “Sweetheart, people already know we’re together. This is just… making it more official. I want you there.”

Rio bit her lip. “But I—I don’t know how to do any of that. What if I trip? What if I get blinded by the camera flashes and accidentally walk into traffic?”

Agatha sighed dramatically. “Then I’ll personally pull you back to safety, like the heroic girlfriend I am.”

Rio groaned, burying her face in her pillow.

“Honey,” Agatha said, softer now. “I promise I won’t let anything bad happen to you. If it gets too much, we leave. No pressure, okay?”

Rio sighed. “Okay. But if I say something weird in an interview, you have to pretend I’m a very sophisticated European model who doesn’t speak English.”

Agatha cackled. “Deal.”

The night before the premier, Agatha posted a short video to her private Snap:

A gorgeous dress laid out on her bed, all deep purple silk and elegance.

Caption: Big night tomorrow. Got the prettiest date, too. Nervous? Me? Never

Rio, watching this from her couch, felt her stomach flip.

Because holy shit. This was happening.

And it was happening tomorrow.

The morning of the premiere, Rio woke up in a state of sheer panic.

Because what the hell was she doing? She was a florist. She arranged pretty little bouquets for a living. Meanwhile, Agatha Harkness was an internationally famous actress.

And somehow, against all logic, Rio was about to walk a red carpet with her.

She arrived at Agatha’s house early in the afternoon, heart pounding.

Agatha, still in silk pajama pants and a half-unbuttoned dress shirt, greeted her at the door with a coffee in hand.

“Hello.” Agatha smirked, leaning in to kiss her.

“Hello, sweetheart.” Rio groaned as she stepped inside. “I think I’m having a heart attack.”

Agatha laughed, tugging her inside. “You’re being dramatic.”

“No, I mean it. My palms are sweating. What if I trip?”

“Then I’ll catch you.”

“What if I say something weird?”

Agatha sipped her coffee. “That’s inevitable.”

Rio gasped. “Rude.”

Agatha just grinned and led her upstairs, where a team of stylists was already setting up in front of a vanity mirror.

“Oh, no,” Rio said. “Oh no, I’m not famous enough for this.”

Agatha rolled her eyes. “You’re famous adjacent, by association. Sit.”

Rio, weak to Agatha in bossy mode, obeyed.

She watched Agatha disappear into another room to get changed while a stylist took over her face.

“You’re gonna be fine,” the stylist assured her.

“I think I might pass away,” Rio muttered.

The stylist laughed.

When they finally arrived at the event, Rio’s stomach was in knots.

The flashing lights, the screaming fans—it was so much worse than she imagined.

Agatha, looking impossibly gorgeous in her deep purple silk dress, just squeezed her hand. “Stay with me, sweetheart. I got you.”

Which was sweet. But also, Agatha was famous, so all eyes were on her.

It was fine at first. They posed for some pictures, Agatha’s arm wrapped securely around her waist.

Then, interviews started happening.

And that was when Rio completely lost her ability to function as a human.

A reporter turned to her. “So, Rio, how are you handling your first big event?”

Rio blinked. Brain empty. Zero thoughts. She opened her mouth. “Uh. Sweating.”

Agatha snorted, trying to cover her laugh.

The reporter smiled. “Sweating?”

“Yeah, um.” Rio gestured vaguely. “It’s hot out here.”

It was not hot out here. It was a pleasant 68 degrees.

The reporter, bless them, rolled with it. “And what’s it like dating Agatha?”

Rio, still panicking: “Well. She’s very…um… she’s okay.”

Agatha lost it.

Cameras flashed. Reporters laughed.

Rio immediately wanted to dig a hole and live in it.

Chapter 23

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

From the moment Rio stepped onto the red carpet, she knew she had made a terrible, terrible mistake.

The cameras were blinding. The screams from fans were deafening. The sheer pressure of standing next to Agatha freaking Harkness at a major Hollywood event was enough to make her feel like she was going to melt into a puddle of awkwardness right then and there.

Agatha, of course, looked like she was born for this. Meanwhile, Rio was simply trying not to throw up on her shoes.

"Just breathe, sweetheart," Agatha murmured, her hand resting lightly on Rio's lower back.

"Breathing is hard," Rio whispered back through gritted teeth.

Agatha just chuckled and squeezed her waist. "You're adorable when you panic."

Rio shot her a betrayed look. This was not a time to be adorable. This was a time to focus on not publicly humiliating herself.

Unfortunately, that goal would not be met.

After already telling one reported Agatha was ‘okay’, they moved further down the carpet, a reporter from ET Tonight stopped them with a bright, beaming smile.

"Agatha! Looking absolutely stunning as always. And this must be Rio, the woman who's stolen your heart!"

Rio, very much not prepared to be acknowledged in such a way, blinked like a deer caught in headlights.

"Yep, this is my girlfriend," Agatha said smoothly, sliding an arm around Rio’s waist. She was so at ease, so effortlessly charming that Rio wanted to cry from how unfair it was.

The reporter turned to Rio, microphone out. "How does it feel to be here tonight, walking the red carpet with one of Hollywood’s biggest stars?"

Rio's brain short-circuited.

The correct response would have been something like ‘It's an honor,’ or ‘I'm so excited to be here.’

Instead, her mouth betrayed her. Again, with the same line.

"I'm sweating a lot."

Agatha immediately burst into laughter.

The reporter, to their credit, took it in stride. "Understandable! Big night, lots of cameras."

Rio, still spiralling, “Yeah. And also, it's…um…I already said this over there, its hot?"

Agatha, grinning ear to ear, leaned into the mic and deadpanned, " She’s nervous."

The reporter laughed. “Well, its a big night, nerves will do that to you!"

Rio, now desperate to recover, blurted out, "She’s just very… tall tonight"

A beat of silence.

Then Agatha completely lost it. She threw her head back, laughing so hard that she had to briefly let go of Rio to clutch her stomach.

The reporter was now laughing too. "Tall?"

Rio, already accepting death, nodded solemnly. "Very tall. Heels."

By the time they reached the main event inside the theater, Rio’s disastrous interview was already trending on social media.

#Tallgate was officially a thing.

Twitter was having a field day.

AgathaHarknessStan: Rio calling Agatha tall as if we didn’t already see the pics of her being taller than Agatha normally???? Girl you could’ve said ANYTHING.

@LesbianDisaster69: Protect Rio at all costs. She’s one of us.

@MovieNerd101: Rio: “She’s okay and tall." Agatha: immediately falls more in love with her

@GayForHarkness: Agathas real laugh at her girlfriend’s awkwardness???? SHE IS SO GONE FOR HER.

@RedCarpetFails: SWEATING. This is the most relatable red carpet moment in HISTORY.

Even Agathas celebrity friends were joining in.

@BuckyBarnes (yes, Agatha's best friend Bucky): Welcome to the elite club of people who publicly embarrass themselves for fun.

@THEGREENWITCH: I just spit out my drink watching Rio’s interview. Protect her. She’s precious.

Meanwhile, Agatha herself decided to lean into it.

She posted a Snapchat story to her friends and family of her looking smug.

CAPTION: Very tall

The next snap was a blurry video of Rio hiding her face in her hands with Agatha's laughter in the background.

Caption: Isn’t she amazing

Unfortunately, Rio’s suffering wasn’t over.

As they were about to enter the venue, one last reporter flagged them down.

"Agatha! Rio! You two look absolutely gorgeous tonight."

Rio, having learned nothing, panicked again. "Oh, well, um, Agatha looks gorgeous. I’m just existing."

Agatha, clearly head over heels even if Rio didn’t see it yet, looked at Rio with so much fondness it was sickening. In a way the world took notice off.

"She looks breathtaking,*" Agatha corrected smoothly, her hand slipping down to hold Rio’s.

The reporter grinned. “So, Rio, what’s it like dating a world-famous actress?"

Rio, again, had so many options for how to answer that.

Instead, she panicked.

"She eats all my fries."

A beat of silence.

Then Agatha, wheezing, turned to the reporter and confirmed, “I do. I absolutely do.”

The reporter laughed. “So, Agatha, how do you feel about Rio’s red carpet debut tonight?"

Agatha turned to Rio and gave her the softest look imaginable.

"I think she’s perfect."

And that was when Rio’s brain fully shut down.

Later that night, in the car on the way home, Rio sat with her face buried in her hands.

"I can never go outside again."

Agatha, still grinning, already holding tight to one of Rios hands, reached over to squeeze Rio’s thigh with the other. "Sweetheart, you crushed it."

Rio lifted her head just enough to glare at her. "I called you tall. On national television."

Agatha giggled. “And I am tall in my heels"

"You’re average height. I’m taller than you!"

Agatha just smirked. "Only by an inch."

Rio groaned dramatically and flopped back against the seat. "Why are you like this?"

Agatha leaned over at a red light and kissed Rio’s temple. "Because I adore you."

Rio peeked at her through her fingers. "…Even though I’m a nervous wreck?"

Agatha smiled. "Especially because of that."

And just like that, Rio’s humiliation was slightly more bearable.

At least until she opened Twitter again and saw #TallGate still trending.

Yeah. She was never living this down.

Chapter End Notes

Feedback/comments are appreciated

Chapter 24

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

For most people, wedding season was a joyful time. Love was in the air, romance blossomed, and happy couples danced under twinkling fairy lights.

For Rio, wedding season was hell.

As a florist, she was slammed with back-to-back wedding orders, last-minute panicked brides, grooms forgetting their bouquets, and one particularly aggressive mother-in-law who threatened to throw an entire centerpiece at her.

She barely had time to sleep, let alone think.

Which was unfortunately how she ended up completely neglecting her relationship with Agatha.

Not intentionally, of course. Rio loved Agatha. Was so madly in love she thought of little else usually, especially the thought of finally admitting to her that she loved her. She was obsessed with her.

But Rio had this horrible little trait where, when overwhelmed, instead of talking about it, she just… shut down.

So, instead of texting Agatha first or calling just to say hi, she only replied when Agatha reached out first.

She figured it was fine. She wasn’t ignoring Agatha—she was just busy!

It was not fine.

Because Agatha was spiraling.

It was a Friday afternoon when Rio finally had a moment to herself. The shop was quieter than usual, the flowers had been delivered, and the last-minute orders were all handled. For the first time in weeks, she could breathe.

She collapsed onto the couch in the backroom, phone in hand.

It started with Bucky sending Rio an extremely pointed Snapchat.

Bucky: Yo. Fix this.

Rio: …Fix what?

Bucky: Agatha is spiraling so hard she just suggested I take her phone away so she doesn’t text you again.

Rio: …Oh.

Bucky: She thinks you’re losing interest.

Rio: WHAT??? NO

Bucky: Then TELL HER THAT.

Bucky: Babe. She is convinced you’re gonna break up with her.

Rio: OH MY GOD

Bucky: You absolute fool.

Rio blinked in shock, her stomach sinking.

She had been so focused on her work, so stressed by the pressure of wedding season, that she hadn't even noticed how much she’d been withdrawing.

Agatha had been calling and texting as much as she usually did but with Rios one word responses that had become less and less as well. When Rio did reply, it was almost robotic, minimal. Not the affectionate, light-hearted banter that had once come so easily. Agatha deserved more than that.

Rio: Oh my god. No, no, no.

She quickly began typing again.

Rio: Tell her I adore her. I just got so caught up in work I didn’t realize I was doing it. Tell her I’m not going anywhere

Bucky: Dude, just fix it yourself. I’m not playing therapist here

Rio: I’m such an idiot

Bucky: Yeah, but at least you’re self-aware. Now go talk to your girl before she burns her phone overthinking this whole thing

Rio stared at the screen, feeling like she was suffocating.

Bucky: Also, you better apologize for being a massive idiot when you finally get to see her

That did it.

Rio: Okay, okay. Thanks. I’m calling her now

She hesitated for a long moment, a lump in her throat. She could feel her heart hammering in her chest as she unlocked her phone and found Agatha’s contact. She clicked on it, stared at the screen, then clicked again.

It was no use—she needed to do this. For Agatha. For herself.

She took a deep breath and dialed.

Agatha picked up on the second ring. Her voice, usually so warm and smooth, was thinner, softer. It cracked when she said her name.

“Rio? Are you okay?” Agatha asked, a trace of worry threading her voice.

“I—yeah. I mean, no. Not really,” Rio replied quickly, her voice shaking as she settled herself against the couch. “I’m so sorry, Agatha. I’ve been completely awful.”

There was a pause on the other end. The soft shuffle of a chair could be heard as Agatha shifted, but she didn’t speak.

“I’ve been so wrapped up in wedding season and the shop,” Rio continued, her words stumbling over each other. “But that’s not an excuse. I should’ve been there for you. I should’ve talked to you more. I—God, I just went quiet, and you didn’t deserve that.”

Agatha’s voice was quiet when she spoke again. “I thought you were pulling away. I thought maybe you didn’t want to be with me anymore.”

Rio closed her eyes, feeling the ache of guilt bloom in her chest. "Agatha...no. That’s the last thing I want. I was just overwhelmed, and I shut down. But that's not your fault."

“I’m not mad at you,” Agatha said softly, but there was still a sadness to her tone that Rio hated. “I just—I thought you didn’t want this anymore, and I don’t know if I can cope with that.”

Rio bit her lip, trying to figure out the right words. “I want this. I want you, Agatha.” She paused. “I never should’ve let work make me forget that. I was being an idiot.”

There was a long silence. Agatha let out a soft breath, as if she was collecting herself. “I don’t want to be the one who’s constantly chasing you,” she said, her voice tinged with vulnerability. “I don’t want to feel like I’m the only one trying.”

Rio’s chest tightened. “You’re not the only one, Agatha. You’re not. I’m sorry, okay? I’m so sorry.”

“I just need you to show me, Rio,” Agatha whispered, her voice barely audible. “I need to feel like I’m a priority too.”

A tear slipped down Rio’s cheek as she nodded, even though Agatha couldn’t see her. “You are a priority, Agatha. I swear to you.”

“Then show me,” Agatha said, her voice gaining strength. “Show me that you’re all in.”

“I will,” Rio promised. “I’ll do whatever it takes.”

“I need to believe you,” Agatha replied, her voice still soft, but now tinged with hope.

“I’ll prove it to you. I’ll fix this. I promise.”

Another long pause followed, but it wasn’t uncomfortable anymore. This time, it was filled with understanding, with the acknowledgment of their shared feelings.

“I’m not mad at you,” Agatha finally said. “Just...next time, don’t disappear on me, okay?”

“I won’t,” Rio replied. “I won’t.”

“I’m holding you to that.”

“Agatha, I swear.”

A few minutes later, Rio sent Agatha a snap. It was a simple photo of her sitting in the back room of the shop, a sad but earnest smile on her face. She’d meant what she said.

Caption: I’m going to fix this, I swear. I adore you. Please don’t ever think I’m pulling away

Agatha replied instantly with a snap of her own—a picture of her smiling, looking a little more relaxed than she had in days.

Caption: I believe you

It was the first step.

And as Rio wiped away the last of her tears, she knew she’d do anything to make sure it stayed that way. For Agatha.

It was nearly midnight when Rio finally sat down at home, phone in hand, staring at the chat from Agatha.

Agatha: Can we talk tomorrow? Just us?

Her heart sank. Rio had been so sure they were on the same page, so confident that she was making things right after her recent silence. But now, with this simple message, it felt like the floor had fallen out from beneath her.

Rio couldn’t help it. She began to spiral.

Talk? She hadn’t meant to mess things up, but what if she had? What if Agatha was done? Maybe she had grown tired of Rio’s awkwardness, her insecurities. She’d had enough of this back-and-forth with Rio being distant, especially when Agatha was so used to being in the spotlight and surrounded by people who understood her.

Maybe Rio wasn’t enough.

Her phone buzzed in her hand, and she jumped, pulling her eyes away from the screen for a moment. It was a Snapchat from Alice.

Alice: You okay? I’ve not heard from you for a while

Rio stared at the message for a second. Alice always had that sixth sense when it came to knowing when something was up. And, of course, this time wasn’t any different. With a sigh, Rio snapped back quickly.

Rio: I don’t know, Al. Agatha just sent me a message asking if we can talk tomorrow. But I think she’s just tired of me. Like, maybe I’m just too much for her, you know? She’s probably realized she deserves better.

She hesitated for a moment before sending another message.

Rio: I can’t shake the feeling that she’s just over me, I’ve been accidentally ignoring her the last few weeks

Her phone buzzed almost immediately. Alice’s response was just as fast.

Alice: Wait, wait, wait...did you even see Agatha’s interview last week?

Rio frowned, tapping out a quick response.

Rio: What interview? I didn’t know she had one.

Alice: Omg, Rio. Are you serious? I thought you kept up with her stuff. In the interview, they asked her about you. And she literally lit up. She gushed about how much she cares about you, like, so much. She talked about how she loves your little quirks, how you make her feel grounded, like a normal person. She even mentioned how much she enjoys being with you, how you’re different than anyone else she’s been with.

Rio blinked, feeling a rush of warmth flood her chest, but at the same time, a wave of guilt rushed in. How had she missed that?

She’d barely been keeping up with Agatha’s stories lately, lost in the haze of her own work stress and spiraling thoughts, never mind what she was doing with work. But hearing Alice’s words, seeing them written out like that, made Rio feel worse.

How had she not even known about it?

Rio: What? She really said that?

Alice: Yeah, she literally couldn’t stop smiling when they brought you up. You should go watch it. I’ll send you the link.

Rio was stunned. She felt the weight of her own insecurity slip just a little bit, but it didn’t take away the knot in her stomach.

Agatha was clearly still invested in their relationship—maybe more than Rio had given her credit for—but now Rio felt like she had missed the chance to be involved in something that had obviously meant so much to Agatha.

A few minutes passed before Alice sent over a link to the interview. Rio opened it, fingers trembling, and the first thing she saw was Agatha sitting in front of a camera, looking effortlessly beautiful in a soft beige dress, her eyes twinkling with amusement as the interviewer asked about her relationship.

“So, Agatha, the public has been buzzing about your love life recently. We’ve seen glimpses of someone special on your social media and as your date for the red carpet. Care to tell us about that?”

Agatha smiled, her lips curving with a soft fondness. She leaned forward, her tone warm and inviting.

“Oh, you mean Rio? Yeah, I’m very happy. Rio’s amazing—she’s honestly the best thing that’s ever happened to me. She’s real, you know? I love how she’s grounded. She doesn’t let the fame thing overwhelm her, and she makes me feel...normal.”

Rio paused the video, her hand trembling as she replayed those words in her mind. I make her feel normal?

The interviewer continued, clearly intrigued by Agatha’s openness.

“So, what is it about her that makes her stand out from the rest?”

Agatha’s smile softened even more, and she took a deep breath before responding.

“She’s just...different, you know? She’s not intimidated by me. She doesn’t put me on a pedestal, and she’s incredibly patient. She’s quirky, too. Her little weird habits just...they make me smile. Honestly, I don’t know how to explain it, but there’s something special about her. I can’t see myself with anyone else.”

Rio hit pause again, staring at the screen, her heart pounding in her chest. She can’t see herself with anyone else? Shes said all of this about me while I’ve ignored her?

Alice’s snap came through just as Rio was digesting everything.

Alice: See? You’re her person, Rio. She’s obviously mad about you.

Rio’s stomach still twisted with uncertainty, but Alice’s words gave her a sliver of hope. She had always known Agatha cared about her, but to hear it so clearly from Agatha herself… it was different.

Despite the little voice in her head that still wondered if she was somehow unworthy, Rio knew that Agatha had always been the kind of person who was truthful to a fault. If Agatha had said all of that in an interview, there was no way she didn’t feel the same way Rio did.

Still, Rio couldn’t shake the nagging worry.

Rio: Okay, I’m going to watch the rest of it. But... I’m still nervous about what Agatha meant by talk

Alice: Trust me, just watch it. You’ll see. And don’t freak out. You two are meant to be together

Rio took a deep breath, tapping the play button on the interview once more. She had to stop spiraling. Agatha clearly cared, and Rio needed to show her she did too.

As the interview continued, Rio couldn’t help but feel a little lighter, but she still wasn’t completely convinced. There was still a part of her that feared the conversation Agatha wanted to have.

But for now, all she could do was watch and take things one step at a time.

Chapter Notes

Rio’s nerves hadn’t lessened overnight. She had spent the entire day at her shop, busying herself with arrangements, but her mind kept drifting back to Agatha’s message. What did she want to talk about?

The anticipation of their conversation hung heavy in the air, making her hands tremble as she arranged petals and foliage in the most perfect way she could manage. Each time her phone buzzed, her heart would race, convinced it was Agatha asking for their talk.

But it wasn’t.

It was Alice sending her memes, or the occasional delivery notification from her online orders. The silence from Agatha made her heart feel heavy. It was becoming too much to bear, and she was starting to wonder if Agatha had changed her mind about her despite how she spoke in the interview.

When the doorbell to the shop jingled, Rio’s head snapped up. She didn’t expect to see Agatha, not in person at least. But there she was, standing in the doorway with a cautious smile. Agatha’s expression softened the moment their eyes met, and Rio’s heart skipped a beat.

“Hey, sweetheart,” Agatha said, stepping inside with a gentle sway of her hips. In her arms was an enormous bouquet, not of flowers, but something entirely different—an arrangement of chocolates, caramels, and various sweet treats, all carefully wrapped and tied together with satin ribbons.

“Hi,” Rio’s voice cracked, as if it hadn’t fully realized she was breathing again.

Agatha didn’t seem to notice her slight nervousness. She smiled warmly and stepped closer, holding out the gift.

“These are for you,” Agatha said softly. “I know you’ve been having a stressful time with work.” Her voice was calm, almost hypnotic. There was no tension between them, just warmth, understanding, and a gentleness Rio couldn’t quite explain.

Rio took the bouquet of treats from Agatha’s hands, her eyes flitting over the assortment. There were chocolate truffles, little caramel squares, and some gourmet cookies. It was thoughtful. It was so her.

“I—thank you,” Rio whispered, her voice unsteady. She looked at Agatha, feeling suddenly vulnerable.

Agatha tilted her head, her eyes soft and understanding as she took in Rio’s expression. She gently cupped Rio’s cheek, guiding her gaze back to her. “You don’t have to thank me for this, Rio,” Agatha murmured, her thumb tracing gentle circles on Rio’s skin. “Your my girlfriend, I want to support you in anyway I can, especially when I can see how hard things have been for you lately. Ive really missed you.”

Rio felt the warmth spread through her chest, but it didn’t stop the tears that threatened to well up in her eyes. She wasn’t sure why she was on the verge of tears, but everything felt so overwhelming in the most tender way. She gadnt realised how much she’d been absent until hearing Agatha say she’s missed her.

Agatha’s kindness, the thoughtfulness behind this small gesture, it all settled in a place deep inside Rio that she hadn’t realized was aching.

Before she could stop herself, a tear slipped down her cheek. Agatha noticed instantly, her gaze softening even further, a quiet understanding passing between them.

“Hey, hey,” Agatha whispered, her voice full of affection as she reached out to wipe the tear away. “Don’t cry, honey. It’s okay.”

Rio shook her head, struggling to compose herself. “I’m sorry... I don’t know why I’m crying. It’s just... I’ve been a shit girlfriend, I’ve been such a mess. I didn’t mean to shut myself off from you, I didn’t mean to make you think I was pulling away, Agatha. I’m just—”

Agatha cut her off gently, her fingers still on Rio’s cheek as she leaned in, forehead brushing softly against Rio’s. “You don’t need to apologize. You’re not a mess, Rio. You’re just human and I know you’ve had a lot on your plate. But I want you to know—” Her voice was almost a whisper, the sincerity in her words clear as she spoke, “—I care about you. So much.”

Rio’s breath hitched, her eyes searching Agatha’s face for any signs of insincerity, but all she saw was compassion, tenderness and although they’d not said the words to each other, love. The knot in her chest slowly started to loosen, the weight she’d been carrying lightening just a little. She swallowed hard, feeling an overwhelming sense of relief.

Agatha smiled softly, brushing a stray lock of hair behind Rio’s ear. “I get it, Rio. But I want you to know that I’m here for you. You don’t have to shut me out, even if things get overwhelming. We’ll figure it out together.”

Rio closed her eyes for a moment, a single tear slipping down her cheek at the realization of how much Agatha truly meant to her. She leaned into the touch, sighing softly as the tension in her body finally started to melt away.

“You really mean that?” Rio asked in a voice barely above a whisper, her hands trembling as she set the bouquet of sweets on the counter.

“Of course I do,” Agatha replied, her voice warm and unwavering. “I want to be there for you, no matter what.” She paused for a moment, looking at Rio with a gentle smile. “In fact, I’ve got something else for you too...”

Rio’s brow furrowed. “What?” she asked, trying to hold back the emotion that was still swirling inside her.

Agatha grinned and reached into her bag, pulling out a small envelope. She handed it to Rio, her eyes twinkling.

“Open it,” Agatha urged.

Curious, Rio opened the envelope and pulled out a gift card for a luxurious spa, a full massage session, facial, and everything. It was exactly the kind of thing Rio would never have bought for herself. But Agatha had done it for her, understanding that she’d been working too hard, neglecting herself.

“I figured you could use a little relaxation,” Agatha said with a teasing smile, her eyes glinting. “Just you, make a day of it, just take some pictures for me.”

Rio couldn’t help but laugh at that. Her heart felt lighter than it had in days. The anxiety that had been plaguing her seemed to disappear just by being with Agatha—just by seeing how much Agatha cared.

“Thank you,” Rio said again, this time her voice steadier, full of gratitude. “You really know how to make me feel better.”

Agatha smiled, pulling Rio closer until she could press a soft, reassuring kiss to her forehead. “You don’t need to thank me, Rio. Just promise me one thing...”

“Anything,” Rio whispered.

“Promise me you won’t push me away when things get tough again. We’re a team, remember?” Agatha said softly, her voice full of warmth.

Rio nodded, feeling more certain than ever. “I promise,” she said, her heart finally at peace.

As they stood there in the warmth of Agatha’s presence, with the bouquet of treats between them and the soft promise lingering in the air, Rio realized just how lucky she was. Lucky to have found someone who saw her for who she was—flaws, quirks, and all. And most importantly, she felt lucky to have found someone who was willing to stick by her side through it all.

The next morning, Rio felt a strange mix of excitement and nervousness as she headed to the spa. Agatha had insisted she go on her own, encouraging Rio to truly relax and focus on herself. Rio had been hesitant at first, unsure about being by herself, especially after everything that had happened with Agatha. But after hearing the sincere tone in Agatha’s voice, Rio decided to take the plunge and indulge in some much-needed self-care.

The spa was tucked away in a tranquil corner of the city, surrounded by lush greenery and an aura of peace that seemed to wash over her the moment she stepped through the door. As she was greeted by a receptionist, Rio could already feel her muscles relaxing, the weight of the past few weeks slipping off her shoulders.

When she was led to the changing room, she noticed that the spa was buzzing with energy. There were a few whispers here and there, and she caught one staff member looking at her curiously. Rio didn’t think much of it at first, but, the spa’s employees seemed to recognize her. She found herself becoming the subject of soft, polite murmurs as she was ushered into the serene space.

“Are you... Rio?” one of the attendants asked hesitantly.

Rio smiled, slightly confused. “Yes?” she answered, wondering how the staff knew her name.

“We’ve seen you in the news a lot lately, and... well, we had to ask.” The attendant blushed. “You know, with you being Agatha’s... well, her girlfriend.”

Rio froze. The word felt so surreal to her, like something out of a dream. The idea of being Agatha’s girlfriend still hadn’t fully sunk in. She had been too focused on the whirlwind of everything happening around her to think about the label, but now, hearing it from a stranger’s lips made her feel like she was living in a world she couldn’t quite wrap her head around.

“Uh… yeah, that’s me,” Rio replied, laughing nervously. “I’m just, you know, normal.”

Another attendant, a woman with a bright smile, chimed in, “Oh, we know! But we’ve been following you both on social media, and we think it’s so sweet. Agatha is such a beautiful person, and it’s lovely to see her so happy. We’re so excited for you two!”

Rio’s cheeks flushed, and she shifted awkwardly on her feet. She hadn’t quite realized how much Agatha’s public life—and, by extension, her own—was becoming a topic of interest to others. It felt strange to be the subject of questions, to feel like her relationship with Agatha was no longer a private thing.

But at the same time, the kindness in their voices made her feel accepted. Still, she couldn’t quite shake the surreal sensation that she was somehow more visible than she’d ever wanted to be.

After her treatments, which included a calming facial, a massage, and a soak in the hot tub, Rio felt utterly relaxed. The spa had done wonders, and for the first time in weeks, she felt like she could breathe again.

When she left the spa and headed to Agatha’s, Rio was floating, almost weightless. She wasn’t sure if it was the massage or the idea of finally spending time with Agatha, but she felt lighter than she had in ages. As she arrived at Agatha’s house, the familiar warmth greeted her.

The pool outside glistened in the fading sunlight. Rio kicked off her shoes and wandered into the backyard, where Agatha was waiting for her.

Agatha had already changed into a simple yet elegant robe, her hair still damp from a shower. She was sitting on one of the lounge chairs, her eyes hidden behind a pair of sunglasses, but Rio could tell she was smiling just by the way her lips twitched.

“Hey,” Agatha said as Rio walked closer. “How was the spa? Did you get to really relax?”

Rio grinned, her eyes sparkling. “It was amazing. I think I needed that more than I realized. Thank you.”

Agatha’s smile softened. “I’m glad you did. You deserve it.”

Rio took a deep breath, feeling the stillness of the moment between them. Agatha was such a calming presence, and it made Rio feel completely at ease. She walked over to the edge of the pool and dipped a toe into the water, testing its coolness.

“You’re going to love the water,” Agatha teased. “It’s perfect.”

Rio laughed, her nerves slowly melting away in Agatha’s presence. “I’m sure it is.”

She hesitated for a moment before stepping fully into the pool. The cool water surrounded her, and she let out a content sigh as she swam toward the center. She turned back to Agatha, who was watching her intently, clearly amused.

Without saying anything more, Agatha stood up from the lounge chair and slid into the water, her feet gliding gracefully through the pool. She moved toward Rio with effortless elegance, the water rippling around her.

Rio couldn’t help but stare. Agatha, even in something as simple as a robe, was effortlessly beautiful.

Agatha stopped in front of her, her eyes full of warmth. “Come here,” she said softly, reaching out for Rio’s hand.

Rio took it without thinking, and Agatha pulled her close. She guided Rio to float on her back in the water, the sounds of the world muffled by the serenity of the pool.

Agatha settled herself beside Rio, her back against the edge of the pool as they both floated together. Rio could feel Agatha’s gentle presence beside her, the soft splash of water surrounding them. She wasn’t sure what it was about the moment—whether it was the calm of the water or the closeness between them—but Rio felt incredibly safe and at peace.

They stayed like that for what felt like hours, floating in the pool together, the sky shifting from shades of pink and purple to the deep indigo of night. The stars above twinkled softly, and Rio couldn’t help but think how lucky she was. She was here, with Agatha.

“Do you ever think about the future?” Rio asked quietly, breaking the silence.

Agatha turned her head to look at her, her expression thoughtful. “I think about it all the time.” She paused before adding with a small smile, “But with you, it feels different. I’m not worried about it. I’m just... happy to be here, with you.”

Rio smiled back, feeling her heart swell at Agatha’s words. “Yeah... me too.”

And for the first time in a long while, Rio let herself truly believe it. Everything that had happened—her spiraling doubts, the anxiety about their relationship—suddenly didn’t seem as important. It was just them, in the pool, floating together in perfect peace.

“Hey, I’m really glad we’re together,” Rio whispered, feeling a warmth in her chest she couldn’t explain.

Agatha grinned. “Me too, Rio. Me too.”

And for that moment, nothing else in the world mattered.
