Chapter 26

The news came one evening as Agatha sat on the couch, flipping through a script for her upcoming film. Rio had just finished a long day at the flower shop and had made her way over to Agatha’s house, as was becoming their usual routine. Agatha smiled when she saw Rio walk through the door, exhaustion fading from her face at the sight of her.

"Hey, my love," Agatha said softly, patting the space next to her on the couch. "I’ve got some news."

Rio’s eyebrows furrowed at the pet name, as she dropped her bag by the door and joined her on the couch. "What’s up? You look like you’ve got a heavy heart," she said, settling next to Agatha and giving her hand a reassuring squeeze.

Agatha sighed, looking down at the script in her hands. "I just got a call from the studio," she said, her voice slightly trembling. "They’re sending me across a few different countries to film the next part of my project. It’s going to take a couple of months."

Rio blinked in surprise. "Wait, what? You’re going away for a couple of months?" she asked, her voice tinged with a mix of disbelief and sadness. "That’s... that's a lot."

Agatha nodded, rubbing her hands together nervously. "Yeah, it’s been in the works for a while. But I didn’t want to tell you until everything was confirmed. I’ll be filming in Spain, Italy, and then a few weeks in Japan. It’s a huge opportunity, but..." She trailed off, looking at Rio with a sad smile. "I don’t know how I’m going to do this without you."

Rio’s heart sank. She had known Agatha’s career meant long hours, but a few months away felt like a lifetime. Her stomach twisted in anxiety as she reached out to cup Agatha’s face, gently guiding her to look up. "I’ll miss you too," she said softly, trying to keep the tears at bay. "But you’re going to kill it. You’ve always been so amazing at what you do."

Agatha smiled through her sadness, brushing her fingers against Rio’s cheek. "I know. But it’s not just about the filming. I’m going to miss you" she said, her voice breaking slightly. "I’ll miss waking up next to you. I’ll miss seeing you every day, talking about the most random stuff. And I’ll miss the way you laugh when I do something ridiculous."

Rio’s heart squeezed as she realized just how much Agatha was going to miss her, too. She could see the vulnerability in Agatha’s eyes, the same vulnerability that Agatha had rarely shown to anyone, even in the quiet moments when they were alone.

"I’m going to miss you so much, Agatha," Rio whispered, brushing a few stray strands of hair behind Agatha’s ear. "But we’ll make it work. We’ll figure it out."

Agatha shook her head slightly. "I just... I wish I didn’t have to leave. I don’t want to go, but I have to."

There was a long pause as both women sat in the stillness of the room, the weight of the situation settling in. Rio felt her chest tighten, the thought of being apart from Agatha for months weighing on her. "What about Remi and Señor Scratchy?" she asked, trying to keep the mood light. "Are they coming with you?"

Agatha’s lips curled into a small smile. "Of course. They’re my emotional support team," she said, voice a little lighter. "I can’t leave them behind. Remi will be a menace if she’s not with me."

Rio chuckled softly, but it didn’t quite reach her eyes. "They’re lucky," she said quietly. "I wish I could come with you."

Agatha turned to her, her expression soft and understanding. "I know. I wish you could be there, too. But I promise, when I get back... we’ll make up for lost time, okay?"

Rio nodded, but her heart ached at the thought of how many moments they were going to miss together. "Okay," she whispered, her voice small.

Agatha leaned in and kissed her forehead, lingering for a moment before pulling back. "I’m going to miss you so much, Rio. More than I can even say."

Rio’s eyes welled up with tears, but she held them back, not wanting to make the moment any harder than it already was. "I’m going to miss you too. I just wish this was easier."

The next few days were filled with a mix of bittersweet moments. They spent every minute they could together, making plans for video calls and long-distance communication. Agatha promised to send Rio little things to remind her of her girlfriend —photos, voice notes, and whatever else she could think of.

The night before Agatha was supposed to leave, they sat on the couch together, curled up in blankets. Remi and Señor Scratchy were both lounging around them, adding a sense of comfort to the space. Rio didn’t want to talk about it, but Agatha kept bringing it up, her anxiety creeping in.

"I’m so sorry about all of this," Agatha said, her voice thick with emotion. "I know this is going to be hard, and I hate putting this on you."

Rio shook her head, holding Agatha’s hand tightly. "It’s not on me. It’s not your fault you’re amazing at your job," she said with a small smile. "I’ll be fine. I promise. I just wish we didn’t have to be apart."

Agatha leaned into her, resting her head on Rio’s shoulder. "I know. But I’m going to make it up to you. When I get back, I want to take you somewhere special, just the two of us. We’ll make memories that’ll last a lifetime."

Rio smiled, her heart swelling with affection. "I’ll be counting down the days," she said softly, kissing Agatha’s temple.

The next morning, as Agatha packed her bags to leave, she kissed Rio goodbye, taking a moment to hold her close before slipping away. "I’ll be back before you know it," she said, her voice soft, almost like a promise. "I love you."

She said it first. Agatha actually said it.

"I love you too," Rio whispered, watching as Agatha drove away, her heart torn between longing and the excitement that Agatha would return to her soon.

For now, all Rio could do was hold on to the memories of their time together, knowing that their love would only grow stronger, even from miles away.

As the days passed, Rio found herself slipping back into a rhythm without Agatha physically by her side. The mornings were quieter, and she couldn’t help but feel the empty space beside her in bed. It was only the second day after Agatha had left for Italy, but it already felt like too long.

However, Agatha’s constant presence on her Snapchat made it a little easier to breathe. It was the only way Rio could stay close to her during this time. Agatha had promised to stay in touch every night, and true to her word, she did. Rio found herself eagerly awaiting each Snap from Agatha, as if each one was a lifeline to bridge the distance between them.

Agatha’s stories were filled with stunning views of Italy, from the charming cobblestone streets of Rome to the winding vineyards in the countryside. The landscape was breathtaking, but Rio’s focus was always on Agatha—how the actress looked while navigating these new experiences, how effortlessly beautiful she seemed in every snap, and how she made even the simplest moments feel like magic. One night, Agatha posted a picture of herself sipping a glass of red wine on a terrace overlooking a sunset-drenched landscape.

Caption: Wish you were here. The view’s incredible, but I’d rather be with you.

Rio’s heart skipped at the words, and she immediately replied with a message: I wish I could be there with you too. I miss you already

Each time Agatha posted, Rio would immediately watch the story, her fingers hovering over the screen as if she could touch Agatha through the phone. Sometimes, Agatha would give her a behind-the-scenes peek at the film set. One day, she shared a quick video of herself and the cast goofing around between takes, her laughter infectious. The lighting was perfect, and Rio couldn’t help but smile at how genuinely happy Agatha seemed.

Yet, as much as she loved seeing Agatha so engaged with her work, Rio felt a pang of jealousy. Agatha was surrounded by people—people who got to experience her laughter and company in person. Meanwhile, Rio could only watch from afar, living for the moments when Agatha would call her at the end of the day.

And every night, like clockwork, Agatha would call.

The phone would ring, and Rio’s heart would skip a beat each time. She would answer with a breathless, “Hey, you,” before Agatha’s warm, familiar voice filled her ear.

“How was your day?” Agatha would ask, her tone soft and affectionate, as if they were right next to each other.

“It was good, but it’s been a little quiet without you,” Rio would reply, the ache of missing Agatha apparent in her voice.

Agatha would laugh lightly, the sound comforting in Rio’s ears. “I miss you too. But I’ve got some funny behind-the-scenes stories for you.”

Sometimes it would be a video of Agatha and the crew taking a break. The sun would be setting behind her, casting a golden glow on her features. She’d turn the camera toward herself, her face illuminated, and say, “This is what happens when you work with a bunch of goofballs.” She would then turn the camera to a group of crew members laughing, or a quick shot of a cat on set that had become the unofficial mascot. Agatha’s stories never failed to make Rio smile, and she’d reply with enthusiastic messages, teasing Agatha about her "adorable" crew or how much she wished she could join them.

One night, though, Agatha’s snap was different. Instead of her usual cheerful demeanor, Agatha posted a story of herself sitting alone in a hotel room, the lights dimmed, a glass of wine in her hand, and her expression contemplative. The caption simply read: I hate not being able to share this with you. I miss you more than I expected

Rio’s heart sank at the sight of her, but it also filled her with warmth. I miss you too. It’s been tough, but I know we’re getting through it.

Rio typed in response, her fingers trembling slightly as she sent the message.

Minutes later, Agatha replied, her voice cracking slightly through the voice note. "I know. I just... I hate that I’m here, doing all this cool stuff, but I don’t have you to share it with. I keep thinking about what you’d say or how you’d react to everything. I want to be able to show you these things in person, not just over a screen."

Rio felt her throat tighten as she listened to Agatha’s message. She wanted so badly to be there with her, to hold her and reassure her. “When you come back,” Rio replied, her words slow and thoughtful. “We’ll make up for all of this time. I’m so proud of you, though, Agatha. You’re doing amazing things.”

A few seconds passed before Agatha responded again, this time more upbeat. “I can’t wait. And you’re right, I know it’s just a couple of months. But it feels like forever when I’m thinking about you.”

After the call ended, Rio sat in silence for a few minutes, lost in thought. As much as she missed Agatha, hearing her voice, even through the phone, was a balm to her soul. She knew that no matter how hard this distance was, Agatha’s commitment to their relationship was clear.

But the loneliness was real. Rio found herself turning to Agatha’s Snap stories in the quiet moments, watching Agatha’s life unfold in a way she could only observe. She would scroll through the posts, often replaying them, each one a reminder of the beautiful woman who had changed her life.

One morning, Agatha posted a story of herself enjoying a simple breakfast outside a café, the Italian sun shining down on her. Mornings in Italy but miss my person she wrote, a hint of sadness in the message. Rio, feeling the weight of the distance between them, replied immediately: I wish I could get there. But we’ll make new memories when you’re back. I promise.

She sat there for a while, her phone in her hands, just thinking about Agatha. Despite the miles between them, Rio couldn’t shake the feeling that their bond was growing stronger, even through the screen. Agatha had a way of making Rio feel special, even from afar.

At night, when Rio got into bed, she would send Agatha goodnight snaps. They’d sometimes be goofy, sometimes sweet—like one where Rio was holding up a ridiculous stuffed bear and saying, “I got you a souvenir from the flower shop!” Agatha would reply with a snap of her own, showing a stuffed dog that she had picked up for Remi, adding, “Got Remi one too! But don’t get jealous.”

It wasn’t perfect. It wasn’t what they both wanted, but it was enough. It had to be enough for now. And somehow, Rio felt like Agatha’s promise—that they would make it through this time apart—was something she could hold onto.

As the days wore on, Rio found herself anxiously awaiting the nightly phone calls, the moments of connection that kept her grounded. And slowly, she came to realize that distance, no matter how far, couldn’t break the bond they were building.

Chapter 27

It had been a month since Agatha had left for filming, and Rio had gotten used to the quiet mornings without her. Agatha’s Snap stories, full of the stunning Italian coastline and behind-the-scenes moments from her set, had become Rio’s daily dose of joy. She loved seeing Remi frolicking in the sand, and Agatha, who had gotten a beautiful sun-kissed tan, looked more relaxed than Rio had ever seen her.

On one particular morning, Agatha posted a video of herself lounging on the beach, Remi happily rolling around in the sand beside her. She was wearing a wide-brimmed hat, sunglasses perched on her nose, and a warm smile on her face.

“You’re really missing out, Rio. I think you’d like this beach, but I guess I’ll save it for when you’re here. Remi's having the best time though.”* Her voice was lighthearted and carefree. Rio smiled, watching the video multiple times and sending a quick reply.

Rio: I can’t wait to come visit you. The beach looks amazing. I wish I was there with you both.

Rio was still feeling the ache of missing her but was doing her best to stay occupied with work and her daily routine. The shop had kept her busy, and she loved the calming scent of flowers that surrounded her during the day. But as much as she enjoyed her work, her thoughts were still consumed by Agatha and the distance between them.

However, the quiet routine Rio had settled into was abruptly interrupted when she caught sight of the tabloids at the coffee shop on her way to work one morning. Her stomach dropped when she saw the headline: Is Agatha’s New Relationship on the Rocks? Sources Suggest Rio and Agatha Have Split!

There was a picture of Rio, taken when she was on her way to work—her face scrunched in concentration, brows furrowed, and her posture slightly hunched as she walked, looking tired and preoccupied. The image made her look like she was going through something, and the tabloid had twisted it into a narrative that didn’t match reality. Beneath the photo was the article, full of speculation and rumors about their relationship. The tabloid questioned whether Rio’s ‘moodiness’ was a sign that things were falling apart with Agatha, feeding the public’s hunger for drama.

Rio froze, holding the paper in her hands, her heart sinking into her stomach. She couldn’t understand how something so mundane could be twisted into a headline like that. She quickly discarded the paper in a nearby trash bin, feeling her chest tighten with anxiety. She hadn’t said anything to Agatha about the rumors, but now she was sure they’d reach her sooner or later. The last thing she wanted was for Agatha to see that nonsense about them. It made her feel exposed, vulnerable, and helpless.

She couldn’t keep it to herself. So, she grabbed her phone, opening Snapchat and sending Agatha a quick message.

Rio: Hey, I don’t know if you’ve seen it, but there’s a rumor in the tabloids saying we’ve split... thanks for telling me lol. Just ignore it if you see it.

Her thumb hovered over the send button, her fingers trembling slightly as she tapped it and sent the message.

Within minutes, Agatha’s reply came through.

Agatha: I haven’t seen it yet, but I don’t care what they say. I know what we have. It’s just noise. Don’t let it get to you, okay? I miss you like crazy

Rio’s heart swelled at Agatha’s words, the reassurance washing over her.

Rio: I miss you too... a lot. I just feel kind of weird about it all, you know? They’ve got my picture and made it look like I’m miserable

Rio sent a photo back of herself standing in her shop, holding a bouquet of flowers and smiling.

Caption: This is me today, okay? Not miserable

Agatha responded almost immediately.

Agatha: I know you’re not miserable. I see you every day in my heart. Don’t let some weird tabloid mess with your head. It’s just the press trying to create drama where there isn’t any

Rio took a deep breath, feeling the weight lift slightly off her shoulders. She typed back.

Rio: You’re right. I know you’d never do that to me. I just don’t want the world getting involved in our relationship. It feels... invasive

Agatha’s reply was simple but heartfelt.

Agatha: I understand. It’s hard, I know. But we’re stronger than that. We’re good, Rio. I promise. I love you

There was a voice note attached to the message, and when Rio played it, she heard Agatha’s voice, low and soothing. “Don’t let them take away our peace. You’re mine, and I’m yours. That’s all that matters, love you sweetheart.”

Rio felt a wave of warmth spread through her at her words. It made the tabloids feel small and insignificant, like they didn’t even deserve a second thought. But still, the emotional toll was there. Rio had been living a quieter life before Agatha, and now, suddenly, she was thrust into the public eye.

And though she loved Agatha, the attention that came with their relationship was overwhelming.

Later that evening, Agatha sent a snap of herself on set in a beautiful Italian villa, with Remi in the background, playing in the garden. *“You’d love this place. Remi's already found the best napping spots. How’s your day been?”

Rio responded, feeling more connected to Agatha than ever.

Rio: Busy, but I’ve been thinking about you a lot today. Miss you more than I can say.

Her heart skipped a beat as she saw Agatha’s reply.

Agatha: I miss you too. Can’t wait for this shoot to be over so I can be with you again. It’s not the same without you here

Rio’s phone buzzed with another message. It was a message from Alice.

Alice: Girl, don’t stress over that tabloid nonsense. You and Agatha are solid. She’s got your bac

Rio chuckled at the message, feeling a little better. She snapped a picture of herself holding up her phone with a peace sign and sent it to Agatha.

Caption: Getting through the chaos with you in my corner

Agatha’s reply was quick.

Agatha: Always, sweetheart. You and me against the world.

Despite the tabloids, despite the chaos, Rio felt grounded in Agatha’s words. She realized then that it didn’t matter what anyone else thought. Their relationship was real, and no amount of rumors or paparazzi could change that. It was just her and Agatha, and nothing else mattered.

A few days after the tabloid rumors about Rio and Agatha started circulating, the media frenzy seemed to intensify. It wasn’t just the paparazzi anymore; talk shows, gossip blogs, and even interviews with Agatha's co-stars began to touch on the subject of her relationship. But this time, it wasn’t Agatha speaking out about the rumors—it was Bucky.

Bucky had his own talk show appearance coming up, and Rio was sitting in her apartment when she saw a snippet from the show flash across her feed. The headline read: Bucky Defends Agatha’s Relationship with Rio: ‘She’s Head Over Heels!’

Rio felt a knot form in her stomach. She clicked on the clip and started watching.

On screen, Bucky was seated comfortably in the talk show’s plush chair, laughing and chatting with the host, a friendly older woman who had a reputation for being blunt.

Host: “So, Bucky, let’s talk about your friends. We’ve seen Agatha looking absolutely head over heels for her girlfriend, Rio. But recently, there have been rumors swirling about them—rumors that suggest they might have split. You’ve known Agatha for years now, so what’s really going on?”

Bucky’s face dropped into something more serious, a shift that had the audience quieting down.

Bucky: “Rumors are exactly that—rumors. I mean, come on. You know how tabloids work, right? They create drama where there isn’t any. Of course Rio looked miserable in that picture. You’d be miserable too if your girlfriend, who you’re head over heels for, was filming abroad for months on end. I’m also miserable. Our favorite girl is in Italy right now, and we miss her like crazy. But, I’ll tell you this—Agatha is crazy about Rio. They’re not breaking up. If anything, they’re stronger than ever.”

The host raised an eyebrow, clearly amused by Bucky’s sincerity.

Host: “But you’re saying it’s just the distance making things look worse than they are?”

Bucky nodded vigorously, leaning forward in his chair.

Bucky: “Exactly. I’ve known Agatha for years, and let me tell you, she’s never been like this with anyone. I’ve seen her with other people, and it was never this serious. She talks about Rio all the time, she adores her. And Rio? She’s just as into Agatha as Agatha is into her. Sure, the distance is tough, but it’s temporary. Trust me, when Agatha comes back, you’ll see it in person—the connection they have is undeniable. They’re solid.”

Rio’s heart fluttered as she listened to Bucky’s words. It was so reassuring to hear him speak so highly of her and Agatha. She didn’t realize until then how much she needed someone to have her back in this mess. It wasn’t just Agatha’s voice she wanted to hear; Bucky, who knew Agatha so well, was validating their relationship in a way that made her feel less alone.

She quickly grabbed her phone, snapping Bucky a message on Snapchat.

Rio: You have no idea how much that means to me. Seriously, thank you. It’s been tough, but hearing you say that really helped

Bucky’s response came almost immediately, his familiar sense of humor coming through despite the serious topic.

Bucky: Of course, I’ve got your back. Agatha’s head over heels for you, and anyone who thinks otherwise is a damn fool. Besides, if anyone’s miserable around here, it’s me. I’m stuck with no Agatha to pester. So, yeah, I’m definitely feeling the absence too. 😅

Rio laughed softly, feeling a warmth in her chest. She quickly typed back.

Rio: It’s been a long month. Agatha’s not here, and it feels like everything’s just off. I miss her so much

Bucky: I know, it’s hard. But you’re doing great, Rio. Agatha’s not going anywhere, and neither am I. And hey, once she’s back, we’ll throw a welcome home party and I’ll make sure you both are properly celebrated, alright?

Rio smiled, feeling more grounded in her own heartache.

Rio: Thanks, Bucky. You’re really making this whole thing easier. I needed to hear that today.

Bucky: Anytime. And listen, if the tabloids keep messing with you, just let me know. I’ll take care of them, too. No one messes with Agatha and Rio on my watch. Got it?

Rio couldn’t help but laugh at how fierce Bucky was. She felt so much more at ease knowing she had him on her side.

Rio: You’re a good friend, Bucky. Really appreciate you. We need to all hang out when she’s back—Remi too.

Bucky: Remi’s got her own fan club now, so don’t be surprised when she demands a treat every five minutes. But I’m all in on the hangout, as long as I get to see you two making out like a couple of lovebirds in front of me. Kidding. Or am I? 😜

Rio giggled, feeling a little lighter after the conversation.

Rio: Yeah, no kissing in front of you, thanks! 😂 I’ll pass on that.

Bucky: Alright, alright. But when she gets back, we’re having a proper catch-up, okay? You, me, Agatha, Remi and Senor Scratchy. I’ll bring the margaritas

Rio: Deal. And again, thank you for everything. You really helped today.

Bucky: Always. Can’t wait to see you soon

As Rio put down her phone, she felt an overwhelming sense of relief. Hearing Bucky speak so confidently about her and Agatha was exactly what she needed. It made her believe in their relationship again, reminded her that no matter how difficult the situation seemed, Agatha cared for her deeply, and so did the people closest to them.

She sent Agatha a quick message after chatting with Bucky.

Rio: I heard what Bucky said on his talk show. I love that you have such amazing friends in your life. I miss you so much. Can’t wait to see you again soon.

Agatha’s reply came almost instantly.

Agatha: I miss you more than words can say, Rio. We’ll be together soon. Don’t let the tabloids get to you. Just hold on for a little while longer. I promise, it’ll be worth it.

Rio smiled at her phone, feeling a renewed sense of connection despite the distance. The wait wasn’t easy, but it was more than manageable knowing that Agatha and Bucky were in her corner.

Chapter 28

A few days after their heart-to-heart conversations, Rio was back to her routine. Work was busy with wedding season still in full swing, but the longing for Agatha never really faded. Each day, she would check her Snapchat for updates from Agatha, smiling at her posts, watching her adventures in Spain unfold. The distance was hard, but Agatha had been reassuring her in every way possible—nightly calls, sweet messages, and even the occasional unexpected snap of her laughing with Remi or soaking up the sun.

One evening, Rio was wrapping up her day at the shop, arranging flowers for an event, when her phone buzzed with a notification. She picked it up, expecting it to be a message from Alice or a reminder about a wedding. But when she opened the notification, her heart skipped a beat.

It was a Snapchat from Agatha.

Agatha: I miss you so much. I’ve been thinking about you constantly. So, I’ve made a decision…

Rio’s heart raced as she opened the snap. It was a picture of Agatha sitting in a chic, sunlit café, a playful smile on her lips. In her hand was an envelope with her name written on it.

Caption: I know how much we’ve both been missing each other. So I did something a little crazy… I’ve got a surprise for you. Check your email in 10 minutes

Rio blinked, completely caught off guard. She stared at the snap for a few moments, replaying it over and over in her mind. Her emotions were a mixture of excitement and confusion. What was Agatha up to? What surprise? She’d never expected Agatha to do something like this. Her heart pounded as she quickly switched to her email app, awaiting the mysterious message.

Ten minutes later, she received an email notification from Agatha, subject line: A Surprise for You.

Rio’s fingers trembled as she opened it.

Inside the email was a PDF attachment, and the moment she opened it, her breath caught in her throat. It was a plane ticket—an all-expenses-paid round trip to Spain for the next week.

The email itself read:

Rio, I can’t stand being away from you any longer. I’ve taken the liberty of booking you a ticket to come out here for a week. You deserve a break, and I want us to have the time we’ve been missing. I’ll be here waiting. I know it’s short notice, but I hope you can take a little time off and come. I want to show you Spain, show you a piece of my life here. I can’t wait to have you with me. Love, Agatha.

Rio felt a rush of emotion hit her all at once. She stared at the screen in disbelief. Agatha was flying her out to Spain. The thought of being with Agatha, exploring Spain, and just being in her arms again made her giddy with excitement. But then doubt crept in. Could she really leave her shop for a week? Would it be too much?

Before Rio could overthink it, her phone buzzed again—another Snapchat from Agatha.

Agatha: Don’t think about it too much. You’ve been working so hard. You deserve this, and I want you here. You’re the most important thing right now. Just say yes, please.

Rio’s heart melted as she read Agatha’s words. She felt her anxieties melt away. Agatha was so sure, so kind, and so determined to make this happen. Rio could feel her affection in every message, every gesture, and it was impossible to resist.

Rio quickly replied on Snapchat, her fingers flying across the screen.

Rio: You’re insane! But… I can’t say no. I’ll be there. I can’t wait to see you. You’ve seriously outdone yourself, Agatha. I’m so lucky to have you.

Agatha’s response was immediate.

Agatha: I’m the lucky one. I’ll be waiting at the airport when you land. See you soon, my love.

Rio felt a surge of joy and excitement that she couldn’t contain. She called Alice immediately, her voice trembling with happiness.

“Alice! You won’t believe this,” Rio exclaimed. “Agatha just booked me a ticket to Spain! I’m going to see her in two days! I can’t believe it.”

Alice’s voice was full of laughter. “I told you she was crazy about you! That’s so sweet of her. Honestly, you two are giving me all the feels. I hope you’re ready for some serious romantic adventures in Spain!”

Rio couldn’t stop smiling, feeling giddy. “I know, right? I just… I can’t believe she did this. I feel like I’m dreaming. But I’m also nervous, I haven’t traveled like this in ages.”

Alice chuckled. “You’ll be fine. Just enjoy every second of it. She’s your person, Rio. Go and have fun with her.”

After hanging up with Alice, Rio spent the next hour packing. She’d never traveled so spontaneously before, and her mind raced with a hundred thoughts. What should she wear? How was she supposed to act in front of Agatha’s world in Spain? She took a deep breath and reminded herself that Agatha wanted this. She wanted to be with her. Everything would be fine.

The day of her flight, Rio made her way to the airport. Her stomach fluttered with excitement and nerves. She had a good feeling about this trip. It felt like the start of something special, and maybe even the next chapter in their relationship.

As her flight landed in Spain, Rio’s heart raced. She followed the signs for arrivals, scanning the crowd. And then, she saw Agatha.

She looked stunning—radiant, relaxed, and so effortlessly beautiful. She was waiting at the exit with a sign that read “Mi amor."

Rio felt tears prick at her eyes as she walked toward her, and Agatha’s face lit up as she caught sight of her.

“Rio!” Agatha exclaimed, rushing forward and pulling her into a tight embrace.

Rio hugged her back, the world around them fading away. She was finally with Agatha again, and it felt like everything was exactly where it was supposed to be.

“I can’t believe I’m here,” Rio murmured against Agatha’s shoulder. “You’re real. This is real.”

Agatha pulled back slightly, cupping Rio’s face with her hands. “You’re here, and that’s all that matters. Welcome to Spain, my love. Let’s make the most of this week.”

Rio smiled, tears threatening to spill over, but she was too happy to care. She was here, and Agatha was everything she could have dreamed of.

The week ahead promised to be full of adventure, passion, and the kind of connection they had both been longing for. As they walked out into the warm Spanish night, Rio couldn’t help but feel like her life was beginning to fall into place, and it was all because Agatha had decided to bring her along for the ride.

As Rio and Agatha spent the week in Spain, their Snapchat stories became a window into their shared adventure. Agatha had prepared an itinerary of romantic and fun excursions, and Rio couldn’t have been more excited. The days were filled with exploring the picturesque streets of Barcelona, sunbathing by the Mediterranean, and indulging in delicious tapas. Agatha’s Snapchat was constantly updating, each post more beautiful than the last, capturing the stunning landscapes, their laughter, and the undeniable chemistry between them.

Snap : Hola from Barcelona!

A video of Agatha and Rio walking hand-in-hand down La Rambla, the lively street lined with shops and performers. Agatha’s smile was radiant, her sunglasses perched atop her head. Rio, a few steps behind her, was beaming, her face flushed from the warmth of the sun. Agatha playfully panned the camera over the crowds of tourists and street performers, the iconic architecture of Gaudí’s buildings just visible in the distance.

Snap : I brought my girl to Park Güell

A picture of them sitting on the colorful mosaic bench, overlooking the city. Rio had her arms wrapped around Agatha’s waist, their faces close together, enjoying the warmth of the sun and each other’s company.

Caption: She’s breathtaking—inside and out. 💛

Snap: Fell in love with Barcelona.

A video from the top of Montjuïc, showing the stunning panoramic views of the city and the Mediterranean Sea. The two were laughing, with Agatha’s arm around Rio’s shoulders. Rio, a little nervous but giddy, gave the camera a quick wave.

The next day, the pair headed out to explore more cultural spots.

Snap: Got lost in the history of the Gothic Quarter!

A picture of Rio and Agatha standing in front of the Barcelona Cathedral, the intricate gothic architecture towering behind them. Rio snapped a shot of Agatha smiling brightly as she spun in the street, laughing at how confused they both had been about directions. Rio’s hair was slightly tousled, her cheeks pink from the summer heat.

Snap: And now we’re eating all the tapas, because why not?

A video of Rio trying to navigate a plate of patatas bravas, giggling as she failed to get a perfect bite without spilling the sauce everywhere. Agatha laughed alongside her, snapping a quick shot of Rio’s messy face.

Rio wiped her chin and mock-gasped. “I don’t think I’m cut out for tapas…” Agatha’s voice rang out in the background, “You’re cute, don’t worry about it.”

Snap: Winding down at the beach 🏖️

A serene photo of them on a private beach, the turquoise waves gently rolling in. Agatha was lying on her back with her sunglasses on, while Rio rested on her stomach, her head nestled into Agatha’s chest. The sun was setting behind them, casting a golden glow over everything. Rio posted it on her own Snapchat too.

Caption: Here. With her. ❤️

Rio’s Snapchat Story was also filled with her time in Spain.

A photo of Rio smiling shyly in front of the famous La Sagrada Familia. Agatha had managed to capture Rio with the grand church in the background, and the sunlight made Rio’s hair almost glow. The way Agatha had taken the shot made Rio feel like she was a part of something magical.

Rio tagged Agathas public instagram in the post, captioning it: *“I’m so in awe of everything here. And her. 💖

Snap: Woke up to this view this morning 😍

A video showing the view from the hotel balcony—endless blue sky, sun shimmering over the rooftops of Barcelona. Agatha’s laugh could be heard as she called out to Rio, who had clearly just woken up, her messy hair and sleepy eyes a stark contrast to the picture-perfect surroundings. Rio snapped Agatha as she leaned out over the balcony, her hair blowing in the wind.

Snap: I can’t get enough of these churros.

A video showing Rio taking a bite of the churros, dipping it into chocolate sauce while Agatha encouraged her to “live her best life.” The video ended with Rio laughing, her face covered in chocolate and Agatha playfully wiping her face with a napkin. Rio could hear her voice, “Why does it always end up like this with you?”

As the week went on, the pair took a trip to the southern coast of Spain to explore Seville and Marbella. Their Snapchat stories chronicled their visits to ancient ruins, Roman baths, and cozy local markets. Each snap radiated their joy, their undeniable connection growing stronger by the day.

But, just as they were finally settling into their vacation bliss, the paparazzi caught wind of their whirlwind holiday.

One afternoon, while Agatha and Rio were walking hand in hand through a bustling market in Seville, they were surrounded by flashing cameras. The papparazzi had somehow found them in the crowd, and before either of them could react, the photos were taken.

She was quick to post a photo of her and Rio laughing amidst the chaos of the paparazzi to her own snapchat.

Caption: Guess they finally found us... 😅

Rio, still trying to process the sudden invasion of their privacy, snapped a selfie of her wide-eyed face to her own snapchat.

Caption: Not how I imagined this day going... but, here we are

The next morning, after the flash of cameras died down, Agatha and Rio decided to take a moment for themselves. They went for a walk in the countryside just outside Marbella, where the view of rolling hills and vineyards was peaceful and serene. Rio couldn’t help but feel both excited and overwhelmed by the situation. She was just a small-town florist, trying to navigate the whirlwind of Agatha’s world.

But Agatha, sensing Rio’s nerves, took her hand and whispered, “Don’t worry about them. This is our time, not theirs.”

They posted more photos, this time on a quiet vineyard tour. Agatha posted a photo of her and Rio with glasses of wine, their faces radiating happiness. The caption was simple: Here’s to us. 🍷❤️

Despite the paparazzi chaos, the pair found solace in each other’s company. Agatha, protective and loving, made sure Rio felt at ease, reminding her that their connection was more important than the cameras flashing around them. And for Rio, it was clear: this was a moment in time that she would cherish forever. Even though the world was watching, Agatha made sure she felt like the only person in it.

Chapter 29

Rio sat at her kitchen table, the early morning light spilling over her counter as she absentmindedly stirred her coffee. It had been ten long weeks since Agatha had left to start filming. Three weeks since she visited, so three weeks of solitary mornings, awkward nights alone, and an aching emptiness that she couldn’t shake. The reality of Agatha’s absence had hit harder than Rio expected. She’d known the job would take Agatha away for long stretches, but now that the days without her were piling up, it was much harder to deal with than she had thought. Especially after spending a week connecting emotionally and physically in Spain.

She picked up her phone, scrolling through Agatha's Snapchat stories for the hundredth time that day.

It was a strange kind of comfort to see Agatha’s smiling face, to feel connected to her even from miles away. Today, Agatha was wrapping up filming in Spain before heading off to Japan. Rio smiled as she watched Agatha in her stories, a few behind-the-scenes glimpses of a quiet moment where she was sitting with the crew, sipping coffee and looking effortlessly stunning.

Rio’s phone vibrated in her hand, and she glanced down to see a new snap chat from Agatha. She eagerly opened it, feeling a flutter of excitement in her chest.

Agatha: Last day in Spain! Gonna miss this place... but I can’t wait to get to Japan. It’s all going so fast, and I feel like I haven’t seen you in forever even though its only been three weeks. Miss you, sweetheart ❤️

Rio’s heart did a little flip at the words. She quickly typed back a response, not wanting to keep Agatha waiting.

Rio: I miss you so much, I don’t even know how to deal with it. Everything here feels so empty without you. Hope you enjoy Japan, but please, come back soon

She hit send and immediately felt a wave of longing. Ten weeks had felt like a lifetime, and even though they kept in touch through their personal snaps, facetime and calls, it wasn’t the same as having Agatha there with her.

Rio couldn’t help but feel a little disconnected sometimes, watching Agatha’s glamorous life through her stories, feeling like an outsider in this whirlwind world. Agatha’s snap had been lighthearted, but Rio could sense the underlying exhaustion in her words. Agatha was working non-stop, traveling across the globe, always under pressure, but she made the effort to check in every night, even when the time difference between them was a challenge.

As she scrolled through her Snapchat feed, Rio saw more behind-the-scenes snaps of Agatha in Spain. There was one of her walking with her arm around the director, another of her on set, laughing with the crew. Agatha looked so radiant, her usual confidence shining through despite the exhaustion in her eyes. But Rio knew the reality—Agatha missed her too, even if she didn’t say it every time.

Agatha: I think it's going to be my last stop for a while before I head back to the states. Counting the days until I see you again

Rio’s heart swelled. The thought of Agatha returning to the States was a beacon of light in the fog of missing her. The idea of having her close again, the anticipation of feeling her arms around her, made Rio's chest ache with longing. It felt like Agatha had been a thousand miles away for far too long, and even though they stayed in contact, it just wasn’t the same.

She quickly typed out a message to Agatha, wanting her to know how much she meant to her.

Rio: You’re everything to me, you know that? I can’t wait for you to come home. It’s so hard without you here. But I’m proud of everything you’re doing. Can’t wait to hear all about Japan when you get there ❤️

Before hitting send, she added a little emoji of a heart, something small to show Agatha how deeply she felt.

Rio paused for a moment, staring at her phone. She missed Agatha’s voice, the little inside jokes they shared, the way Agatha always made her feel seen. It wasn’t just the physical presence that was missing—it was the way Agatha made her life feel whole.

The thought of spending more time apart was overwhelming, but Rio was determined to be strong, to support Agatha in her career. That’s what love was, after all—sacrifice, patience, and belief in each other’s dreams.

As she sent the message, she felt the familiar twinge of excitement when Agatha replied almost immediately.

Agatha: Japan’s going to be crazy, but I’ll be thinking of you the whole time. I’ll text you tonight when I land. Promise. Miss you more than you know

Rio could practically hear Agatha’s voice in her head, and the tenderness in her words made her stomach flip. It was crazy how much she could miss someone, even when they were so far away. They’d only been together a few months, but Rio felt like she’d known Agatha forever.

A wave of nostalgia and longing washed over her, and she leaned back in her chair, closing her eyes for a moment, imagining what it would be like when they could finally be together again, without the interruptions of travel and work. The thought was enough to give her the strength to keep going through her day, even if it felt like a huge chunk of her heart was on the other side of the world.

Later that day, as Rio was cleaning up her shop, she found herself scrolling through more of Agatha’s stories. She watched as Agatha walked along the cobblestone streets of Seville, a beautiful red dress fluttering in the breeze. Then there was a snap of her on set with the director, a warm smile playing on her lips. She looked like she was thriving. But Rio could tell there was a certain weariness in her eyes, a weariness that came from being apart from someone she loved.

Rio sighed softly, her fingers lingering on the screen as she stared at Agatha. She missed her so much.

The phone buzzed in her hand again, and Rio saw Agatha’s name pop up on her screen.

Agatha: Just landed in Japan. I’m going to miss Spain, but I’m so ready for this next chapter. You’re on my mind the whole time, Rio. Let’s do something special when I get back. I’ll make sure we have all the time we need

Rio felt a warmth spread through her chest. Her heart swelled as she read the message. It was clear Agatha was as eager to be with her as she was to see her again. And with that, Rio made a silent promise to herself that she’d wait—wait for Agatha, for their future together, no matter how long the distance stretched between them. She was ready for the next chapter, and she would be there, waiting for Agatha’s return, every step of the way.

Rio had spent the next month counting the days, each one feeling like it dragged on a little longer than the last. The moment Agatha landed back in the States was a huge relief for her.

It had been over a month since they were in the same time zone, let alone in the same room. Rio could hardly believe it. She’d been waiting for this moment, but now that it was here, her emotions were overwhelming.

She was standing in Agathas living room, fiddling with the hem of her sweater, pacing back and forth with excitement. She’d missed Agatha so much, it felt like the very air around her was electric with anticipation.

But it wasn’t just Agatha she’d missed. The days without Remi and Señor Scratchy had felt long, too. It had been quiet without the sound of Remi’s excited barking or the comfort of Scratchy’s quiet presence. She’d grown used to them in a way that surprised her.

A car door slammed shut. Rio’s heart skipped a beat, her nerves turning into pure excitement. She opened the door and there stood Agatha, with her signature smile, looking effortlessly beautiful.

“Hey,” Agatha said, a playful twinkle in her eye. “I’ve been dying to see you.”

Rio felt her heart race, her stomach flipping in a way that made her feel like she was fifteen again, having her first crush. She didn’t even think twice. She stepped forward, her arms opening wide, and Agatha didn’t hesitate. Before Rio could even say a word, Agatha was there, her arms wrapping around her waist, pulling her in so tightly that Rio could feel her warmth all over.

“Oh my god, I missed you so much,” Agatha said, her voice muffled against Rio’s shoulder.

Rio couldn’t help herself. She jumped, wrapping her legs around Agatha’s waist and holding onto her like she never wanted to let go. Agatha let out a small laugh, adjusting to hold Rio even closer. It felt so natural, like they had never been apart. Rio felt like she could stay like this forever, basking in the feeling of having Agatha in her arms again.

“I missed you too,” Rio said, her voice thick with emotion. “More than you’ll ever know.”

Agatha chuckled, her hands gently stroking Rio’s back. “I swear, I was counting down the days until I could see you again. You’re everything to me, I love you, Rio.”

Rio pulled back just enough to look at Agatha’s face, her eyes scanning her features, noting how Agatha’s face had softened, how her hair was slightly longer, and the little laugh lines around her eyes that appeared when she smiled. It was like she had never left. She was the same Agatha—the same woman Rio had fallen for.

And yet, there was something even more special about seeing her right here, right now.

“I love you too. I’ve missed everything about you,” Rio said softly, before leaning in and kissing Agatha gently.

The kiss was slow at first, just a soft brushing of lips, but it quickly deepened as Agatha’s hands cupped Rio’s face. The familiar taste of Agatha, the feeling of her lips, it was all too much for Rio. She wanted to stay lost in this moment, but the reality of the time apart still hung in the air, making her want to savor every second.

Agatha pulled back first, breathless. “I have a surprise for you.”

Rio raised an eyebrow, curious. “A surprise?”

Agatha smiled, her eyes gleaming. “You’ll see.”

Agatha gently set Rio down and then grabbed her hand, leading her into the living room before going back outside. She returned withRemi, jumping up and down excitedly, tail wagging, and Señor Scratchy, perched on the arm of the couch with that familiar, lazy look. Both were so excited to see her, as if they, too, knew they were finally home.

Rio's heart melted. “Remi! Señor Scratchy!” she exclaimed, crouching down to give them both love.

Remi practically leaped into her arms, and Rio couldn’t help but laugh at the excitement. “I missed you two too,” she whispered, scratching behind Remi’s ears and giving Scratchy a soft pet on his head.

Agatha stood back, watching the scene unfold, a soft smile on her face. “We’ve missed you so much.”

“I love you,” Rio said, looking up at Agatha with an expression that was full of awe and warmth.

Agatha walked up to her, gently cupping her face in her hands. “I love you too, Rio. More than anything.”

The moment felt so right. The long distance, the days spent apart—it was all worth it for this. The way Rio felt in Agatha’s arms, the way everything seemed to fall back into place with the simple act of holding hands, being together, it was like no time had passed at all.

Remi barked excitedly, breaking the spell of the moment, and Rio couldn’t help but laugh. She gave the dog another quick kiss on the head, then stood and turned to Agatha. “You’re finally here,” she said softly.

“I’m here,” Agatha replied with a grin, leaning in to kiss Rio once more. This time, the kiss was full of the heat that had built over the past weeks—the kind of kiss that made the world fall away. For those few seconds, it was just the two of them, no distance, no time zones, just the pure connection they shared.

“I’m so happy you’re back,” Rio whispered when they broke apart. “I’ve missed you so much.”

Agatha smiled, her eyes softening with affection. “I’m not going anywhere anytime soon, I promise.”

Rio leaned her forehead against Agatha’s, her heart full of love and relief. “Good,” she whispered. “I don’t think I could stand being apart from you any longer.”

“I’ll never make you go through that again,” Agatha said with a playful grin, her fingers brushing through Rio’s hair.

The world outside might be busy and loud, but in that moment, as they stood together in the comfort of their shared space, Rio felt like she had everything she could ever need.

Chapter 30

The next morning, after an intimate breakfast in bed with cups of fresh coffee, Agatha told Rio that she had arranged a lunch with her mother, Lilia, who was eager to see her. Rio, still somewhat nervous from the whirlwind of emotions the past few weeks had caused, smiled but couldn’t shake the butterflies in her stomach.

They arrived at Lilia’s house, a cozy, whimsical home with sprawling gardens, lots of mismatched furniture, and trinkets that told stories. As soon as they stepped inside, Rio was met with the scent of lavender and citrus, and before she could even catch her breath, Lilia appeared in the doorway.

The second she saw Rio, she embraced her like an old friend, as though the two had known each other for years rather than the singular impromptu meeting over midnight margaritas.

“Oh darling, it’s so wonderful to see you again!” Lilia exclaimed, pulling back and holding Rio at arm’s length, her eyes scanning her face as if she were searching for something. “Agatha doesn’t stop talking about you, you’re perfect for her.”

Rio smiled, feeling a little awkward but grateful for Lilia’s openheartedness. Agatha stood by with a playful smirk on her face, clearly amused by the exchange.

“I’m happy to see you again too, Lilia,” Rio replied, feeling herself relax under Lilia's warm gaze. “I’ve heard so much about you.”

Lilia’s eyes twinkled. “I’m sure you have, darling. Now, let’s sit down and I’ll tell you all about how I met Agatha when she was just a little thing. You’ll love these stories.”

The three of them sat down at the dining table, and Lilia immediately launched into her storytelling.

“Agatha was always a stubborn one,” Lilia began, her voice full of affection as she looked at her daughter. “When she was five, she walked right up to me in the park, grabbed my hand, and declared, ‘You’re going to be my mom.’ I hadn’t even met her before!” Lilia chuckled, her eyes softening as she glanced over at Agatha, who was trying to hide her embarrassment.

“I didn’t believe in waiting for things to come to me, Mom,” Agatha said, rolling her eyes but clearly amused. “I figured, why not take matters into my own hands?”

Lilia continued, “I remember thinking, ‘What am I supposed to do with a child?’ But she was so full of life, so sure of herself, that I couldn’t say no. I ended up taking her out for ice cream, and from that day on, we were inseparable.”

Rio couldn’t help but smile, completely enchanted by the story. She could see so much of the confident, driven woman that Agatha had become in that little five-year-old, and the bond between them was undeniable.

“So, you decided to adopt her on the spot?” Rio asked, amazed.

Lilia nodded. “It was the craziest decision I ever made, and one of the best. She was always meant to be my daughter. I’ve never been able to imagine life without her. And look at her now,” Lilia said with pride, glancing toward Agatha, “still as determined as ever.”

Agatha groaned in mock annoyance. “I think I might’ve inherited that from you, Mom.”

Lilia winked. “Well, I do have my own brand of stubbornness. But you, Agatha, you’ve always known exactly what you wanted. Even when you were a little girl.”

As Lilia continued sharing anecdotes from Agatha’s childhood, Rio felt her heart swell. The more she learned about Agatha’s past, the more she understood the woman she loved. She could see why Agatha was so driven, so independent, and so full of love despite the obstacles she had faced. It was clear that Lilia had played a huge part in shaping Agatha into the person she was.

At one point, Lilia leaned in toward Rio and lowered her voice. “Agatha doesn’t always show it, but she really cares about you. She’s been a little, how do I say this, emotionally reserved to other people, since I’ve known her, but the way she talks about you? Darling, it’s as though she’s found someone who understands her completely.”

Rio felt her cheeks flush at the compliment. She looked over at Agatha, who had her head down, a slight blush on her cheeks as she quietly stirred her drink.

“I feel the same way,” Rio confessed. “I’ve never met anyone like Agatha. She’s just…” Rio trailed off, searching for the right words.

“Extraordinary?” Lilia finished for her, raising an eyebrow.

Rio smiled, nodding. “Yes. Exactly.”

Lilia gave a satisfied nod and patted Rio’s hand gently. “Well, I’m glad you two found each other. It’s about time someone could keep up with my daughter’s energy.”

The rest of the afternoon passed with lighthearted conversation and laughter. Agatha and Rio shared glances that spoke volumes—though they hadn’t said it yet, they both knew they were building something special. As the sun began to set and they prepared to leave, Lilia gave them both a long, tight hug.

“I’m so glad you came by, Rio. Don’t be a stranger. And take care of my girl, alright?”

Rio nodded, her heart full. “I will, I promise.”

As they left Lilia’s house, Agatha took Rio’s hand, her grip tight and comforting. “I’m so glad you’re here with me, Rio,” she said softly.

“Me too,” Rio replied, leaning in to kiss Agatha’s cheek.

The open love between them was new, still growing, but Rio knew in that moment that whatever they had would be something lasting. Something worth fighting for.

The press tour for Agatha's film was in full swing, and the media was buzzing with excitement over her return to the big screen. Everywhere she went, cameras flashed, fans cheered, and reporters eagerly waited to ask her questions about her latest role. But it wasn’t just her acting career that had captured the world’s attention—Agatha’s relationship with Rio was now front and center in the tabloids and social media.

The couple had been quiet about their relationship, only sharing glimpses of their life together through their private social media accounts to friends and family. The public images were all taken by tabloids.

Still, fans and journalists alike had taken notice of the way they looked at each other, the obvious affection in their movements, and the playful comments exchanged between them.

As Agatha sat in a plush studio, preparing for the latest round of interviews, she could feel the nerves crawling up her spine. It had been a whirlwind few weeks, juggling her career, the press tour, and trying to stay connected with Rio, who had been busier with her shop and personal life. The last few weeks had been hard, the distance between them growing as Agatha was swept into the chaos of the tour. But tonight, she was going to be asked about Rio again, there was no question about that. And she was ready for it. Or so she thought.

The interviewer, a friendly woman in her early thirties, adjusted her microphone and smiled brightly as she introduced the segment. "Agatha, it's wonderful to have you here today. Your new film is already getting rave reviews, and the world is so excited to see you back on screen. But, of course, we can’t ignore the growing interest in your personal life. You've been quite open about your relationship with Rio, and we love seeing how happy you two are together. So, let me ask you this: have you ever thought about the future with Rio? Do you ever see yourself getting married and starting a family one day?"

The room went silent for a split second, and Agatha’s heart skipped. She wasn’t expecting the question to come up so directly. It was as if the interviewer had read her mind and skipped over the typical questions about her role in the film. The weight of the question hit her like a ton of bricks.

Agatha’s mind raced. She had never publicly discussed marriage or children, and certainly not in relation to Rio. Sure, she and Rio had spoken about their future, but nothing had been decided. Agatha had always been careful to keep things private, knowing how the public could dissect and twist their every word. But now, with the cameras rolling and the interviewer looking at her expectantly, Agatha could feel the pressure building.

She cleared her throat, trying to regain her composure. "Well, uh... I mean, Rio and I, we—" She stopped herself, her words trailing off as she realized just how flustered she sounded. It was unusual for Agatha to be caught off guard like this. She was used to being in control of interviews, but this felt personal, and a little too real.

The interviewer noticed the shift in Agatha’s demeanor and smiled knowingly. "It’s a big question, I know. But people are curious. You’ve been together for over six months now and it’s clear how much you care for each other. So, what does the future look like for you two?"

Agatha paused, taking a deep breath, her fingers gripping the edge of the armrest of the chair. She didn’t want to misstep or say anything that might sound like a promise she wasn’t ready to make. But she also didn’t want to dismiss Rio, to brush aside the possibility of a future together.

"I... I think I can say that I’ve never been as happy as I am with Rio," she said, her voice slightly shaking as she spoke. "We’ve had a lot of time to talk about our future, but it’s... it’s something we’re still figuring out together." She gave a nervous laugh, trying to ease the tension in the room. "We’re both kind of... taking it one step at a time."

The interviewer nodded, still smiling, but Agatha could see the subtle shift in her expression. The room was heavy with expectation. Agatha wanted to say more, but she couldn’t shake the feeling that she had just made things more complicated than they needed to be.

"Taking it one step at a time," the interviewer repeated, her tone now more inquisitive than sympathetic. "So, no wedding bells or baby plans on the horizon just yet?"

Agatha’s eyes widened, and for a moment, she panicked. "No! No wedding bells, no... no plans for that," she stammered, fumbling for the right words. "I... I love Rio, and we’re happy right now, but we’re not rushing into anything. We’re just enjoying being together, you know?"

The interviewer gave her a nod of understanding, though Agatha could sense the slight awkwardness hanging in the air. She could feel her cheeks flush, the embarrassment of her uncharacteristic slip-up weighing on her. She wasn’t used to stumbling over her words, especially when it came to her personal life. Agatha was usually so careful, so calculated in everything she did.

The interviewer smiled, clearly sensing Agatha’s discomfort. "That’s completely understandable, Agatha. It’s so important to let things unfold naturally. But I have to say, you two make such a great couple, and it’s obvious you bring out the best in each other."

Agatha nodded, relieved that the conversation had taken a less awkward turn. "Thank you," she said, her voice steadier now. "Rio and I... we’re just really happy, and that’s all that matters."

As the interview continued, Agatha’s thoughts raced. She had tried to be careful, to keep things low-key, but the pressure was starting to get to her. She didn’t want to rush anything with Rio, but she also didn’t want to hide the fact that she was in love with her. Her feelings for Rio were strong, undeniable, but the idea of a future with her—of public expectations and the reality of a relationship being dissected by the world—it was all so overwhelming.

After the interview ended, Agatha retreated to her dressing room, still feeling flustered. She pulled out her phone, immediately scrolling through her messages until she found Rio’s name. Her fingers hovered over the screen for a moment, and she sighed.

She couldn’t keep running from the truth. Rio deserved to know what she was thinking, what she was feeling.

Agatha opened a new message to Rio and typed, her heart racing as she did.

Agatha: Hey my love, I hope the interview went well. Just wanted to tell you something... I know we’ve talked about taking things slow, but I have to admit, I’m thinking more and more about the future. I love you, and I don’t know what that looks like yet, but I want to explore it with you. Just wanted to be honest with you

She hit send before she could second-guess herself.

A few minutes later, Agatha’s phone buzzed. It was a message from Rio.

Rio: I love you too, Agatha. And whatever the future holds, I’m happy we’re in this together. Take your time, we’ve got all the time in the world

Agatha smiled, relief washing over her. Rio understood her, more than anyone else ever had.

Agatha knew they were far from having all the answers, but for the first time, she wasn’t scared of the unknown. She was ready to face whatever came next, as long as Rio was by her side.

Chapter 31

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

The next few months passed in a blur of love, excitement, and a feeling of anticipation that hung in the air like the sweetest of promises. Rio had officially moved in a few weeks after Agathas return from Japan and life had settled into a routine.

After many deep conversations about the future, they decided to start trying for a baby—something they had both longed for, though neither expected the process to be as emotional and overwhelming as it was. After all, it was one thing to talk about building a family, but it was another to take the first steps toward it.

They’d spent late nights together, talking about how they imagined their future would unfold. The conversations always turned to their dreams of children, what kind of parents they would be, the values they wanted to instill, and how they would handle the chaos that inevitably came with adding a little one to their family. But beneath all of that, there was an underlying excitement, a feeling of knowing that they were taking a giant leap toward something extraordinary.

As for Agatha, she was the one who would be carrying their child. It wasn’t a decision they’d made lightly—there had been countless conversations, moments of uncertainty, and late-night talks about what family meant to them. In the end, this path felt right.

They had chosen to pursue IVF, using DNA derived from Rio’s bone marrow to fertilize Agatha’s eggs. It meant that the baby would truly be theirs—both of them—and that made the journey even more profound.

Rio felt a deep sense of awe and gratitude. Agatha was offering her body, her strength, to bring their child into the world. And Rio would be right there with her through it all. They weren’t rushing. There was no pressure. They began the process, clinical, but no less sacred. Each appointment, each injection, each hopeful scan became part of something bigger than themselves.

One night, after a long week of work for both of them, Agatha sat in their living room, gazing out at the sunset. The warmth of Rio’s hand in hers was grounding, comforting. She was aware of every little detail of the moment, the way Rio’s fingers intertwined with hers, how her breath felt slow and steady.

“You okay?” Rio asked softly, noticing the thoughtful look on Agatha’s face.

Agatha smiled, leaning back into the couch, her head resting on Rio’s shoulder. “I’m just thinking about everything. About the future. I’m excited, but I also can’t believe we’re really doing this. We’re trying for a baby.” She chuckled lightly, trying to brush off some of the nerves that were bubbling up.

Rio smiled and squeezed Agatha’s hand. “I’ve never been more sure of anything in my life, Agatha. I’m ready for this. I’m ready for us. And I think we’ll make amazing parents.”

Agatha could feel the warmth in Rio’s words, the truth behind them. She had no doubt they would make great parents, but that didn’t mean the road ahead was going to be easy. It was full of unknowns, and they both knew that. Yet, Agatha couldn’t deny that the thought of creating a life with Rio—the person who made her feel more alive than she ever had before—was the most exciting thing she could imagine.

“We’re going to be okay, right?” Agatha asked, her voice quiet, almost hesitant.

“Of course,” Rio answered immediately, wrapping her arms around Agatha’s shoulders, pulling her in closer. “We’ve already built something so strong together. We’ll be okay, Agatha. You and me, we’ve got this.”

A sense of calm washed over Agatha, and she closed her eyes, leaning into the warmth of Rio’s embrace. As much as she had doubts, Rio always had a way of making everything feel possible.

The weeks that followed were full of subtle changes. Agatha started to pay more attention to her body, and Rio was always there to support her—whether it was running errands or simply being by her side when the anxiety about the unknown crept in.

One afternoon, after Agatha had just finished a work call, she collapsed on the couch, her hand resting gently over her stomach. She was on day 30 of her cycle, and while she had tried to stay calm, the anticipation was beginning to eat away at her. Rio was at the counter, preparing a snack, when Agatha finally spoke.

“You know, if this doesn’t work right away, I won’t be mad. But I really want it to happen. I’m so ready, Rio,” she admitted, her voice soft but filled with sincerity.

Rio turned to her, walking over and kneeling down in front of her. “I know you are. And so am I. But remember, we’re in this together. No matter how long it takes. It’s about us, not just about the baby. We’ll get there.”

Agatha’s heart swelled with affection for Rio. She was so grounded, so calm, and it was just one of the many things Agatha loved about her. They shared a soft kiss, just a gentle press of lips that spoke volumes in its simplicity.

A few weeks later, Agatha was sitting at the kitchen table with a cup of coffee in her hand when Rio walked in, her face glowing with excitement. “Agatha... I think you should take a test today,” Rio said with a wink, handing her a small box from the pharmacy.

Agatha looked at her with raised eyebrows, a smile tugging at her lips. “Are you trying to get my hopes up?”

“I’m just saying... it might be time,” Rio said playfully. “I love you no matter what. But I think this is it.”

With a deep breath, Agatha stood up, accepting the box from Rio. “I’ll be right back,” she said softly, her pulse quickening.

As Agatha stepped into the bathroom, her mind raced. She tried to remain calm, but this moment felt so significant, so life-changing. She sat there in silence, waiting, her hands trembling slightly as she read the test result. The world seemed to hold its breath, waiting for the moment when she could walk out of the bathroom and show Rio the news.

When Agatha stepped back into the living room, Rio was pacing. She looked up, her eyes wide with anticipation.

“I can’t believe this,” Agatha whispered, her voice thick with emotion as she held out the test.

Rio looked down at it, her eyes filling with tears when she saw the result.

“Agatha...” Rio whispered, taking a step forward, her voice shaky. “Is this real?”

Agatha smiled, nodding, her hand placed gently over her heart. “It’s real, Rio. We’re going to be parents.”

Tears filled Rio’s eyes as she wrapped her arms around Agatha, pulling her into a tight embrace. “I’m so happy. I love you, Agatha. I love you so much.”

“I love you too,” Agatha whispered. And in that moment, surrounded by love and anticipation, they knew their world was about to change in the most beautiful way possible.

The decision to keep the pregnancy a secret from the public was not an easy one for Agatha and Rio, but it felt like the right choice. Their lives were always in the spotlight, but this was something that was just for them—something deeply personal that they wanted to protect for as long as possible.

Agatha’s work was demanding, with her film commitments still taking priority, but she made a point to be home with Rio in the evenings. They shared quiet dinners with Remi and Senor Scratchy and built a cocoon of privacy comfort in their home.

It was a Sunday morning when Agatha finally decided to tell Bucky and her mother.

She had been keeping it a secret for weeks, and while she was excited to share the news, she was also nervous about how they would react.

Lilia was over for Sunday brunch, and Bucky was there too, lounging on the couch with a beer in his hand, looking like he had just rolled out of bed. Rio was busy in the kitchen, arranging a plate of pancakes, but she kept glancing over at Agatha, who was visibly nervous.

“So,” Agatha began, sitting at the kitchen table, her hands fidgeting slightly. “I have something I need to tell you both. It’s... important.”

Lilia looked up from her coffee mug, her eyebrows raised in interest. “What is it, sweetheart? You look like you’re about to confess you’ve decided to run away and join the circus.”

Agatha laughed softly, shaking her head. “Mom!. Actually... I’m pregnant,” she said, her voice suddenly full of emotion.

Bucky, who had been scrolling through his phone, looked up with wide eyes. His jaw dropped, and he immediately shot up from the couch, crossing the room in two large strides. “Wait. What?” he asked, eyes flicking between Agatha and Rio, who had just stepped into the room.

“Wait, what?” Rio echoed, her face flushed in surprise. She hadn’t expected Agatha to say it quite like that—out of the blue and with such a casual nonchalance. But seeing the stunned expressions on everyone’s faces, she realized that Agatha had been holding this in for quite some time.

“You’re pregnant?” Bucky asked, his voice filled with disbelief, before it was quickly replaced with a grin. “Holy shit, Agatha, I didn’t see that one coming.”

Lilia blinked a few times, taking a moment to process what Agatha had said. Then, she put down her coffee mug and stood up, her face lighting up with joy. “Oh, my baby,” she said, rushing over to Agatha and pulling her into a tight hug. “I’m so happy for you. So happy! This is wonderful news!”

Agatha’s nervousness melted away as she wrapped her arms around her mother. She had known that Lilia would be thrilled, but hearing her mother’s joy made it feel even more real.

Bucky’s face softened as he walked over to Agatha, placing a hand on her shoulder. “You’ve got this, you know that, right? You’re going to be an amazing mom. And Rio... well, you’ve already got her.”

Rio, who had been standing quietly by the counter, smiling at the scene before her, felt her heart swell at Bucky’s words. She wasn’t sure when, exactly, she had shifted from being terrified about being a mother to actually looking forward to it. But in that moment, surrounded by people she loved, she realized that she had everything she needed.

Lilia beamed at Rio, reaching out to give her a hug as well. “I’m so glad she has you, Rio. And I’m even more thrilled that you two are starting a family together. Agatha’s been through so much in her life, and you... you’re exactly what she needed.”

Rio hugged her back, feeling the weight of Lilia’s words settle deep inside her. It was a beautiful moment, one that made her feel like this truly was the next step in their journey together.

“We haven’t told anyone else yet,” Agatha said quietly, her eyes flicking toward Rio. She wasn’t sure why she felt the need to add that detail, but it felt important. “We wanted to keep it private for a while. Just... for us, you know?”

Bucky nodded thoughtfully. “That makes sense. This is a huge change for both of you. Take your time. Don’t let the press or anyone else rush you into anything.”

Lilia wrapped her arm around Agatha’s shoulders. “And if they try, I’ll knock some heads together,” she added with a mischievous smile.

Agatha laughed, feeling a huge weight lift from her chest. For the first time in weeks, she was able to breathe easy, knowing that the people she cared about were just as excited for her as she was for herself.

Later that evening, Agatha and Rio sat together on the couch, the soft light of the fireplace flickering in the background. They were still processing everything—the excitement, the nerves, the emotions that came with knowing that in just over six months, their lives would change in the most beautiful way.

Rio leaned her head on Agatha’s shoulder, her hand resting over Agatha’s still-flat stomach. “I’m so glad we’ve got each other. I can’t imagine doing this with anyone else,” she whispered, her voice filled with sincerity.

Agatha turned her head, kissing the top of Rio’s head. “I feel the same way. We’re in this together, always.”

“Do you think we’re ready?” Rio asked, her voice soft and uncertain, but filled with hope.

“I think we’re more than ready,” Agatha replied, squeezing her hand gently. “We’ve got this. Together, we’ve got everything we need.”

Rio called Alice on a quiet Thursday afternoon to say she had some big news to share, Alice could immediately sense something was different.

“What’s going on?” Alice asked, her voice crackling with curiosity. “You sound all serious. It’s not the flowers getting weird again, is it?”

Rio laughed nervously, pacing around the living room. “No, no... nothing like that. It’s just... I’ve got something important to tell you.”

The nerves in Rio’s voice made Alice feel a small pang of concern. She knew Rio well enough to know when she was holding back something big. “Okay, spill. You’ve got me worried now.”

Rio took a deep breath before she finally spoke, her words tumbling out in a rush. “Agatha’s pregnant. We’re having a baby. Well, she’s pregnant, but... you know what I mean. We’re going to have a baby.”

For a moment, there was only silence on the other end of the line. Rio’s heart raced as she waited for Alice’s response. Was she shocked? Happy? Confused? Rio had no idea what to expect, but she hoped that, as always, Alice would be happy for her.

Then Alice burst into laughter.

“Wait, WHAT?” Alice practically yelled, making Rio wince a little. “You’re—she’s—Agatha’s pregnant? Holy shit, Rio, this is huge! I... I can’t believe it!” Her voice was filled with both disbelief and joy. “Wait, are you serious? Is this for real?”

“Yes!” Rio replied, laughing nervously. “It’s real. We’re just... keeping it quiet for now. Just, like, for us.”

Alice was still giggling in the background, clearly processing the news, but she quickly switched gears. “Oh my God. Wait, are you okay? Like... I know you’ve been super quiet lately. I thought something was up with you two. Are you sure you’re ready for this? I mean, it’s huge, Rio.”

Rio paused, her heart rate increasing as she reflected on the whirlwind of emotions that had been running through her since Agatha told her. “I’m not sure I’m ready, but I think I am,” she admitted, her voice softening. “I’ve never felt more sure of something in my life. And it’s with her. Agatha’s... she’s everything to me.”

There was a long pause on the line before Alice responded, and when she did, her tone was filled with warmth. “Well, if you’re sure, then I’m sure. I’m so happy for you, Rio. I can’t believe it’s happening, but I’m so excited for you both.”

“Thank you, Alice,” Rio whispered, the weight of the secret they’d been holding suddenly feeling so much lighter. “You have no idea how much I needed to hear that.”

Alice, still processing, started asking all the questions. “Wait, so, when did she find out? How far along is she? Is it a boy or a girl? Oh my God, this is so... so much.”

Rio chuckled softly, the anxiety in her voice easing with Alice’s support. “She’s twelve weeks along, and we’re not telling anyone yet. We wanted to keep it private for a while. As for the rest of it, I don’t even know yet. I just—” Rio stopped herself, realizing she was rambling. “I just wanted you to know. I needed you to know.”

“Of course you did,” Alice replied, her voice suddenly serious. “I’m always here for you, Rio. Always.”

The two of them spent the next half hour talking about the whirlwind of emotions Rio had been feeling, how excited she was but also how nervous. Alice asked about Agatha, how she was doing, and whether she was ready for the massive change. Rio assured her that Agatha was already over the moon, but still, the pressure of keeping this a secret was weighing on both of them.

“Wait, so you’re really keeping it a secret from everyone? Like, no one knows?” Alice asked, raising an eyebrow.

Rio nodded, even though Alice couldn’t see her. “Her Mom and Bucky know but…Yeah. We want to enjoy this moment ourselves first. But it’s hard. It feels like it’s too big to hide forever.”

“I get that,” Alice replied thoughtfully. “But when you’re ready, you’ll share it. And I’ll be right here, cheering you on.”

With that, Rio felt a sense of relief she hadn’t realized she needed. Alice wasn’t just accepting the news—she was fully supportive of it, just as she had always been. And that felt like a weight off her shoulders.

A week later, Rio found herself with Alice in a coffee shop, the two of them catching up over cups of coffee. Alice was all smiles as she listened to Rio talk about her life with Agatha, how they’d been spending more time together, and how, despite the chaos and excitement, everything felt right.

“So, tell me everything,” Alice said, leaning forward with a grin. “Do I need to start planning your baby shower?”

Rio laughed, shaking her head. “It’s way too early for that. We’re just taking it one step at a time. But, I don’t know... It’s kind of surreal. I never thought I’d be here, like, planning a future with Agatha.”

“Well, it’s real,” Alice said, her tone serious now. “And you’re going to make an amazing mom. I know you will.”

Rio smiled, feeling a warm rush of gratitude. “Thank you. I really needed to hear that.”

Alice reached over and squeezed her hand. “Anytime, bestie. Anytime.”

Chapter End Notes
