Chapter 32

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

Agatha’s morning sickness had been getting worse over the past few days, despite her being in the second trimester. It had started out as a light queasiness that disappeared by midmorning, something she could push through with dry toast and peppermint tea. But now, the nausea clung to her like a second skin. She’d wake up with a dull, throbbing headache and that unmistakable tightness in her stomach. The kind of sick that made her flinch at the smell of her favorite lotion, that turned the thought of breakfast into a cruel joke.

Rio was always the first to notice.

“You barely slept,” she murmured one morning, brushing a damp curl from Agatha’s face as she lay curled on the couch, a blanket tucked up to her chin.

Agatha didn’t argue. Her eyes fluttered open slowly, the light through the curtains making her wince. “I’m fine,” she mumbled, even though she looked anything but with her pale complexion.

Rio crouched beside her, resting a hand on her arm. “You don’t have to pretend with me.”

“I’m not,” Agatha replied, but the words sounded thin.

Rio kissed her forehead and stayed close, her fingers gently combing through Agatha’s hair. She never pushed, never lectured. Just stayed. And Agatha adored her for that.

Later that afternoon, Agatha posted a short, silent video to her Snapchat story—just a quick clip of Rio pouring her tea in the kitchen, sleeves pushed up, hair tied in a messy bun.

 

Caption: My girl. I’m obsessed with her ❤️

She didn’t show the nausea, or the way her hands trembled sometimes, or how she’d had to sit on the bathroom floor for twenty minutes that morning. That part wasn’t for anyone else. No one but their closest family knew.

Still, she documented the good—the little joys. Like Rio snuggled under a blanket with three different types of snacks. Or the playlist she made for lazy Sundays that included everything from acoustic love songs to old R&B jams.

“Do you know how hot you are when you’re snacking and being cute and not even trying?” Agatha teased one night, panning the camera slowly across Rio’s concentrated face as she tried to open a stubborn jar of Nutella. No makeup, just sweatpants and sincerity.

Rio looked up, smirking. “You’re just saying that because I bring you toast at 3 a.m.”

“Okay, maybe that too.”

But behind all the private jokes and late-night videos, things weren’t always easy. Some evenings, the sickness was unbearable.

One night, after Agatha had barely touched her dinner and spent the better part of an hour lying on the bathroom floor, Rio made her a mug of ginger tea with honey and sat beside her on the couch.

“You don’t have to be strong all the time,” she whispered, tucking a fresh blanket around her.

Agatha leaned into her touch. “I just… I don’t want you to worry.”

Rio looked at her, brows drawn together. “Too late for that. I’m already completely gone for you.”

Agatha gave a soft, tired smile. “I know. And I love you for it.”

Rio slid her hand over Agatha’s stomach, fingers feather-light over the faintest curve that only she seemed to notice. “We’re doing this together, remember? You’re not alone.”

“I know,” Agatha said again, her voice quieter this time, like the reassurance was sinking in deeper. “I’m just tired and feel like shit.”

Rio leaned down and pressed a kiss just beneath her ribs. “I know Mi Amor. But we’ve got this.”

That night, they curled into bed like puzzle pieces—Agatha’s back pressed to Rio’s front, Rio’s hand resting over her stomach. She whispered softly like she did every night, a ritual now, a quiet promise only the three of them heard.

“You’re strong, baby. So strong. And I love you so much. Both of you.”

Agatha, eyes half-closed, let out a soft hum of contentment. “You’re such a sap,” she whispered.

Rio grinned against her shoulder. “Only for you.”

The next day, Agatha posted another story—just Rio’s hand clasped around hers on a blanket-covered knee, the morning sun lighting up their living room.

Caption: Peace looks like this

Then, a few minutes later, a clip of Remi chasing a Senor Scratchy through the hallway, Rio’s laugh echoing in the background.

Caption: Chaos also looks like this

No mention of the nausea, or the nights spent half-sleeping in the bathroom, or the faint, constant headache. Just love. Just Rio, Remi and Scratchy. Just the quiet life they were building piece by piece.

Sometimes, when the world outside felt too loud—paparazzi lurking in cars down the street, whispers online that speculated about everything from her wardrobe to her weight—Agatha would slip her phone into her pocket and curl up next to Rio on the couch.

Rio would wrap her up in a blanket, press a kiss to the crown of her head, and murmur, “Let them talk. This—” she’d gesture to the room, the tea, Remi snoring in the corner, “—this is real.”

And it was. It was theirs.

Their life, their love, their little world full of messy rooms and inside jokes and soft, reverent touches. A world where Rio whispered to Agatha’s stomach like it was a only them, where love spilled over in little ways—through forehead kisses, mismatched mugs of tea, the way Rio’s fingers always found Agatha’s without having to look.

Every night, as the world hummed outside their windows and the day settled into silence, Rio would hold her close and whisper:

“I love you. I’m so proud of you. And I can’t wait to meet the piece of us we’re growing.”

And Agatha, resting her head against Rio’s chest, would close her eyes and smile—tired, yes, but never alone.

Chapter 33

At five months pregnant, Agatha’s belly had begun to show in a way that was no longer easy to hide, but she still found ways to keep it under wraps. Her wardrobe had evolved; she was expertly selecting outfits that draped over her stomach in flattering ways, opting for loose, flowy tops, oversized blazers, and dark, high-waisted pants. Despite her growing bump, she was determined to keep the pregnancy a secret from the public for as long as possible. She hadn’t shared the news with only a select few close friends and family members actually being aware.

Agatha had hired a new PR manager, Jen Kale, to help manage the situation and ensure that the media didn't catch wind of the pregnancy. Jen was an expert in keeping things under wraps and managing high-profile celebrities, and Agatha felt confident that she would be able to protect their secret. Jen worked tirelessly behind the scenes, keeping Agatha's public appearances under tight control and ensuring that her social media presence was strategically curated. It wasn’t long before Agatha’s entire public image was being carefully controlled to avoid any leaks.

Jen was a no-nonsense woman in her mid-thirties, tall, with a shaved head and sharp features. She always appeared calm, collected, and prepared for anything. Agatha trusted her completely, and their working relationship was off to a good start.

“Keep a low profile,” Jen would advise, reminding Agatha to stay out of the public eye as much as possible. “We’ll manage the press with calculated posts, but you need to lay low on any big public events for now.”

Agatha took Jen’s advice to heart, limiting her outings to only the most necessary events—private dinners with industry colleagues, a few charity galas where her appearance was a must—but all of it was calculated. Rio was fully on board of keeping the pregnancy under wraps. She didn’t want the media breathing down their necks any more than they already had.

It wasn’t just about the public eye anymore; it was about what felt right for them. They both felt a deep need for privacy during this special time, a time to focus solely on each other, on their relationship, and on the new life they were creating together. They didn’t need the noise of the world interrupting that.

Despite the secrecy, it wasn’t easy. Agatha would sometimes get so tired of hiding the pregnancy and wished she could shout from the rooftops about how excited she was. She wanted to walk down the street with Rio and let people see how much she was growing and changing. But she knew that would have to wait.

Agatha would often spend time alone with Rio at home, where she could freely touch her belly and speak openly about the pregnancy. They’d laugh together about the baby’s unpredictable growth spurts or the foods Agatha suddenly craved—she had become obsessed with pickles and cheese, which Rio thought was the strangest combination but still lovingly brought them to her when Agatha asked.

It was on one of these quiet evenings, when they were alone at home, that Agatha finally decided to tell Rio what she had been holding in for weeks. She had been struggling with the secrecy, and it weighed heavily on her heart.

“I feel like I’m lying to the world, you know?” Agatha said, looking over at Rio as they sat on the couch, the evening light casting a warm glow in the living room. “I love our life together, and I love this baby so much… But it’s like I have to keep this part of me hidden, and it’s not easy.”

Rio looked over at Agatha, her expression filled with understanding. “I know, my love. But I think we’re doing the right thing, for us. We don’t need the world’s approval. It’s just about us, right now.”

Agatha nodded, letting out a sigh of relief. “Yeah… you’re right. I just wish I could shout it from the rooftops and let everyone know how happy I am. I love you, Rio, and I love this little one.”

Rio smiled softly, leaning over to rest her head on Agatha’s shoulder. “One day, we’ll tell them. But for now, I think we’re doing what’s best for us. We’ve got our little bubble of love, and nothing else matters.”

Agatha kissed the top of her head, her hand gently resting on her belly. “I just can’t wait for our family to grow,” she said softly, the love in her voice unmistakable.

Rio wrapped her arm around Agatha’s waist, hugging her close. “Me neither.”

Despite the secrecy, their bond had never been stronger. Every day, they grew closer to each other and to the baby, and though the world would have to wait to find out about their little miracle, Agatha and Rio knew they had something truly special.

A week later, as Agatha was getting ready for a private dinner event with Jen and a few key industry contacts, Rio was by her side, helping her pick out the perfect outfit. Agatha stood in front of the mirror, adjusting the hem of her navy-blue, tailored dress, which cleverly concealed the curve of her belly. Her bump was getting harder to hide, but Agatha was determined to make it work.

“How do I look?” she asked, turning to Rio with a playful smile.

“You look gorgeous as always,” Rio replied, her eyes sparkling with affection as she looked at Agatha, “But I can tell you’re tired. Don’t push yourself too hard.”

Agatha chuckled softly, nodding. “I know, I know. But I’ve got to keep up appearances.”

“I get it,” Rio said, her tone warm and understanding. She reached out, gently resting her hand on Agatha’s stomach, feeling the slightest flutter of the baby’s movements. “But don’t forget to take care of yourself. You’re the most important thing to me. You’re both my world.”

Agatha’s eyes softened, and she placed her hand over Rio’s. “I’m lucky to have you,” she whispered, her voice thick with emotion.

Rio smiled up at her. “We’re both lucky.”

The secret was still being kept, they would continue to hold it close—just the two of them, and the little life growing between them.

The weeks passed by quickly, Agatha and Rio settled into a new rhythm of life, more in love than ever. Rio’s work with her florist business had calmed down for the time being, giving her more time to spend with Agatha. Despite the inevitable pressures of being in the public eye, they found moments of peace and happiness together in the quiet of Agatha’s home.

One evening, after a long, tiring day, Agatha and Rio were curled up on the couch together, watching a movie. Agatha’s head rested on Rio’s chest, as usual, her hand gently placed on her growing belly. Remi and scratchy snuggled together in front of them. The soft rhythm of Agatha’s breath and the quiet sound of the movie playing in the background made the world outside feel so distant.

Rio looked down at Agatha, her mind racing with thoughts she had been carrying for a while now. The thought of spending her life with Agatha felt like the most natural thing in the world. Everything had changed between them, and every day she spent with Agatha only solidified that she never wanted this to end.

Agatha, sensing the quiet tension in the air, lifted her head slightly and looked up at Rio, her eyes searching her face. “What’s on your mind, my love?” Agatha asked, her voice gentle.

Rio paused for a moment, heart racing. “I’ve been thinking a lot,” she began, her voice softer than usual. “About us… about the future.”

Agatha’s eyebrows furrowed slightly, concern creeping into her expression. “What about the future?”

Rio took a deep breath, trying to calm the nervous energy bubbling inside her. “I don’t want to wait anymore. I don’t want to wait for the right moment or for the world to catch up with us. I want to spend the rest of my life with you, Agatha. I want us to be a family. You, me, our baby…”

Agatha’s breath caught in her throat as she listened intently, not sure where this was going but already feeling her heart swelling with affection.

“I don’t think I could love you any more than I do right now, Rio,” Agatha said quietly, her voice thick with emotion. “But what… what are you trying to say?”

Rio swallowed, gathering her courage. “I want you to marry me, Agatha. I want you to be my wife.”

The words hung in the air between them, the weight of them settling in a soft silence. Agatha blinked, her eyes wide with surprise, and for a moment, Rio thought she might have misheard or misinterpreted the situation. But then Agatha’s lips parted into a smile so wide that it reached her eyes, and Rio’s heart skipped a beat.

“Marry you?” Agatha whispered, her voice cracking slightly with emotion. She sat up, her hand gently resting on Rio’s knee. “You really want that? You want to marry me?”

Rio nodded, her eyes never leaving Agatha’s. “More than anything. I don’t want to waste any more time. I want us to be tied together in every possible way we can be. I want to stand by you in everything we do.”

Agatha’s eyes softened, tears threatening to spill as she reached for Rio’s hand, gently holding it in hers. “Rio,” she whispered, her voice full of wonder. “You’re everything to me. You’re everything I’ve ever wanted. I’ve been dreaming about this, about you, about us… and I can’t believe you’re asking me.”

Rio smiled, her heart pounding with a mix of relief and joy. “So, you’ll marry me?” she asked, her voice barely above a whisper, hoping she hadn’t misread the situation.

Agatha chuckled softly, tears glistening in her eyes as she leaned forward, pressing her forehead against Rio’s. “Yes,” she breathed, a smile tugging at the corner of her lips. “Yes, I’ll marry you, Rio. A million times yes.”

Rio’s heart swelled as she leaned in, kissing Agatha softly at first, but it quickly deepened into a passionate kiss. The world around them faded away, and all that mattered in that moment was the connection between them, the love they shared, and the future they were about to build together.

When they pulled apart, Agatha gazed at Rio with a soft, adoring smile. “I love you, Rio,” she whispered, brushing a strand of hair behind Rio’s ear.

Rio’s chest tightened with affection as she cupped Agatha’s face in her hands. “I’ve known since that first date that I was meant to be with you, Agatha. I just want to make this real.”

Agatha smiled, her heart full. “It’s real. We’re real, Rio. We’re a family.”

The two women wrapped their arms around each other, the world outside their home seeming so far away as they held each other close. The love between them was undeniable, and in that quiet, intimate moment, they knew they were exactly where they were meant to be.

Rio’s heart was full as she whispered, “I love you.”

Agatha leaned in, her voice soft and full of promise. “I love you more than you’ll ever know.”

Chapter 34

Chapter Notes

See the end of the chapter for notes

The night had been peaceful. Rio and Agatha had spent it curled up in bed, talking about everything and nothing, enjoying their final few weeks of peace before their baby arrived. They laughed, joked, and whispered about all the little things they were excited about—Agatha’s unexpected cravings for pickles and peanut butter, the baby’s nursery they’d set up together, and how they’d each imagined the day their son would be born.

It was late, nearing 1 AM when Rio, her head nestled against Agatha’s chest, heard a sudden, distinct sound—a popping noise, followed by a trickle of water.

Agatha flinched slightly, her eyes going wide. She sat up slowly, looking down at the bed. “Uh, Rio… my water just broke.”

Rio's breath caught in her throat. For a moment, she couldn't process what Agatha had just said. She blinked several times, her mind struggling to catch up with the sudden rush of reality. She looked down at Agatha’s now-wet pyjama bottoms, the unmistakable signs of her water breaking.

“Oh my God,” Rio gasped, her voice panicked. Her heart began to race, and a cold sweat broke out on her brow. “Agatha, are you okay? Are you—are you sure?”

Agatha took a steadying breath, trying to calm the sudden chaos that had rushed into her. “I’m okay. I think it’s time… but we need to get to the hospital.”

At the mention of the hospital, Rio’s panic skyrocketed. She jumped out of bed, pacing nervously. “Okay. Okay, let’s go. We can’t just—what about the paparazzi? What if they follow us? We need to keep this quiet.”

Agatha’s eyes softened with reassurance. “We’re going to be fine, I promise. I’ve got everything ready. We just need to stay calm.”

But Rio wasn’t calming down. Her thoughts were spiraling, the panic building in her chest. What if the paparazzi got wind of it? What if they were caught on camera when Agatha was in labor? They’d managed to hide that Agatha was expecting, they had worked so hard to keep this part of their lives private.

Agatha grabbed Rio by the shoulders, stopping her frantic pacing. “Hey, hey,” she said gently. “It’s going to be okay. Let’s call Jen.”

Jen was a godsend. She’d helped them navigate the labyrinth of media attention, keeping their personal lives as private as possible. But now, with labor imminent and everything moving so quickly, Agatha knew Jen would need to step in.

Rio nodded, still breathing quickly, and immediately pulled out her phone. “I’ll call her,” Rio said, her voice shaky as she quickly dialed Jen’s number. The phone rang twice before Jen picked up, her groggy voice instantly sharp with attention.

“Jen, it’s Rio,” Rio said quickly, barely able to get the words out. “Agatha’s water broke. We need to go to the hospital, but we can’t let the press get wind of it. They’ll follow us if they know. We need you to help us.”

There was a moment of silence before Jen spoke. “I’m on it, Rio. Don’t worry. I’ll arrange everything. I’ll make sure the hospital is kept private, and I’ll make sure no one is alerted. You and Agatha just get to the car, and I’ll handle it from here.”

“Thank you,” Rio breathed, her voice full of relief. She hung up, her eyes meeting Agatha’s. “Jen’s got it. She’s gonna make sure we’re not followed.”

Agatha gave her a small, reassuring smile, though she was starting to feel the first waves of labor contractions. She could tell Rio was overwhelmed, and it broke her heart a little to see her so panicked.

“We have to get moving,” Agatha said, taking a deep breath. “It’s time.”

Rio helped Agatha get dressed quickly, her hands trembling as she zipped up Agatha’s jacket. She was still panicking, her mind racing with thoughts of how this would unfold in the middle of the night. But she tried to focus, taking steady breaths to calm herself.

“Okay, okay,” Rio muttered to herself, running a hand through her messy hair. “You’ve got this. We’ve got this.”

Agatha, now fully dressed, placed a gentle hand on Rio’s arm. “You’re doing great, my love. You’re going to be a great mom. Let’s just get through this together.”

They made their way to the garage, where Agatha’s G-Wagon was parked. Rio held the door open for Agatha, her hands shaking as she helped Agatha into the passenger seat. Her thoughts were racing as she jumped into the driver’s seat. She checked her rearview mirror nervously, hoping no one would notice them. Agatha had made sure her PR team had a plan, but still—this felt too real, too quick.

“Jen said she’s got eyes on the hospital,” Rio murmured, her voice strained. “No one will follow us, but I can’t help but feel like I’m in some kind of movie right now. This feels… surreal.”

Agatha reached over, touching Rio’s hand gently. “I know. But we’re going to do this, together.”

They drove in silence for a few moments, the weight of the situation sinking in. Rio was still nervous, but Agatha’s calm presence helped ground her. She reached over and squeezed Agatha’s hand, trying to focus on the road ahead.

When they arrived at the hospital, everything was already set up. Jen had worked quickly, making sure that no photographers were in sight and that Agatha’s entrance was as discreet as possible. Rio helped Agatha out of the car, and the two of them walked in, Agatha’s arm wrapped tightly around Rio for support.

Jen was waiting in the hospital lobby, and she gave them a small nod as they entered, signaling that everything had been handled.

“You’re good,” Jen said quietly. “No one is here. You’re safe.”

As they made their way to the private maternity suite, Rio finally let out a breath she didn’t realize she’d been holding. She was exhausted—physically, mentally, emotionally. But now that they were inside and secure, all that mattered was that Agatha was okay. And soon, their son would be too.

Agatha gave her a soft smile, her voice calm but laced with a hint of exhaustion. “I’m ready, Rio. Let’s do this.”

Rio kissed her forehead, her heart swelling with a mixture of love, awe, and nervous excitement. “We’re in this together, Agatha. I’m not going anywhere.”

And as they prepared to bring their child into the world, the world outside felt miles away.

The hours seemed to drag on, and Rio felt the weight of the situation pressing down on her chest with each passing minute. She could barely process what was happening. Agatha was in so much pain, the contractions coming one after another, and the sound of her labored breaths filled the room. The sterile smell of the hospital seemed to disappear as the two of them entered their own world—one of pain, fear, and the unknown.

Agatha gripped Rio’s hand tightly, her knuckles white from the force. Her forehead was slick with sweat, and her face was pale. The nurses and doctors moved quickly and efficiently, but to Rio, it felt like everything was happening in slow motion. Every sound, every movement, was amplified in her ears as she watched Agatha fight to keep her composure.

Lilia was there by her other side, wiping the sweat from Agatha’s forehead with a cool cloth. She spoke to Agatha in soft, calming words, doing everything she could to provide comfort in the chaos of the moment.

"You're doing so well, sweetheart. Just breathe," Lilia murmured, her voice steady even though Rio could see the worry in her eyes. She looked up at Rio for a moment, and there was a silent exchange between them. Lilia's gaze said everything: Stay strong for her.

Rio nodded, swallowing hard. Her hands were shaking, but she held on to Agatha’s tightly, trying to stay calm for both of them. Agatha’s eyes flickered to her in between contractions, the vulnerability in them almost too much to bear.

“I can’t… I don’t know if I can do this, Rio,” Agatha gasped between breaths, her voice strained. The fear in her eyes mirrored Rio’s own.

“Shh, you’re doing amazing,” Rio whispered, leaning down to press a kiss to Agatha’s forehead, her fingers threading through Agatha’s damp hair. “I’m right here. We’re going to do this. We’ve got this.”

But as the labor dragged on, Agatha’s condition began to worsen. Her breathing became more erratic, and she started to lose color. Rio’s stomach churned with dread. She could feel her heart racing in her chest, and her thoughts started to spiral into a dark place. Something was wrong.

“Agatha?” Rio asked, her voice trembling with concern. “Agatha, are you okay?”

But Agatha didn’t respond. Her grip on Rio’s hand weakened, and for a terrifying moment, Rio thought she’d lost her. Her heart lurched in her chest, and panic surged through her veins.

“Agatha! Look at me!” Rio pleaded, her voice rising with fear. She tried to gently shake Agatha, but the woman’s body had gone limp, her face pale and covered in a sheen of sweat.

“Doctor!” Rio shouted. She was hyperventilating now, her breathing shallow, struggling to keep it together for Agatha. She looked to the nurse, whose face had gone grim as she quickly moved to Agatha’s side.

The room exploded into action. Rio felt like she was drowning in the chaos, unable to do anything except watch. Nurses were moving around the bed, checking Agatha’s vitals, and doctors were barking orders, but everything seemed muffled, distant. The walls felt like they were closing in on her.

“Agatha!” Rio cried, her voice breaking. “Please, don’t leave me. I need you.” Tears blurred her vision, and her body felt like it was shaking uncontrollably. She couldn't lose her. Not like this. Not when they’d come so far.

Lilia stepped forward, her hand resting on Rio’s shoulder. Her face was taut with concern, but there was something else—something fierce in her eyes. “She’s strong, Rio. Agatha is strong. Just breathe, darling. We’ll get her through this.”

Rio nodded, doing her best to steady herself. She couldn’t lose it now. She had to be there for Agatha.

The doctors worked quickly, and after a few agonizing minutes, they stabilized Agatha. She was pale, her eyes closed, but she was alive. The fear slowly ebbed away from Rio as she saw the faint rise and fall of Agatha’s chest. Her pulse was steady once again.

One of the nurses looked at Rio, her face sympathetic but serious. “She’s lost quite a bit of blood,” the nurse said softly. “We need to monitor her closely, but right now, we need to focus on getting the baby out safely.”

Rio nodded mutely, tears still falling, her eyes never leaving Agatha’s face. She couldn’t believe how close she had come to losing her. Her hands shook as she held Agatha’s again, her voice barely a whisper as she leaned down to speak into Agatha’s ear.

“I love you,” Rio said, her heart aching. “I’m right here. You don’t have to do this alone. Please, Agatha, I need you to be strong. For us.”

Agatha’s eyes fluttered open briefly, her lips parting as if to say something. A weak, strained smile appeared on her face. “I love you too… so much…” she whispered, the words barely escaping her lips before her eyes closed again.

Lilia, who had been silently observing the scene with a mix of concern and determination, wiped away her own tears before speaking gently to Rio. “She’s a fighter. Our girl is going to be just fine.”

Rio looked up at Lilia, swallowing hard. “I can’t… I don’t know what I’d do without her. I can’t lose her.”

“You won’t,” Lilia said firmly, her voice soft but filled with strength. “You have each other, and that’s all that matters. She’ll be okay.”

The minutes dragged on, but gradually, the tension in the room began to dissipate. The nurses and doctors were still working tirelessly, but there was a sense of hope. Agatha was going to make it through this.

Finally, Agatha’s voice cut through the noise of the hospital room. “Rio…” Her voice was weak, but it was there.

“I’m here, baby,” Rio whispered, her voice breaking. “I’m here, Agatha. I’ll never leave you.”

Agatha’s fingers slowly curled around Rio’s hand again, her touch shaky but reassuring. “We’re going to be okay,” Agatha whispered. “We’re going to be parents… together.”

And in that moment, Rio knew that no matter how hard this journey was, she would never face it alone. With Agatha by her side, she could get through anything.

Chapter 35

Chapter Notes

The labor stretched on, longer than either of them had expected, but Rio could feel the faint sense of relief creeping in. Agatha’s breathing had finally stabilized, and she was able to focus once more on the final stages of giving birth. It wasn’t over, but the worst of it was behind them. Agatha squeezed Rio’s hand tighter as the pain intensified once again, and Rio leaned closer, her lips close to Agatha’s ear.

“You’re so strong, Agatha. You’re doing amazing,” Rio whispered, her voice trembling with a mix of admiration and love. “I’m so proud of you.”

Agatha’s eyes fluttered open, and she managed a small, weak smile through the exhaustion. Her skin was still pale, but there was a glimmer of determination in her eyes. She was exhausted, but she wasn’t giving up.

The room was filled with the sounds of the doctors and nurses as they worked to bring their son into the world. Rio stood by Agatha’s side, her heart racing, never leaving her. She rubbed Agatha’s hand, whispering encouraging words, even as her own body trembled with nervous energy.

“Just a little more, Agatha. You’re doing so well,” one of the doctors encouraged, glancing up at her with a calm, reassuring smile.

And then, after what felt like an eternity, Agatha gave one final, forceful push. The room was filled with a collective exhale of relief as the baby was finally born. Rio’s breath caught in her throat as she watched the nurses gently take the tiny, wriggling bundle into their hands, and in that moment, she could hardly believe it.

Their son.

He let out a loud, indignant cry as the nurses cleaned him off, and Rio’s chest tightened with emotion at the sound. She was overwhelmed—by the sheer beauty of the moment, by how much her heart had expanded in a single instant. She was a mother now, in the most profound way, and their family was finally complete.

Agatha, though still weak from the labor, managed to turn her head toward Rio, her voice strained but full of love and awe. “Rio… he’s here. Our son.”

Rio blinked away tears as she looked at Agatha, her heart swelling with pride and love for the woman beside her. “We did it. We really did it,” she whispered, her voice catching in her throat.

The baby was quickly wrapped in a soft, light blanket, and one of the nurses gently brought him over to Agatha’s chest, where she could finally hold him. Agatha’s hands trembled as she cradled their son for the first time, her eyes brimming with tears as she gazed down at him.

“I can’t believe it,” Agatha said softly, her voice trembling. “He’s perfect.”

Rio watched her, completely captivated by the scene before her. Agatha, who had been so strong and determined throughout the labor, was now completely undone in the best possible way. Her tears fell freely, mixing with her smile as she looked at their baby.

“He is perfect,” Rio agreed, her voice barely more than a whisper as she gazed at their son for the first time. “I love you so much, Agatha.”

Agatha’s eyes found Rio’s, and there was something so raw and pure in her gaze, something that spoke volumes about everything they’d been through to get here. Agatha pulled Rio closer, one arm still wrapped around their son, as if holding on to both of them at once. “I love you, too. I can’t wait for you to hold him.”

The doctor spoke again, and it took Rio a moment to realize that it was time for the next step.

“Okay, Rio,” the doctor said gently, “If you’re ready, it’s time to cut the cord.”

Rio’s breath caught in her throat, but there was no hesitation in her movements. She nodded, swallowing hard as she stepped forward. Agatha’s hand was still gripping hers, tight and reassuring.

With a sharp, but gentle snip, Rio cut the cord, her heart swelling with emotion as she realized just how monumental this moment was. Their son, now a part of their family forever. Rio had never felt such a sense of connection, of purpose.

The doctor handed their son back to the nurses, who began to weigh him and measure him, making sure he was healthy. Rio, though still overwhelmed by the events of the past few hours, couldn’t take her eyes off him. He was tiny—so small, yet so perfect.

As the nurses finished with the baby, they handed him back to Agatha, and she carefully placed him into Rio’s arms. It felt surreal to finally hold their child. Rio looked down at the little bundle in her arms, the tiny hands and feet, the soft, delicate face. She leaned down to kiss his forehead gently, her heart expanding with love for the little person she and Agatha had created together.

“Hi, little one,” Rio whispered, her voice full of awe and emotion. “I’m your mami, and I love you so much.”

Agatha reached over, resting her hand gently on Rio’s shoulder. “We did it,” she whispered, her voice full of wonder and tenderness. “We’re parents now.”

Rio nodded, her voice thick with emotion. “We’re a family.” She looked up at Agatha, tears still in her eyes. “You’re the best thing that’s ever happened to me, Agatha. I’ll never take that for granted.”

Agatha smiled, her eyes shining with tears as well. “And you, Rio. You’re the best thing that’s ever happened to me, too.”

In that moment, surrounded by their son, their hearts full of love and hope for the future, they both knew that no matter what challenges lay ahead, they would face them together. They had created something beautiful—something that was theirs—and they would cherish it with everything they had.

The following days after the birth were a blur of joy and emotion. The world had shifted in the most profound way, and Agatha and Rio couldn’t wait to share the news with their closest family and friends. They decided to announce their son's birth through a series of Snapchat stories.

She snapped a picture of their son’s tiny hand wrapped around her finger, a delicate contrast against her own long, manicured fingers. The image was simple, but it said everything.

"Meet our son," Agatha wrote over the picture, her words a soft declaration of the love they’d created. "We’re so in love."

Rio, standing beside Agatha, couldn’t stop staring at their son. She kissed his forehead gently before pulling out her own phone, capturing a moment of Agatha holding him and looking down at him with all the tenderness in the world.

"Can’t believe I’m a mom," Rio added, her voice trembling with happiness. "This little guy is already everything to me."

She tagged Agatha’s private friends list and included close family members, making sure that the people who mattered most could see the birth announcement. The story was a quiet, intimate affair, but it spoke volumes. They weren’t interested in the flash of public attention—they just wanted to share their joy with the people they loved.

Later that day, Lilia came over to the house, her arms open wide as she approached Rio and Agatha in the living room. She had a radiant smile on her face, already looking like she’d come prepared to spoil her new grandson.

“He’s perfect. Absolutely perfect.”

Agatha, holding their baby in her arms, smiled as Lilia gently took the little one from her. "You’re already spoiling him, aren’t you, Mom?"

Lilia gave a playful shrug. "Spoiling? Oh, darling, I’m just giving him the love he deserves!" She kissed the baby’s head, her eyes filled with a tender warmth. "I’m going to spoil him with love, and if I happen to sneak him a cookie or two before he’s old enough to know better, well… that’s between me and him."

Agatha chuckled, her heart swelling with affection as she watched her mother fawn over their son. "I can already tell he’s going to have you wrapped around his little finger."

Lilia shot Agatha a wink. "Of course, dear. But he’s going to be so loved, and that’s what matters."

The day continued with laughter and warmth, and soon, Bucky and Alice arrived, both eager to meet the newest member of their family. The moment Alice stepped inside, she went straight to Rio, pulling her into a tight hug. “I’m so happy for you,” Alice whispered, her voice thick with emotion. “You’re going to be the most amazing mom. I know it.”

Bucky, ever the jokester, wiped away a fake tear and gave Rio a quick but heartfelt hug. “You’re doing a great job, Rio. Agatha may have been carrying the little guy, but you’ve been by her side the whole time. You’re a team. I can already tell you’re gonna be the coolest mom.”

Rio laughed, wiping away her own tears as she held the baby in her arms. “You both are too sweet,” she said, her voice thick with emotion. “I’m just… in awe of everything. He’s perfect.”

Bucky nodded, his eyes softening. “He really is. And you two,” he gestured between Agatha and Rio, “You’re perfect together. Look at you. You’re parents now.”

Agatha beamed, looking over at Rio with so much love that it was almost palpable. “I couldn’t have asked for a better partner in this. I love you, Rio.”

Rio leaned in, brushing her lips against Agatha’s in a soft kiss. “I love you too. So much.”

The room was quiet for a moment as everyone admired the baby. Then, Alice broke the silence with a soft, emotional chuckle. “I’m not crying, you are,” she said, wiping at her eyes. “He’s just so beautiful. It’s all so perfect.”

Lilia, sitting on the couch with the baby cradled in her arms, agreed with a contented sigh. “I’m so glad we’re here to witness this. Our family is growing, and it’s so full of love.”

As the afternoon went on, the group spent time together, laughing, sharing stories, and marveling at how much the world had changed in such a short period of time. It was clear that this little boy had already brought an abundance of love and happiness into their lives, and the future looked bright.

Later that night, after everyone had gone home, Rio sat on the couch beside Agatha, their baby sleeping peacefully in the bassinet beside them. Rio rested her head on Agatha’s shoulder, feeling the warmth of their family bond, and the overwhelming sense of love that had settled in their home.

“This is everything,” Rio whispered, her voice barely audible. “I never imagined life could be this full.”

Agatha wrapped her arm around Rio, pulling her closer. “Me neither. But I wouldn’t want to experience it with anyone else.”

They both gazed at their son, the love and admiration in their eyes so palpable it seemed to fill the entire room.

“This is just the beginning,” Agatha said softly, her voice full of certainty. “Our little family is just getting started, and I know it’s going to be amazing.”

Rio smiled, the weight of the moment sinking in. She felt so incredibly lucky, so deeply loved, and her heart swelled as she whispered, “I can’t wait for the rest of our lives.”

Chapter 36

The press had been buzzing with speculation, their headlines increasingly louder and more desperate. ‘Agatha and Rio: Are They Still Together?’ one tabloid headline screamed. ‘Fans Wonder Why Agatha Hasn't Been Seen in Public Recently – Has She and Rio Split?’ another asked.

It was all nonsense, of course. But the press couldn’t seem to get enough of it. They took Agatha’s recent disappearance from the public eye as a signal that something was wrong between her and Rio. They noticed the absence of their usual public outings, the lack of pictures captured over the lat few months.

Some suggested Agatha was hiding away because of a breakup. Others, more dramatically, claimed that she was depressed or maybe even retreating into seclusion because of an undisclosed personal crisis. It was all a little ridiculous—and completely off the mark.

But Agatha and Rio? They were completely in love, stronger than ever, and just enjoying their life together behind closed doors. The reality of their situation was simple: Agatha had given birth to their baby, and they were keeping it private for now. No one—except for their closest friends and family—knew that they had a newborn at home.

One lazy afternoon, Rio sat with Agatha in their living room, both of them scrolling through the latest tabloid rumors with a mixture of amusement and disbelief. Agatha was resting her head on Rio’s shoulder, her hand gently resting on Rios arm.

"Omg, Rio," Agatha chuckled, swiping through a particularly dramatic headline. "Look at this one. 'Has Agatha been hiding because she’s heartbroken?' I don’t think I’ve ever felt more in love in my life."

Rio laughed too, squeezing Agatha’s hand. "I know, right? Who writes this stuff?"

Agatha smiled, pressing a kiss to Rio's cheek. "Well, we are good at keeping secrets. It’s just, this is a secret I’m happy to keep."

"You know," Rio said, glancing down at the article again, "there’s nothing like a good breakup rumor to make us look even more in love. Not that they know, of course."

"Exactly. They think we're falling apart, but we’re just over here, in total bliss with a newborn," Agatha laughed, sitting up a bit. "I can’t even tell you how happy I am right now. We’ve got our baby, we’re together, and we’re just… doing our thing."

Rio smiled softly, nodding. "Yeah. It’s been a rollercoaster, but I wouldn’t change a thing. Besides, I kind of love the idea of the press thinking we’re falling apart when we’re actually over here having the best time. The whole world’s completely missing the mark."

Agatha laughed, leaning back into the couch. "I think they’re just upset they don’t get to be a part of this. But I’m happy it’s just ours. Our little secret."

She reached out, wrapping her arms around Rio’s waist, pulling her closer. "Besides, who cares what they say when I’ve got you, my love?"

Rio’s heart fluttered as she returned Agatha’s embrace. "I’ve got you too. And I think it’s amazing that we get to have this time for ourselves. No one knows what we’re doing, what we’re building together. It’s just us."

"Exactly," Agatha said, pressing her lips to Rio’s forehead. "I’m not hiding from anyone. I just want to enjoy this, you know? Nicky, you, everything. All of it."

Rio nodded. She felt the weight of those words, the love Agatha spoke with. "Yeah," she whispered. "We’re a family now. And we’re stronger than any rumor they can throw at us."

They both laughed again, this time the sound easy and free, as they leaned back together on the couch. The noise from the press faded into the background. They didn’t need to worry about what was being said or speculated. What mattered was what they had—what they were building.

And what they had was more than enough.

They shared a quiet, knowing look, both of them feeling the quiet magic of being together, just the two of them , their pets and their son. The world could speculate all it wanted, but they knew the truth. They were a family, happy, in love, and absolutely nothing was going to change that.

Later that evening, after they had put Nicky to sleep in his crib, Rio and Agatha decided to do something for themselves. Agatha poured them both a glass of wine, and they settled onto the couch once more, casually scrolling through their social media to check in with friends.

Rio couldn’t help but smile when she saw Alice’s Snapchat pop up. It was just Alice being her usual goofy self, pulling faces to the camera.

Caption: I’m so happy for you both. You guys are everything

Rio sent a quick reply, letting Alice know how much they appreciated her support, while Agatha, meanwhile, sent a quick message to Bucky, who was in the middle of a live interview.

Bucky’s response made both of them burst into laughter: You two are unbreakable. I see all these rumors and all I can think is, Yeah, right, they’re so happy.

The love and support from their inner circle were all that mattered. And Rio couldn’t help but feel grateful for how far they had come.

As they snuggled together on the couch, Agatha’s hand gently resting on Rio’s, the room was filled with a comfortable silence. Rio leaned over and kissed her softly, a silent promise to stay strong, to be there for each other through everything. They were untouchable, unbothered by the chaos outside their little bubble.

And as they pulled the blanket over themselves, settling in for the night, Rio whispered quietly into Agatha’s ear.

"Let them speculate. We’ve got everything we need right here."

Agatha smiled, her eyes glinting in the soft light. "I love you."

“I love you more”.

And with that, they drifted off to sleep, knowing they had all they needed.

A month had passed since Nicky’s birth, and Rio still couldn’t get over how quickly Agatha had bounced back. Agatha’s body, once round with pregnancy, was now back to its natural shape, and she looked as radiant as ever. Rio couldn’t help but marvel at how strong and beautiful Agatha was. It seemed like she was glowing even more now that she had their son in her life.

Agatha was sitting on the couch, cradling Nicky in her arms as she breastfed him. The scene was intimate, peaceful, and filled with so much love that it made Rio’s heart swell. The way Agatha looked at their son, the tenderness with which she held him—Rio knew, without a doubt, that they were both absolutely meant to be parents.

Rio was sitting beside them, her hand gently resting on Agatha's leg as she watched the two of them, her emotions swirling. She was in awe of how natural Agatha was as a mother, how perfectly she fit into this role, even though it hadn’t been long. She couldn’t wait for the world to see just how beautiful their family was, but a part of her hesitated. The weight of the public’s scrutiny always loomed over them.

Agatha looked up at Rio and smiled softly, her eyes soft and full of affection. "What’s on your mind?" she asked, her voice a quiet hum of warmth.

Rio hesitated for a moment, her fingers tracing small patterns on Agatha’s knee. "I’ve been thinking," she began slowly, "about when we’ll tell everyone about Nicky. I mean, the press and fans are getting worse with speculations, and I can’t keep the joy of him to myself much longer. He’s just… so perfect, Agatha."

Agatha’s gaze softened even more, and she gently moved Nicky to her other arm, giving him a gentle kiss on the top of his head. "I know," she said, her voice full of thoughtfulness. "I’ve been thinking about that too. It feels strange, you know? Hiding this part of our lives when it’s the most beautiful thing that’s ever happened to me." She looked over at Rio, her expression serious but warm. "But we’ve kept it private for a reason. The world doesn't need to know everything, not yet, at least. We’ve had our own time, just the three of us, and I’m not ready to let go of that just yet."

Rio nodded, understanding where Agatha was coming from. The weight of their public lives was a heavy burden to carry, and Agatha had become fiercely protective of their little family. "I get that," Rio said softly. "But I also think Nicky deserves to be celebrated. We shouldn’t have to hide him forever. He’s part of our world now. He’s a part of us."

Agatha’s eyes twinkled, and she reached out to take Rio’s hand, squeezing it gently. "I’m not saying I want to hide him forever. But I want to do it on our terms, in our time. Maybe we’ll just... ease into it. Let the world get to know him slowly, when we feel ready."

Rio smiled, nodding in agreement. "Yeah, that sounds right. We can still share pieces of our joy without feeling overwhelmed by everything else."

Nicky gave a small, sleepy sound as he nursed, and Agatha laughed softly, brushing a lock of hair from his tiny face. "He’s so precious," she whispered, her voice filled with wonder. "I just want to protect him, keep him safe and happy."

Rio leaned in, pressing a soft kiss to Agatha’s temple. "We’ll protect him together. And when the time comes, we’ll share him with the world, but on our terms. He’s our son, and no one can take that away from us."

Agatha smiled up at her, her expression full of love and gratitude. "I love you so much, Rio. I’m so lucky to have you in my life, and Nicky’s life."

Rio’s heart swelled, and she leaned in to kiss Agatha’s lips, soft and tender. "I love you too, Agatha. And I love Nicky more than I ever thought possible. Our little family... it's everything to me."

They stayed like that for a while, just the three of them, basking in the quiet happiness that only a family could bring. Rio kept glancing at Nicky, watching as Agatha carefully tended to him, and she couldn’t help but smile. Their son was the greatest gift they had ever received, and she was beyond excited for the future they would build together.

After a few moments, Agatha broke the silence again, her voice thoughtful. "We can announce his birth soon. Maybe when we’ve settled a little more. But I’m happy to just enjoy these moments with you. That’s the most important thing to me."

Rio smiled, a sense of peace settling over her. "I’m happy with that too. We’ll do it when it feels right. Just us, at first."

Agatha nodded, her gaze soft and loving as she cradled Nicky close. "Exactly. Just us."

As they sat there, the world outside seemed to fade away, and it was just them—their love, their son, their quiet little family. And for now, that was all they needed.

After weeks of keeping their joy to themselves, Agatha and Rio sat down one evening, both of them feeling the excitement and the weight of what they were about to do. The time had come to share their beautiful son, Nicky, with the world.

It wasn’t something they took lightly. The press had already been speculating about their relationship, about Agatha's time away from public life, and about their quiet, private family life. But now, they had a moment that was theirs—a moment they wanted to share in their own way, on their own terms.

"I think we should do it on Instagram," Agatha said, looking at Rio, her voice filled with a mixture of excitement and calm determination. "It’s the best way to share him with the world, and to do it the way we want. Simple, private, but still... beautiful."

Rio nodded, her heart racing with a mix of nerves and excitement. "Yeah, I agree. No need to make it over the top, just something that feels... real. Something that represents who we are right now—just the three of us, figuring it all out together."

They decided to keep things simple, using one of the most intimate and precious moments they had experienced with Nicky. The photograph was black and white—timeless, tender, and honest. It showed the tiny hands of their newborn son, clutching their fingers, both of them holding onto him, their faces nowhere to be seen. It was a picture of their hands, intertwined with his.

The caption was brief, yet powerful. Agatha typed it out slowly, letting the words sink in:

Welcome to the world, Nicky Harkness Vidal. We’re so in love and settling into life as a family. Thank you for giving us this beautiful gift

With a final deep breath, Agatha hit the Post button on her public instagram.

The post was up, and almost instantly, their 180 million followers on Instagram began reacting. The comments section exploded with joy and well-wishes, while hashtags like #NickyHarknessVidal and #Agathario trended on Twitter within minutes. People couldn’t get enough of the intimate, beautiful photo, and the caption left them in awe.

From the moment the post was shared, the comments flooded in. There were fans from all over the world, offering their congratulations, some of them writing in multiple languages, others sharing their excitement about the couple becoming parents.

@OfficialHarkyfan: Oh my god, I’m crying 😭😭 Nicky is the most beautiful gift. You both are incredible. Congratulations 💖

@MamaBear23: SO happy for you both!! You’re going to be amazing parents. Sending all the love to your little family! 🍼💙

@StarsAndStripes: Such a beautiful moment shared! I respect your privacy, but thank you for letting us see this piece of your life. Welcome to the world, Nicky!! 🌟💫

It wasn’t just the fans who were commenting. Major news outlets and entertainment journalists began posting about it almost immediately. The narrative that had been building—questions about Agatha’s private life, about her time away from the public eye—was suddenly flipped into something heartwarming, joyful, and relatable.

@PopCultureDaily: BREAKING: Agatha Harkness and Rio introduce their son, Nicky, to the world in a touching Instagram post. Congratulations to the happy couple! 💖 #NickyHarknessVidal #FamilyGoals

The tabloids, who had previously speculated on everything from Agatha's mental health to a breakup with Rio, now had an entirely new narrative to run with. The focus shifted. People started to forget about the rumors of a split, and instead, they were enveloped in the joy and love that Agatha and Rio were sharing with their son.

Of course, the press wasn’t entirely without criticism. A few articles popped up questioning how the couple managed to keep their pregnancy and then birth of the baby out of the public eye for so long, but the overall response was overwhelmingly positive. Fans and followers celebrated Agatha’s transparency in the most meaningful way she knew how—through the simplicity of their family photo.

Later that night, Agatha and Rio sat together in the living room, Nicky nestled in his bassinet, sleeping soundly. They had read through the comments and the posts, grinning at the outpouring of love they were receiving. Agatha was leaned back, her legs stretched out on the couch, Rio curled up beside her. It was a quiet, peaceful moment, just the two of them processing everything.

"I can’t believe we did it," Rio said softly, still smiling at the phone screen, scrolling through the endless congratulations. "I’m so happy... I’m just so happy."

Agatha’s hand found Rio’s, and she squeezed it gently, her eyes full of love. "I know. Me too. It feels right, sharing this with everyone. But also... I still want to keep him protected, just between us sometimes. I don’t think I’ll ever get used to the spotlight being on him. He’s our little miracle."

Rio nodded. "I feel the same. He’s our world. I just want to protect him, give him everything."

Agatha smiled and kissed the top of Rio’s head. "We will. And we’ll take it one day at a time. I love that we’re doing this together, on our terms."

Rio smiled back up at her, her heart full. "Yeah, me too. We’re a family."

Meanwhile, Bucky and Alice were already reacting to the post. Alice sent Rio a text that was filled with emojis and exclamation points.

Alice: OH MY GOD, YOU DID IT!! 😭😭😭 He’s PERFECT! I can’t believe the world knows you two are parents now. He’s already got the whole world in his hands. I’m so happy for you both!!! 💙💙💙

Bucky, on the other hand, had taken a more relaxed approach. He sent Rio a Snap video of him lying on his couch, looking ridiculously comfortable in his pajamas.

Bucky’s Snap: Yo, you did it. You both did it. Nicky’s a lucky kid. He’s got two amazing parents. Let’s get a drink soon, yeah? I’m pumped for you two."

Agatha was in stitches watching the Snap, knowing that Bucky was going to continue to spoil Nicky.

As the comments continued to flood in, Rio and Agatha sat there in quiet contentment, knowing they had made the right decision. Their world had just become a little bit bigger, a little bit brighter, and now it was time for them to enjoy every second of it.

Chapter 37

A few days after sharing their son Nicky's first glimpse with the world on Instagram, Agatha was preparing for her first interview since giving birth. It was scheduled with a popular morning talk show, and she was set to talk about her new film, navigating motherhood, and how life had changed after Nicky’s birth.

Although Agatha had hesitated about stepping back into the public eye so soon, the support from Rio and their shared commitment to protecting Nicky had given her the confidence to do so. They'd made a pact that Nicky's face would remain private for now, and they’d keep their family life as peaceful and out of the spotlight as possible.

On the morning of the interview, Agatha was in her trailer, a soft light filling the room as her makeup artist applied the finishing touches. She wore a loose, flowing dress that didn’t cling to her postpartum body. The last month had been a whirlwind—juggling the exhaustion of motherhood with the love she had for their son, and her drive to return to work. It was the kind of chaos she was still getting used to, but Agatha wouldn't have changed it for anything.

Nicky was beside her, swaddled in a blanket, peacefully asleep in a stroller. Rio sat next to Agatha, offering her a soft smile as she carefully cradled their son’s little hand. Rio, ever the attentive partner, checked on Nicky every few minutes, ensuring he was comfortable.

"Are you ready for this?" Rio asked quietly, her voice laced with a bit of nerves but filled with warmth.

Agatha laughed softly, running her fingers through her hair. "As ready as I’ll ever be," she said, giving Rio a reassuring smile. "Just... trying to remember that Nicky is my priority. No one’s getting pictures of him, until we’re ready."

Rio nodded and leaned over to kiss Agatha’s forehead. “I’m here for you. No matter what, we’ve got this.”

With a final glance at Nicky, who was now awake and blinking up at Agatha with sleepy eyes, she leaned down and whispered, "I love you, my love."

The interview was held in a relaxed studio lounge, with cozy couches and large windows letting in natural light. Agatha had requested a quiet corner to breastfeed Nicky during breaks in the discussion. She was determined to keep him close, and the team had graciously agreed.

The host, a seasoned TV personality, greeted Agatha with a warm smile. “Agatha, it’s so wonderful to see you back, and congratulations on your beautiful baby, Nicky. He’s adorable.”

Agatha beamed. “Thank you so much. These past few weeks have been life-changing. It’s been a little overwhelming, but I wouldn’t trade it for the world.”

As the interview progressed, Agatha alternated between answering the host’s questions and looking lovingly at Nicky in the breaks, who was nestled in her arms, feeding quietly. She spoke about the joy of motherhood, the challenges, and the surreal experience of being a new parent.

"How has motherhood been so far?" the host asked. "You’ve been so private about your personal life—how are you adjusting to everything with Nicky?"

Agatha's face softened as she gazed past the camera at their son. "It’s incredible," she said. "It's a lot, but it's also... so fulfilling. Rio’s been an amazing partner and mother. She’s incredible with Nicky. We’re adjusting together, and it's been a beautiful ride so far."

Rio, seated with Nicky, smiled, her hand resting protectively on the stroller. "She’s handling everything so gracefully. I’m the one who’s learning every day." She called towards the camera.

The host laughed and looked at Rio. "I’m sure! So, will we get to see more of Nicky in the future? I know you’ve kept him out of the public eye for now."

Agatha nodded, her eyes filled with love as she looked at Rio. "Right now, we’re just trying to keep him as private as possible, especially while he's so little. We want him to have a normal, peaceful childhood. Maybe one day, when he’s older, we’ll share more, but for now, he’s ours to protect."

The host smiled understandingly. "That makes sense. I think all your fans understand that. You’re already giving them a glimpse into your world by sharing with us today."

As the interview wrapped up, Agatha felt a sense of relief. The weight of the public’s curiosity had felt heavy at times, but she knew she was doing the right thing by keeping Nicky's life as private as possible.

After the cameras stopped rolling, Agatha let out a deep breath. "I’m glad that’s over," she admitted, leaning back on the chair.

Rio, ever the support, squeezed her hand. "You did amazing as always."

Agatha smiled, looking at Nicky, who had fallen asleep in her arms after his feeding session. "He’s just the best."

As they gathered their things, Agatha looked at Rio, feeling a rush of gratitude. "You’re amazing, Rio. You’ve been incredible through all of this."

Rio chuckled softly. "I’m just following your lead, sweetheart. But I have to admit, seeing you with Nicky… it’s the most beautiful thing I’ve ever seen."

Agatha leaned over and kissed her gently. "I’m so glad we’re doing this together. I couldn’t imagine doing it with anyone else."

Later that evening, after the interview aired, Agatha and Rio shared some quiet time at home. They scrolled through the countless messages of support from fans, friends, and family. It was overwhelming but comforting to know that they had the backing of so many people.

“I think we did good,” Rio said, leaning back on the couch. “We showed them that we’re happy, that we’re doing this together. That’s all we really need to focus on."

Agatha nodded, feeling content. "We’re doing it our way. And I wouldn’t want it any other way."

As they spent the night cuddling together, with Nicky asleep in his crib nearby, Agatha knew that no matter what the world thought, she had everything she needed right there. A beautiful partner in Rio, and the love of their precious son, Nicky. Together, they had a family—one that was stronger than anything the world could throw at them.

Chapter Notes

It was a sunny morning in early spring when Agatha and Rio’s wedding day finally arrived. The excitement had been building for months, though they had kept things intimate, not wanting any media frenzy or paparazzi lurking at every corner. It would be a quiet, private affair—a celebration of their love, surrounded by the people who truly mattered to them.

Agatha had insisted on no grand spectacle, just a simple ceremony. Rio, however, had her own ideas of making the day as beautiful as possible, without the public eye taking center stage. They’d chosen a secluded venue near the beach, tucked away in a lush, green corner of the world, where only their son and closest family and friends would be present. The air was crisp, the sound of waves gently crashing on the shore, and the scent of fresh flowers filled the air, each bloom hand selected and prepared by Rio herself.

The morning was calm, but inside the venue, the excitement was palpable. Rio stood in front of the mirror in her dressing room, adjusting her dress. It was simple yet elegant, with lace detailing, hugging her curves in all the right ways, and a modest train that pooled at her feet. Her hair was styled in loose waves, cascading down her back. She took a deep breath, feeling a mixture of excitement and nervousness. She had always dreamed of this day, but now that it was finally here, the reality of marrying Agatha made her heart flutter.

She glanced at her phone, seeing a message from Agatha.

Agatha: Are you ready for this? I can't wait to see you walking down that aisle

Rio smiled and quickly typed back.

Rio: I’m ready if you are. I love you so much

Agatha’s response was swift, as always.

Agatha: I love you more. I’ll see you in a bit, my beautiful fiancée soon to be wife

Rio’s heart skipped a beat. The word wife felt strange but so incredibly perfect.

The ceremony itself was held outside, the soft whirl of wind and sea providing a peaceful soundtrack to the intimate moment. Agatha stood at the front, looking more stunning than Rio had ever seen her. She wore a soft, ivory suit, the jacket tailored perfectly to her form, and the pants flared just slightly at the ankle. Her white shirt underneath was unbuttoned just enough to reveal the delicate necklace that Rio had given her. She was glowing. Agatha's hair, normally messy in the best way, had been neatly styled into a low bun with loose strands framing her face.

As Rio walked down the aisle, she was in awe of how beautiful Agatha looked. She couldn’t help but smile as Agatha’s eyes met hers, and for a moment, it felt like everything stopped. The world faded, and it was just the two of them, eyes locked in a gaze that was filled with love, longing, and a promise of forever.

When Rio finally stood beside Agatha, the look on her face was filled with an emotion that took Agatha’s breath away.

“You’re so beautiful,” Agatha whispered, her voice filled with awe.

Rio grinned, holding back tears. “I should be the one saying that to you.”

The officiant, a close friend of Lilias, started the ceremony as Alice and Bucky stood either side, Nicky held in Lilias arms just slightly behind them.

Rio felt as though she was in a dream. She couldn’t believe she was standing here, about to marry Agatha. Their journey together had been filled with ups and downs, challenges, laughter, and tears—but now, they were here, ready to start this new chapter as wives, as a family.

The vows were short but heartfelt. Agatha spoke first, her voice steady but thick with emotion. “I stand here today not because it’s the next step, but because you are the person I want to spend the rest of my life with. I promise to always cherish you, to love you through the good and bad, and to support you in everything you do. You make me better, and I will spend every day showing you how much I love you.”

Tears glistened in Rio’s eyes as she took Agatha’s hands in hers. “I don’t have the words to fully express how much you mean to me. You’ve made me the happiest I’ve ever been. I love you for exactly who you are—strong, kind, beautiful, and full of passion. I promise to always be by your side, through every challenge and every joy. You are everything to me.”

The officiant smiled, and with a gentle nod, he said, “By the power vested in me, I now pronounce you wife and wife. You may kiss each other.”

Agatha leaned in, and the kiss was soft at first, tender, like the promise of everything yet to come. But as the kiss deepened, it became something else entirely—passionate, raw, filled with all the emotions they had both been holding inside. It was a kiss that spoke of a lifetime of love, of two people who had found their other half.

As they pulled apart, Agatha laughed softly, resting her forehead against Rio’s. “I love you so much.”

“I love you, too,” Rio whispered back, her voice thick with emotion.

After the ceremony, they celebrated with their family and friends. The reception was held at the same venue, a small, intimate gathering with just a few dozen people. There was no need for extravagant decorations or a massive cake—just a few candles, a beautiful table set for dinner, and soft music filling the air.

Lilia, was the first to raise a glass in a toast. “To Agatha and Rio,” she began, her voice slightly wobbly. “You two have always had a special connection, and it fills me with joy to see you both come together in this way not just as mothers but as wives. I couldn’t ask for a better partner for my daughter.”

Tears welled in Agatha’s eyes as she raised her glass, nodding at her mother. She turned to Rio, who smiled brightly, her hand resting on her arm.

“To love,” Agatha said, her voice steady but thick with emotion. “And to our beautiful family, now and always.”

The night went on, filled with laughter, dancing, and stories shared between their closest friends and family. Agatha and Rio couldn’t have been happier, surrounded by the people who had supported them through everything.

As the evening wore on, and the music slowed, Agatha pulled Rio close. “This is it, babe. This is our forever.”

Rio smiled softly, her eyes glistening with tears. “Yeah, it is.”

Everything felt perfectly in place. Their love, their family, and their future—all coming together in one beautiful moment.
